PREFACE
___________________________
This City Code of the City of Shoshone, as supplemented, contains ordinances up
to and including ordinance 573, passed August 6, 2024. Ordinances of the City
adopted after said ordinance supersede the provisions of this City Code to the
extent that they are in conflict or inconsistent therewith. Consult the City
office in order to ascertain whether any particular provision of the Code has
been amended, superseded or repealed.
American Legal Publishing
Cincinnati, Ohio

CHAPTER 1.01
CODE ADOPTION
SECTION:
1.01.010: Adoption
1.01.020: Title; Citation; Reference
1.01.030: Codification Authority
1.01.040: Ordinances Passed Prior To Adoption Of The Code
1.01.050: Reference Applies To All Amendments
1.01.060: Title, Chapter And Section Headings
1.01.070: Reference To Specific Ordinances
1.01.080: Repeal Of Existing Ordinances
1.01.090: Effect Of Code On Past Actions And Obligations
1.01.100: Effective Date
1.01.110: Constitutionality
1.01.010: ADOPTION:
Pursuant to the provisions of sections 50-901 to 50-906 inclusive of the Idaho
Code, there is hereby adopted the Shoshone city code as published by Book
Publishing Company, Seattle, Washington, under the direction of Howard E.
Adkins, Esq. (Ord. 364 § 1, 1982)
1.01.020: TITLE; CITATION; REFERENCE:
This code shall be known as the SHOSHONE CITY CODE and it shall be sufficient
to refer to said code as the "Shoshone city code" in any prosecution for the
violation of any provision thereof or in any proceeding at law or equity. It
shall be sufficient to designate any ordinance adding to, amending, correcting
or repealing all or any part or portion thereof as an addition to, amendment
to, correction or repeal of the "Shoshone city code" and such reference shall
apply to that numbered title, chapter, section or subsection as it appears in
this code. (Ord. 364 § 2, 1982)
1.01.030: CODIFICATION AUTHORITY:
This code consists of all the regulatory and penal ordinances and certain of
the administrative ordinances of the city of Shoshone, Idaho, codified pursuant
to the provisions of sections 50-903 through 50-906 of the Idaho Code. (Ord.
364 § 3, 1982)
1.01.040: ORDINANCES PASSED PRIOR TO ADOPTION OF THE CODE:
The last ordinance included in this code was ordinance 362, passed October 6,
1981. The following ordinance passed subsequent to ordinance 362, but prior to
adoption of this code, is hereby adopted and made a part of this code:
ordinance 363 vacating portions of Beverly Street and designated roadway and/or
alleys. (Ord. 364 § 4, 1982)
1.01.050: REFERENCE APPLIES TO ALL AMENDMENTS:
Whenever a reference is made to this code as the "Shoshone city code" or to any
portion thereof, or to any ordinances of the city of Shoshone, Idaho, the
reference shall apply to all amendments, corrections and additions heretofore,
now or hereafter made. (Ord. 364 § 5, 1982)
1.01.060: TITLE, CHAPTER AND SECTION HEADINGS:
Title, chapter and section headings contained herein shall not be deemed to
govern, limit, modify or in any manner affect the scope, meaning or intent of
the provisions of any title, chapter or section hereof. (Ord. 364 § 6, 1982)
1.01.070: REFERENCE TO SPECIFIC ORDINANCES:
The provisions of this code shall not in any manner affect matters of record
which refer to, or are otherwise connected with ordinances which are therein
specifically designated by number or otherwise and which are included within
the code, but such reference shall be construed to apply to the corresponding
provisions contained within this code. (Ord. 364 § 7, 1982)
1.01.080: REPEAL OF EXISTING ORDINANCES:
So far as the provisions of this code are the same in effect as those of
previously existing ordinances, they shall be construed as continuations
thereof; but subject to the above limitation and the provisions of the next
section, all ordinances and resolutions of the city of Shoshone, Idaho,
heretofore in force (except such as are of a private, local or temporary
nature, including franchises, grants, dedications, vacations of city property,
and specific levies for local assessments), are hereby repealed. (Ord. 364 § 8,
1982)
1.01.090: EFFECT OF CODE ON PAST ACTIONS AND OBLIGATIONS:
Neither the adoption of this code nor the repeal or amendments hereby or any
ordinance or part or portion of any ordinance of the city of Shoshone shall in
any manner affect the prosecution for violations of ordinances, which
violations were committed prior to the effective date hereof, nor be construed
as a waiver of any license, fee, or penalty at said effective date due and
unpaid under such ordinances, nor be construed as affecting any of the
provisions of such ordinances relating to the collection of any such license,
fee or penalty, or the penal provisions applicable to any violation thereof,
nor to affect the validity of any bond or cash deposit in lieu required to be
posted, filed or deposited pursuant to any ordinance and all rights and
obligations thereunder appertaining shall continue in full force and effect.
(Ord. 364 § 9, 1982)
1.01.100: EFFECTIVE DATE:
This code shall become effective on the date the ordinance adopting this code
as the "Shoshone city code" shall become effective. (Ord. 364 § 10, 1982)
1.01.110: CONSTITUTIONALITY:
If any section, subsection, sentence, clause or phrase of this code is for any
reason held to be invalid or unconstitutional, such decision shall not affect
the validity of the remaining portions of this code. The council hereby
declares that it would have passed this code, and each section, subsection,
sentence, clause and phrase thereof, irrespective of the fact that any one or
more sections, subsections, sentences, clauses or phrases had been declared
invalid or unconstitutional, and if for any reason this code should be declared
invalid or unconstitutional, then the original ordinance or ordinances shall be
in full force and effect. (Ord. 364 § 11, 1982)
CHAPTER 1.04
GENERAL PROVISIONS
SECTION:
1.04.010: Definitions
1.04.020: Title Of Office
1.04.030: Interpretation Of Language
1.04.040: Grammatical Interpretation
1.04.050: Acts By Agents
1.04.060: Prohibited Acts Include Causing And Permitting
1.04.070: Computation Of Time
1.04.080: Construction
1.04.090: Repeal Shall Not Revive Any Ordinances
1.04.010: DEFINITIONS:
The following words and phrases, whenever used in the ordinances of the city of
Shoshone, Idaho, shall be construed as defined in this section unless from the
context a different meaning is intended or unless a different meaning is
specifically defined and more particularly directed to the use of such words or
phrases:
CITY AND TOWN: Each mean the city of Shoshone, Idaho, or the area within the
territorial limits of the city of Shoshone, Idaho, and such territory outside
of the city over which the city has jurisdiction or control by virtue of any
constitutional or statutory provision.
COUNCIL: The city council of the city of Shoshone. "All its members" or "all
councilmen" means the total number of councilmen holding office.
COUNTY: The county of Lincoln.
LAW: Denotes applicable federal law, the constitution and statutes of the state
of Idaho, the ordinances of the city of Shoshone, and, when appropriate, any
and all rules and regulations which may be promulgated thereunder.
MAY: Is permissive.
MONTH: A calendar month.
MUST AND SHALL: Are each mandatory.
OATH: Includes an affirmation or declaration in all cases in which, by law, an
affirmation may be substituted for an oath, and in such cases the words "swear"
and "sworn" shall be equivalent to the words "affirm" and "affirmed".
OWNER: Applied to a building or land, includes any part owner, joint owner,
tenant in common, joint tenant, tenant by the entirety, of the whole or a part
of such building or land.
PERSON: Includes a natural person, joint venture, joint stock company,
partnership, association, club, company, corporation, business, trust,
organization, or the manager, lessee, agent, servant, officer or employee of
any of them.
PERSONAL PROPERTY: Includes money, goods, chattels, things in action and
evidences of debt.
PRECEDING AND FOLLOWING: Next before and next after, respectively.
PROPERTY: Includes real and personal property.
REAL PROPERTY: Includes lands, tenements and hereditaments.
SIDEWALK: That portion of a street between the curb line and the adjacent
property line intended for the use of pedestrians.
STATE: The state of Idaho.
STREET: Includes all streets, highways, avenues, lanes, alleys, courts, places,
squares, curbs, or other public ways in this city which have been or may
hereafter be dedicated and open to public use, or such other public property so
designated in any law of this state.
TENANT AND OCCUPANT: Applied to a building or land, include any person who
occupies the whole or a part of such building or land, whether alone or with
others.
WRITTEN: Includes printed, typewritten, mimeographed, multigraphed, or
otherwise reproduced in permanent visible form.
YEAR: A calendar year. (1981 Code)
1.04.020: TITLE OF OFFICE:
Use of the title of any officer, employee, department, board or commission
means that officer, employee, department, board or commission of the city.
(1981 Code)
1.04.030: INTERPRETATION OF LANGUAGE:
All words and phrases shall be construed according to the common and approved
usage of the language, but technical words and phrases and such others as may
have acquired a peculiar and appropriate meaning in the law shall be construed
and understood according to such peculiar and appropriate meaning. (1981 Code)
1.04.040: GRAMMATICAL INTERPRETATION:
The following grammatical rules shall apply in the ordinances of the city
unless it is apparent from the context that a different construction is
intended:
   A.   Gender: Each gender includes the masculine, feminine and neuter
genders.
   B.   Singular And Plural: The singular number includes the plural and the
plural includes the singular.
   C.   Tenses: Words used in the present tense include the past and the future
tenses and vice versa unless manifestly inapplicable. (1981 Code)
1.04.050: ACTS BY AGENTS:
When an act is required by an ordinance, the same being such that it may be
done as well by an agent as by the principal, such requirement shall be
construed to include all such acts performed by an authorized agent. (1981
Code)
1.04.060: PROHIBITED ACTS INCLUDE CAUSING AND PERMITTING:
Whenever in the ordinances of the city of Shoshone, any act or omissions are
made unlawful, it shall include causing, allowing, permitting, aiding,
abetting, suffering, or concealing the fact of such act or omission. (1981
Code)
1.04.070: COMPUTATION OF TIME:
Except when otherwise provided, the time within which an act is required to be
done shall be computed by excluding the first day and including the last day
unless the last day is Sunday or a holiday, in which case it shall also be
excluded. (1981 Code)
1.04.080: CONSTRUCTION:
The provisions of the ordinances of the city and all proceedings under them are
to be construed with a view to effect their objects and to promote justice.
(1981 Code)
1.04.090: REPEAL SHALL NOT REVIVE ANY ORDINANCES:
The repeal of an ordinance shall not repeal the repealing clause of an
ordinance or revive any ordinance which had been repealed thereby. (1981 Code)
CHAPTER 1.08
CITY SEAL
SECTION:
1.08.010: Description
1.08.020: Adopted
1.08.010: DESCRIPTION:
The corporate seal of the city is circular in form, with inner and outer
circles; the outer circle shall be one and seven-eighths inches (17/8") in
diameter and the inner circle one and three-sixteenths inches (13/16") in
diameter; it shall bear upon the space between the outer and inner circles the
words, "City of Shoshone, Lincoln County, Idaho", and upon the space within the
inner circle words, "Incorporated April 20, 1902", and in the center of the
space the word "seal". (Prior code § 1-308)
1.08.020: ADOPTED:
The seal described in section
1.08.010 of this chapter is adopted as the corporate seal of the city. (Prior
code § 1-309)
CHAPTER 1.12
ORDINANCES
SECTION:
1.12.010: Presentation Of Ordinances
1.12.020: Manner Of Passing
1.12.030: Endorsement After Passage
1.12.040: Mayor's Veto; Overrule Of Veto
1.12.050: Certificate To Be Attached When Veto Overruled
1.12.060: Ordinance Becoming Law Without Mayor's Signature
1.12.070: Certificate To Be Attached When Mayor Fails To Sign Or Veto
1.12.080: When Ordinance Passed
1.12.090: Effective Date
1.12.100: Preserving And Recording Of Ordinances
1.12.110: Provisions For Codification
1.12.120: Publication In Book Form
1.12.010: PRESENTATION OF ORDINANCES:
All ordinances shall be written or printed and presented to the council by a
member at a regular or special meeting. (Prior code § 1-401)
1.12.020: MANNER OF PASSING:
Every ordinance shall be read at length in meeting of the council on three (3)
different days. At each reading of an ordinance it shall be open to discussion
and amendment and may be referred to a committee, and shall be passed to the
next reading unless by a vote of the council some other disposition is made of
it. On final passage the "yeas" and the "nays" shall be called and recorded and
a concurrence of a majority of all members elected to the council shall be
required for its passage; provided, that three-fourths (3/4) of the members of
the council present may dispense with the three (3) readings and pass the
ordinances at any meeting. (Prior code § 1-402)
1.12.030: ENDORSEMENT AFTER PASSAGE:
When the ordinance is passed, it shall be signed by the clerk, and the date of
its passage, by the council, shall be added thereto, and within three (3) days
thereafter it shall be presented to the mayor, or in case of his absence from
the city, to the president of the council for his consideration. If he approves
the same, he shall attach his signature thereto, together with the date of such
approval. (Prior code § 1-403)
1.12.040: MAYOR'S VETO; OVERRULE OF VETO:
Should the mayor not approve the ordinance, he shall return the same to the
council with his objections to the same in writing on or before the date of the
next regular meeting after the same was presented to him. When an ordinance is
so returned by the mayor, the council shall proceed to reconsider the same. If,
on such reconsideration, two-thirds (2/3) of all the members elected to the
council vote in the affirmative, the ordinance shall become a law
notwithstanding the mayor's veto. (Prior code § 1-404)
1.12.050: CERTIFICATE TO BE ATTACHED WHEN VETO OVERRULED:
When any ordinance has been passed over the mayor's veto, as provided in
section 1.12.040 of this chapter, the city clerk shall annex a certificate to
the ordinance stating that the same was vetoed by the mayor, giving the date of
such veto, and that on its reconsideration by the council it received the
required two-thirds (2/3) vote of all the members elected to the council,
together with the date of such action. (Prior code § 1-405)
1.12.060: ORDINANCE BECOMING LAW WITHOUT MAYOR'S SIGNATURE:
Should the mayor refuse or neglect to sign any ordinance and return the same
with his objections in writing, on or before the date of the next regular
meeting after the same was submitted to him, it shall become a law without his
signature. (Prior code § 1-406)
1.12.070: CERTIFICATE TO BE ATTACHED WHEN MAYOR FAILS TO SIGN OR VETO:
When any ordinance has become a law without the signature of the mayor, as
provided in section 1.12.060 of this chapter, the city clerk shall annex to
such ordinance a certificate to the effect that the mayor has failed to sign or
veto the same, and it has therefore become a law without his signature. (Prior
code § 1-407)
1.12.080: WHEN ORDINANCE PASSED:
An ordinance shall be considered passed on the date of its approval by the
mayor, and in case of his vetoing an ordinance, on the date of the passage of
such ordinance over his veto, and in the case of the failure of the mayor to
sign or veto an ordinance, on the date of the next regular meeting after such
ordinance was presented to him. (Prior code § 1-408)
1.12.090: EFFECTIVE DATE:
All ordinances, unless otherwise provided in such ordinance, shall take effect
and be in force from and after their passage, approval and publication.
Publication shall be made by being inserted in one issue of some newspaper
published in the city. If no paper is published within the city, then in some
paper having general circulation in the city. (Ord. 360 § 3, 1981: prior code §
1-409)
1.12.100: PRESERVING AND RECORDING OF ORDINANCES:
It shall be the duty of the city clerk to safely preserve the original
ordinances and when passed and approved to record the same in a book provided
for that purpose, the book to be designated as, "ORDINANCE BOOK NO.        ,
CITY OF SHOSHONE". The city clerk shall attach a certificate to each ordinance,
so recorded, to the effect that the same is a true and correct copy of the
original ordinance as passed. (Prior code § 1-410)
1.12.110: PROVISIONS FOR CODIFICATION:
All the ordinances of the city of Shoshone of a general and permanent nature
shall be revised, codified, compiled and published in book form. These changes,
alterations, modifications, additions and substitutions shall be made therein
to the end that a complete simplified code of the general and permanent
ordinances of the city of Shoshone, in force at the time such codification is
completed, is presented with errors, inconsistencies, repetitions and
ambiguities eliminated. (Ord. 353 § 1, 1981)
1.12.120: PUBLICATION IN BOOK FORM:
Ordinances published in book form and passed by the council and approved by the
mayor shall be in full force and effect and no further publication of such
ordinances or revisions will be necessary to make the same effective. (Ord. 353
§ 2, 1981)
CHAPTER 1.16
INITIATIVE AND REFERENDUM
SECTION:
1.16.010: Creation Of Right
1.16.020: Number Of Petitioners Required
1.16.030: Time For Filing Petitions
1.16.040: Time For Election
1.16.050: Validation And Time Limit Requirements
1.16.010: CREATION OF RIGHT:
The people of this city shall have the right to enact ordinances through the
initiative process, and to repeal ordinances through the referendum process,
according to the procedures set forth in this chapter. (Ord. 344 § 1, 1981)
1.16.020: NUMBER OF PETITIONERS REQUIRED:
To enact an ordinance by initiative or to repeal an ordinance by referendum,
there shall be attached or appended to the petition the signatures of the legal
voters of the city equal to at least twenty percent (20%) of the total number
of voters registered to vote at the last general election in the city. (Ord.
344 § 2, 1981)
1.16.030: TIME FOR FILING PETITIONS:
Referendum petitions with the requisite number of signatures attached shall be
filed with the city clerk not less than sixty (60) days following the final
adoption of the ordinance to be subject to referendum. (Ord. 344 § 3, 1981)
1.16.040: TIME FOR ELECTION:
A special election for initiative or referendum shall be provided not more than
ninety (90) days following the certification of the petition, provided that in
the event a municipal election will occur within ninety (90) days, the
initiative and referendum shall be submitted at the time of the municipal
election. (Ord. 344 § 4, 1981)
1.16.050: VALIDATION AND TIME LIMIT REQUIREMENTS:
Referendum and initiative petitions shall conform with the requirements for
signature, verification of valid petitions, printing of petitions, and time
limits, except as expressly modified to meet the purposes of initiative and
referendum to be as nearly as practicable as provided in sections 34-1701
through 34-1705 of the Idaho Code. (Ord. 344 § 5, 1981)
CHAPTER 1.20
ELECTIONS 1
SECTION:
1.20.010: Supervision Of Administration Of Election Laws By County Clerk
1.20.020: Registration Of Electors
1.20.030: General And Special City Elections
 
Notes
1 1. IC title 50, ch. 4.
1.20.010: SUPERVISION OF ADMINISTRATION OF ELECTION LAWS BY COUNTY CLERK:
For each city, the county clerk of the county is the chief elections officer
and shall exercise general supervision of the administration of the election
laws in the city for the purpose of achieving and maintaining a maximum degree
of correctness, impartiality, efficiency and uniformity. The county clerk shall
meet with and issue instructions to election judges and clerks prior to the
opening of the polls to ensure uniformity in the application, operation and
interpretation of the election laws during the election. (Ord. 542, 2013)
1.20.020: REGISTRATION OF ELECTORS:
All electors must register before being able to vote at any municipal election.
The county clerk shall be the registrar for all city elections and shall
conduct voter registration for each city pursuant to the provision of chapter
4, title 34, Idaho Code. To be eligible to register to vote in city elections,
a person shall be at least eighteen (18) years of age, a citizen of the United
States and a resident of the city for at least thirty (30) days preceding the
next election at which he/she desires to vote, or a resident of an area annexed
by a city pursuant to the provisions of chapter 2, title 50, Idaho Code. (Ord.
542, 2013)
1.20.030: GENERAL AND SPECIAL CITY ELECTIONS:
   A.   A general election shall be held in each city governed by this title,
on the Tuesday following the first Monday of November in each odd numbered
year. All such officials shall be elected and hold their respective offices for
the term specified and until their successors are elected and qualified. All
other city elections that may be held under authority of general law shall be
known as special city elections.
   B.   On and after January 1, 2011, notwithstanding any other provisions of
law to the contrary, there shall be no more than two (2) elections conducted in
any city in any calendar year, except as provided in this section.
   C.   The dates on which elections may be conducted are:
      1.   The third Tuesday in May of each year; and
      2.   The Tuesday following the first Monday in November of each year.
      3.   In addition to the elections specified in subsections C1 and C2 of
this section, an emergency election may be called upon motion of the city
council of a city. An emergency exists when there is a great public calamity,
such as an extraordinary fire, flood, storm, epidemic or other disaster, or if
it is necessary to do emergency work to prepare for a national or local
defense, or it is necessary to do emergency work to safeguard life, health or
property.
   D.   Pursuant to section 34-1401, Idaho Code, all municipal elections shall
be conducted by the county clerk of the county wherein the city lies, and
elections shall be administered in accordance with the provisions of title 34,
Idaho Code, except as those provisions are specifically modified by the
provisions of this chapter. After an election has been ordered, all expenses
associated with conducting municipal general and special elections shall be
paid from the county election fund as provided by section 34-1411, Idaho Code.
Expenses associated with conducting runoff elections shall be paid by the city
adopting runoff elections pursuant to the provisions of section 50-612 or 50-
707B, Idaho Code, or both.
   E.   The secretary of state is authorized to provide such assistance as
necessary, and to prescribe any needed rules or interpretations for the conduct
of elections authorized under the provisions of this section. (Ord. 542, 2013)
CHAPTER 1.24
GENERAL PENALTY
SECTION:
1.24.010: In General
1.24.020: Applicability
1.24.030: The Term "Infraction" Changed To "Violation"
1.24.010: IN GENERAL:
Any person convicted of a violation of any ordinance of the city may be fined
in a sum not to exceed three hundred dollars ($300.00) for any offense and such
person may be confined in a jail for a period of not more than thirty (30)
days. Either or both such fine and imprisonment may be imposed; and in addition
thereto, any person so convicted shall pay such costs as the court may assess.
(Ord. 308 § 1, 1981)
1.24.020: APPLICABILITY:
The penalty provided in this chapter shall be applicable to every ordinance of
the city the same as though it were a part of each and every separate
ordinance. Any person convicted of a violation of any ordinance of this city
shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. A separate offense shall be deemed
committed for each day during or on which a violation occurs or continues.
(Ord. 308 § 3, 1981)
1.24.030: THE TERM "INFRACTION" CHANGED TO "VIOLATION":
The word "infraction" wherever found throughout this code, except where it
occurs in relation to a traffic infraction, shall be replaced with the word
"violation". (Ord. 396 § 1, 1989)
CHAPTER 1.28
AREA OF CITY IMPACT
SECTION:
1.28.010: Purpose
1.28.020: Consideration
1.28.030: Geographic Area Of City Impact
1.28.040: Comprehensive Plan
1.28.050: Zoning And Subdivision Ordinances
1.28.060: Administration
1.28.010: PURPOSE:
The purpose of establishing an area of city impact is to identify a logical
urban fringe area adjoining the city of Shoshone, Idaho, pursuant to the
provisions of section 67-6526, Idaho Code. (Ord. 379 § 1, 1986)
1.28.020: CONSIDERATION:
The following factors were considered by the planning and zoning commission and
the council and mayor of the city in the establishment of an area of city
impact:
   A.   Trade area;
   B.   Geographic factors; and
   C.   Areas that can reasonably be expected to be joined to the city in the
future. (Ord. 379 § 2, 1986)
1.28.030: GEOGRAPHIC AREA OF CITY IMPACT:
The officially adopted geographic area of city impact is shown on the map
entitled "area of city impact", attached to ordinance 464 on file in the office
of the city clerk. (Ord. 485, 2003: Ord. 379 § 3, 1986)
1.28.040: COMPREHENSIVE PLAN:
The comprehensive plan and subsequent amendments thereto as officially adopted
by the city shall apply to the area of city impact within the unincorporated
area of Lincoln County, Idaho. (Ord. 379 § 4, 1986)
1.28.050: ZONING AND SUBDIVISION ORDINANCES:
The zoning and subdivision ordinances and subsequent amendments thereto as
officially adopted by the city shall apply to the area of city impact within
the unincorporated area of Lincoln County, Idaho. (Ord. 379 § 5, 1986)
1.28.060: ADMINISTRATION:
   A.   Integration Of Recitals: The recitals set forth in Shoshone city
ordinances and Lincoln County ordinances, pertaining to the area of city
impact, which are on file in the office of the city clerk and in the office of
the county clerk, are incorporated in this document and by this reference are
made a part hereof. (Ord. 485, 2003: Ord. 465, 2000: Ord. 435, 1995: Ord. 379 §
6, 1986)

CHAPTER 2.04
CITY COUNCIL
SECTION:
2.04.010: Number Of Council
2.04.020: President; Authority To Elect
2.04.030: President; Powers
2.04.040: Meetings; Time And Place
2.04.050: Meetings; Notice
2.04.060: Special Meetings; How Called
2.04.070: Special Meetings; Notice
2.04.010: NUMBER OF COUNCIL:
There shall be four (4) councilmen who shall be elected at the time and in the
manner as provided by the laws of Idaho. (Ord. 360 § 1, 1981: prior code § 1-
301)
2.04.020: PRESIDENT; AUTHORITY TO ELECT:
The city council shall have authority to elect one of its members as president
of the council, who shall hold such office until the next biennial election in
the municipality. (Prior code § 1-302)
2.04.030: PRESIDENT; POWERS:
When elected as provided in section 2.04.020 of this chapter, the president
shall preside at all meetings of the city council and serve as mayor in the
absence of the mayor, and when so occupying the office of mayor, the president
of the council shall have the same privileges as the mayor, and all acts of the
president of the council while so acting shall be binding upon the council and
upon the city as if done by the mayor. (Prior code § 1-303)
2.04.040: MEETINGS; TIME AND PLACE:
Starting on March 1, 1998, the regular meetings of the city council shall
commence at the hour of seven o'clock (7:00) P.M. on the first and third
Tuesday of each and every month at the city hall, unless otherwise announced
according to law. (Ord. 485, 2003: Ord. 432, 1995: prior code §§ 1-304, 1-305)
2.04.050: MEETINGS; NOTICE:
Notice of meetings shall be published at the passage of this chapter and then
annually in the official newspaper, and the agenda of each meeting shall be
posted in a front window of the city hall, in plain view of the public, at
least forty eight (48) hours prior to the opening of the meeting. Additional
agenda items may be added by following the requirements of section 67-2343,
Idaho Code. (Ord. 432, 1995)
2.04.060: SPECIAL MEETINGS; HOW CALLED:
Special meetings may be called by the president of the council, mayor, or by
any three (3) members thereof, to be held at the time mentioned in the notice
provided for in section 2.04.070 of this chapter. (Ord. 360 § 2, 1981: prior
code § 1-306)
2.04.070: SPECIAL MEETINGS; NOTICE:
   A.   When the president of the council, or any three (3) members thereof,
desires to call special meetings, he or they shall give not less than one day's
written notice to the clerk, stating the time and object of the special
meeting, and it shall be the duty of the clerk to notify all members of the
council and it shall be the duty of the clerk to file such written notice and
to record same in the minutes of the special meeting called by virtue of such
notice.
   B.   Only one meeting can be held on the same day. (Prior code § 1-307)
CHAPTER 2.08
CITY OFFICERS
SECTION:
2.08.010: Duties
2.08.010: DUTIES:
   A.   In addition to the city councilmen, the officers of the city shall be:
      1.   The mayor, whose duties shall be prescribed by law;
      2.   The city clerk, whose duties shall be as prescribed by law;
      3.   The city treasurer, whose duties shall be prescribed by law;
      4.   The city attorney, whose duties shall be prescribed by law; and
      5.   Such other officers as shall be designated.
   B.   Further duties than those provided by the Idaho Code may be assigned to
the respective officers by the mayor and council of the city; provided,
however, that the city clerk may, at the direction of the mayor and city
council, serve also as treasurer. (Ord. 361, 1981)
CHAPTER 2.10
APPOINTMENT OF CITY OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES
SECTION:
2.10.010: Appointments
2.10.020: Hiring Of Other Employees Of The City
2.10.030: Librarian
2.10.040: Term Of Appointed Officers
2.10.010: APPOINTMENTS:
The city clerk/treasurer, police chief, city attorney, maintenance supervisor
shall be appointed by the mayor with approval of one-half (1/2) plus one of the
city council. If the council does not ratify the appointed officer, the mayor
shall within ten (10) days nominate another person for the job. The city
council at its next regular scheduled meeting or sooner shall then approve or
reject the appointee. This shall continue until the city council and mayor
agree on the nominee. (Ord. 485, 2003)
2.10.020: HIRING OF OTHER EMPLOYEES OF THE CITY:
The officers of the city may hire other employees as needed with the approval
of the mayor and city council. Interviews shall be held by the department head
and the mayor and any other council person that may wish to attend. (Ord. 485,
2003)
2.10.030: LIBRARIAN:
The librarian shall be hired by the library board with approval of the mayor
and city council. (Ord. 485, 2003)
2.10.040: TERM OF APPOINTED OFFICERS:
All appointed officers shall serve a term of four (4) years or until the next
mayor is elected. (Ord. 485, 2003)
CHAPTER 2.12
OFFICERS' BONDS
SECTION:
2.12.010: Designated
2.12.010: DESIGNATED:
   A.   Before entering upon the duties of their respective offices after any
election or appointment, the officers named in this section who do not at this
time have bonds posted shall give bonds to the city for the faithful
performance of their duties, in the amount specified in this section:
      1.   City clerk: In the sum of five thousand dollars ($5,000.00);
      2.   City treasurer: In the sum of five thousand dollars ($5,000.00).
   B.   The premium on the bonds required of the above officers shall be paid
by the city.
   C.   The failure on the part of any of the above named officers to give
bonds as specified in this section before the commencement of his term of
office shall be grounds for, and the city council may thereupon declare such
office vacant and proceed to fill such office as required by law. (Prior code §
1-511)
CHAPTER 2.16
POLICE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
2.16.010: Created
2.16.020: Appointment Of Personnel
2.16.030: Police Officer Powers
2.16.040: Chief Of Police; Administrative Authority
2.16.050: Chief Of Police; Report
2.16.060: Citizenship Requirement
2.16.070: Assisting Police Officer; Refusal Unlawful
2.16.010: CREATED:
There is created a police department in the city. The department shall consist
of a chief of police and such other policemen as shall be authorized by the
mayor and council. (Prior code § 1-701)
2.16.020: APPOINTMENT OF PERSONNEL:
The mayor, with the consent of the council, shall appoint the chief of police
provided for in section
2.16.010 of this chapter, and the chief of police shall have authority, with
the consent of the council, to appoint special policemen from time to time as
exigencies arise. (Prior code § 1-702)
2.16.030: POLICE OFFICER POWERS:
The officers and members of the police department shall have power to arrest
all offenders against the law of the state, or of the city, by day or by night,
in the same manner as other police officers of the state, and keep them in the
city jail or other place to prevent their escape, until trial can be had before
the proper officer. They shall likewise be vested with power to serve any other
process issued under authority of the ordinances of the city. (Prior code § 1-
703)
2.16.040: CHIEF OF POLICE; ADMINISTRATIVE AUTHORITY:
All persons appointed under the provisions of this chapter as policemen or
special police shall be under the direction and supervision of the chief of
police. In the absence of the chief of police, an assistant chief of police,
appointed by the mayor, with the consent of the council, shall have all the
authority herein vested in the chief of police. The policemen shall be subject
to the orders of the chief of police, except in case otherwise provided by
ordinance. It shall be their duty to cause the public peace to be preserved and
to see that all laws and ordinances are enforced within the city limits. When
violation of any law or ordinance is reported to them or comes to their
knowledge, they shall cause the required complaint to be made and see that all
possible evidence is procured for the successful prosecution of the offenders.
(Prior code § 1-704)
2.16.050: CHIEF OF POLICE; REPORT:
The chief of police shall make a written monthly report giving a true account
of the number of arrests made, persons arrested and nature of offenses charged,
during the month and such further reports as may at times be requested by the
mayor and council. (Prior code § 1-705)
2.16.060: CITIZENSHIP REQUIREMENT:
Any person appointed as an officer or member of the police department shall be
a citizen of the United States. (Prior code § 1-706)
2.16.070: ASSISTING POLICE OFFICER; REFUSAL UNLAWFUL:
The chief of police, or any member of the police department, shall have
authority to call upon any person to assist him in making an arrest, capturing
or retaining in custody any person. Any person, when so requested, who refuses
or fails, to the best of his ability, to render such aid as required shall be
guilty of an offense. (Prior code § 1-707)
CHAPTER 2.20
FIRE DEPARTMENT
(Rep. by Ord. 485, 2003)
CHAPTER 2.24
DIVISION OF PUBLIC WORKS
SECTION:
2.24.010: Created
2.24.020: Maintenance Supervisor Of Public Works; Authority
2.24.030: Maintenance Supervisor Of Public Works; Duties
2.24.040: Maintenance Supervisor Of Public Works; Park Duties
2.24.050: Garbage Collection And Disposal System
2.24.010: CREATED:
There is created a division of public works in the city. The division of public
works shall consist of the sanitation, parks, sewer, streets, water, and
irrigation departments. The division shall consist of a maintenance supervisor
of public works and such other personnel as shall be authorized by the mayor
and council. (Ord. 485, 2003)
2.24.020: MAINTENANCE SUPERVISOR OF PUBLIC WORKS; AUTHORITY:
The maintenance supervisor of public works shall, subject to the orders of the
mayor and council, have general charge, direction, and control of all streets,
avenues, alleys, thoroughfares, curbs, gutters, culverts, and bridges, and all
maintenance, repair, grading, building, laying, surfacing and other work
appurtenant to or on the city streets, avenues, alleys, thoroughfares, curbs,
gutters, culverts and bridges and all streets, sewers, parks, water, garbage
and irrigation departments of the city of Shoshone and all work that shall be
needed to maintain, improve and keep up to code such departments. (Ord. 485,
2003)
2.24.030: MAINTENANCE SUPERVISOR OF PUBLIC WORKS; DUTIES:
The maintenance supervisor of public works shall have the following duties:
   A.   He shall see that all open ditches, excavations, or other conditions
that are or might be dangerous or hazardous on or along the streets, avenues,
alleys or thoroughfares of the city are carefully guarded by rails and light or
other proper warning signals.
   B.   He shall install and maintain all signs, traffic signals, except
electric traffic signals, zone markings and other devices necessary for the
safe and orderly direction of vehicles and pedestrians upon the streets,
avenues, alleys, and thoroughfares of the city.
   C.   He shall maintain all the streets, avenues, alleys, and thoroughfares
in a clean and orderly manner, and remove or cause to be removed debris,
rubbish, trash, broken trees, and branches and all other unsightly or dangerous
refuse, and, in addition, when necessary remove such ice and snow that has
accumulated on the streets, avenues, alleys, and thoroughfares in the city.
   D.   He shall at frequent intervals examine and inspect the streets,
avenues, alleys, thoroughfares, curbs, gutters, culverts, and bridges in the
city to enable him to comply with his duties as set forth in section
2.24.020 of this chapter and subsections A, B, and C of this section.
   E.   He shall keep an inventory of all property belonging to the department
of streets and shall, with the consent of the mayor and council, purchase
supplies and equipment necessary for the maintenance of the department.
   F.   He shall, upon request, attend meetings of the city council and render
such reports and statements as may be required by the mayor and city council.
(Ord. 485, 2003)
2.24.040: MAINTENANCE SUPERVISOR OF PUBLIC WORKS; PARK DUTIES:
The maintenance supervisor of public works, subject to the order of the mayor
and council, shall have general charge, direction, and control of the public
buildings, parks, grounds and lands of the city, and the maintenance, repair,
upkeep, and all other work appurtenant thereto of the buildings, parks, grounds
and lands of the city. (Ord. 485, 2003)
2.24.050: GARBAGE COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL SYSTEM:
   A.   The maintenance supervisor of public works shall, subject to the order
of the mayor and city council, have general charge, direction and control of
the garbage collection and disposal system of the city.
   B.   The maintenance supervisor of public works shall see that all garbage,
waste and refuse are collected in the city as set forth in this section:
      1.   Each and every day, except Sunday and holidays, before the hour of
twelve o'clock (12:00) noon from all the public and private business
establishments on and along the north and south side of A Street, North Rail
Street, South Rail Street, and east and west side of Greenwood Street.
      2.   In all other areas within limits of the city, the collection of
garbage, waste, and refuse will be at the direction of the garbage collector,
with the consent of the maintenance supervisor of public works, provided the
garbage, waste, and refuse is collected from each resident within the city
limits no less than once each week; and provided further, that reasonable
notice is given to the residents as to which day or days in the week the
garbage, waste, and refuse will be collected. (Ord. 485, 2003)
CHAPTER 2.28
WATERWORKS
SECTION:
2.28.010: Duties And Responsibilities
2.28.020: Supervision Of Connections, Installations, And Excavations
2.28.030: Pumping Station And Reservoir Maintenance
2.28.040: Meter Inspection
2.28.050: Inspections
2.28.060: Record Of Costs For Connections
2.28.070: Inventory Of Property
2.28.080: Attendance At Meetings
2.28.090: Collection Of Water Charges
2.28.010: DUTIES AND RESPONSIBILITIES:
The maintenance supervisor of public works shall, under the direction of the
mayor and city council, have charge of the water system, the reservoirs,
conduits, water tanks, water mains, fire hydrants, and all machinery, property,
and appurtenances pertaining to the waterworks. (Ord. 485, 2003)
2.28.020: SUPERVISION OF CONNECTIONS, INSTALLATIONS, AND EXCAVATIONS:
The maintenance supervisor of public works shall attend to the tapping of
mains, and laying and connecting up of laterals and installation of meters and
meter boxes, and shall see that all open ditches and excavations on or along
the streets, alleys, and thoroughfares of the city are carefully guarded by
rails and lights or other proper warning signals. (Ord. 485, 2003)
2.28.030: PUMPING STATION AND RESERVOIR MAINTENANCE:
The maintenance supervisor of public works shall have charge of and operate the
pumping station and reservoir and shall keep the mains of the system filled
with pure and wholesome water at a pressure sufficient for proper fire
protection. (Ord. 485, 2003)
2.28.040: METER INSPECTION:
At the end of each and every calendar month the maintenance supervisor of
public works shall read and inspect all meters and enter the present reading
thereof in a permanent record opposite the last previous reading, and shall
prior to the hour of nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. of the fifth business day before
the close of each calendar month deliver the same to the city clerk. (Ord. 485,
2003)
2.28.050: INSPECTIONS:
The maintenance supervisor of public works shall at frequent intervals examine
the premises of customers supplied with water at the flat rate, and report to
the city clerk any improper diversions or use of water, or use of equipment
other than that specified for flat rate customers. (Ord. 485, 2003)
2.28.060: RECORD OF COSTS FOR CONNECTIONS:
The maintenance supervisor of public works shall keep a record of the cost of
the labor and materials for each connection made or for any service rendered,
which cost record shall be completed immediately following each job and be kept
on file in the office of the maintenance supervisor of public works. (Ord. 485,
2003)
2.28.070: INVENTORY OF PROPERTY:
The maintenance supervisor of public works shall also keep an inventory of all
property belonging to the water system and shall, with the consent of the mayor
and council, purchase supplies and equipment necessary for the maintenance of
the system. (Ord. 485, 2003)
2.28.080: ATTENDANCE AT MEETINGS:
The maintenance supervisor of public works shall, upon request, attend meetings
of the city council and render such report and statements as may be required.
He shall perform such other duties as may be required of him by ordinance or
order of the mayor or council, and to the end that the provisions of sections
2.28.010 through 2.28.070 of this chapter may be carried out, the maintenance
supervisor of public works shall be allowed such assistance as the mayor or
council may deem necessary and proper. (Ord. 485, 2003)
2.28.090: COLLECTION OF WATER CHARGES:
   A.   The city clerk shall maintain an office in the business district of the
city and shall keep the same open five (5) days each week except for holidays
as set by the mayor and city council by resolution between the hours of eight
thirty o'clock (8:30) A.M. and four thirty o'clock (4:30) P.M., for receiving
payment and collection of water rates, rentals and charges due from the water
customers as provided in this section, and such other city business as may come
before the clerk.
   B.   The clerk shall compute from the readings furnished to him by the
maintenance supervisor of public works the amount due from each customer at
rates set by the city council and mayor by resolution, and shall keep accounts
with all water customers in proper, permanent books to be provided for the
clerk for that purpose at the expense of the city and shall render monthly
statements to each and every customer, keeping a duplicate thereof on file in
the clerk's office and shall receipt the original when payment is made and of
the amount due.
   C.   At the expiration of the fifteenth day of each and every month, the
clerk shall prepare a list of all delinquent customers with the amount due from
each, including penalty. Upon the expiration of the fifteenth day of the
following month the clerk shall prepare a list of water customers to be cut off
and give names to the maintenance supervisor of public works whose duty it
shall be to collect the same, together with charges, or to shut off the water
of the customers if the same is not immediately paid; provided that the
services rendered by the city shall not be discontinued until the city has
complied with the procedure for notice and hearing as specified in subsections
13.08.730B, C, and D of this code.
   D.   It shall be the duty of the city clerk to make report at the end of
each and every month of all water rentals, and other charges received during
the month. He shall turn the monies over to the city treasurer and shall take
and file the treasurer's receipt therefor and a duplicate of the report shall
be filed with the city council at their next regular meeting, together with a
list of all customers who have been discontinued as provided in this section.
   E.   The maintenance supervisor of public works shall keep on file in his
office a map of the water system showing the locations of mains, gates, fire
hydrants, crosses, tees, plugs and underground fixtures and appendages together
with the sizes thereof. (Ord. 485, 2003)
CHAPTER 2.32
PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION
SECTION:
2.32.010: Created; Membership
2.32.020: Residency Required; Term Of Office
2.32.030: Vacancy Filling
2.32.040: Election Procedure
2.32.050: Organization
2.32.060: Powers And Duties
2.32.010: CREATED; MEMBERSHIP:
There is created a planning and zoning commission for the city to be known as
the planning and zoning commission of the city of Shoshone, Idaho; the
commission shall consist of five (5) members to be appointed by the mayor and
confirmed by a majority of the city council. A sixth member is to be appointed
by the county commissioners of Lincoln County to come from the impact area of
the city of Shoshone. (Ord. 485, 2003: Ord. 351 § 1, 1980)
2.32.020: RESIDENCY REQUIRED; TERM OF OFFICE:
Each member of the commission shall have resided in the city for two (2) years
prior to appointment. The terms of office of the five (5) first appointed shall
be two (2) for three (3) years, one for four (4) years, one for five (5) years,
and one for six (6) years, to be determined by lot, and thereafter the term of
office of each member shall be six (6) years. (Ord. 485, 2003: Ord. 351 § 2,
1980)
2.32.030: VACANCY FILLING:
Vacancies arising other than through the expirations of terms shall be filled
by the mayor and confirmed by the majority of the city council. (Ord. 351 § 3,
1980)
2.32.040: ELECTION PROCEDURE:
Members of the commission shall be appointed without respect to political
affiliations, shall serve without compensation unless per diem and/or mileage
are provided by the city council, and may be removed for cause after a public
hearing by a majority vote of the city council. (Ord. 485, 2003: Ord. 351 § 4,
1980)
2.32.050: ORGANIZATION:
The commission shall select its own chairman and create and fill such other
offices as it may determine it requires. During not less than nine (9) months
in each year, one regular monthly meeting shall be held. A majority of the
members of the commission is necessary to constitute a quorum at any meeting
and all meetings shall be open to the public. Written rules or bylaws
consistent with chapter 65 of title 67 of the Idaho Code and other laws of this
state for transaction of the business of the commission shall be adopted; and a
written record of meetings, resolutions, findings, and determinations shall be
kept as a public record. (Ord. 351 § 5, 1980)
2.32.060: POWERS AND DUTIES:
It is the duty of the commission to recommend and make suggestions to the city
council for the adoption of coordinated plans for the development of the city;
for the formation of zoning districts; concerning the laying out, widening,
extending, locating, or closing of streets or alleys, roads and highways for
the handling of traffic; concerning density of population and development of
lands in the city; concerning the future growth, development, and
beautification of the city in respect to its public buildings, streets, parks,
grounds, and lands, consistent with the future growth and development of the
city, in order to promote the public health, safety, and welfare of the
inhabitants. It is also the duty of the commission to give suggestions and
advice to individuals concerning landscaping or location of buildings,
structures, or works to be erected, constructed, or altered by or for the
individuals. The commission may cooperate with other and like commissions along
the lines and purposes prescribed in this chapter and in the laws of the state,
and shall have all authority granted by, and shall carry out the duties of, the
commission, as provided in title 67, chapter 65 of the Idaho Code and any
amendments thereof. (Ord. 351 § 6, 1980)
CHAPTER 2.36
SALARIES
SECTION:
2.36.010: Mayor And Council Salaries
2.36.010: MAYOR AND COUNCIL SALARIES:
Commencing January 1, 2004, the salaries of the mayor and of the members of the
Shoshone city council shall be as follows:
   A.   The mayor shall receive a monthly salary in the sum of two hundred
seventy five dollars ($275.00);
   B.   Each member of the council shall receive a monthly salary in the sum of
two hundred dollars ($200.00);
   C.   Whenever any member of the council assumes the office of mayor during
his absence such councilman shall receive an additional fifteen dollars
($15.00) per regular meeting while so acting, said sum to be deducted from the
salary of the mayor. (Ord. 487 § 1, 2003: Ord. 476 § 1, 2001: Ord. 430 § 1,
1994: Ord. 385 § 1, 1987: Ord. 330 § 1, 1975)
