CHAPTER 5.01
GENERAL REGISTRATION PROVISIONS
SECTION:
5.01.010: Purpose
5.01.020: Definitions
5.01.030: Registration
5.01.040: Payment Of Fees; Registration, Issuance
5.01.050: Contents And Authority Of Registrations
5.01.060: Term Of Registration
5.01.070: Building And Premises
5.01.080: Inspections
5.01.010: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to maintain an accurate listing of trades,
businesses, and professions located within the city of Shoshone in order to:
   A.   Allow the city of Shoshone and other interested parties to better
communicate with the Shoshone business community and comprehend the business
categories that may be over or under served in the area.
   B.   Any legal business located within the city limits prior to the passage
of this chapter shall be exempt from this chapter.
   C.   Any business that registers with the city of Shoshone will have their
name, address, phone number, and a link to their business/website on the city
of Shoshone's website. (Ord. 537, 2013)
5.01.020: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, trade, business and entities, or activities, excluding
"solicitor", "special event", "temporary merchant", or vendor as defined in
chapter 5.20 of this title, which hold themselves out to the public as
businesses, trades, or professions regardless of size and including such
trades, businesses, or professions constituting home occupations. (Ord. 537,
2013)
5.01.030: REGISTRATION:
No person shall engage in or carry on any trade, business, or profession within
the limits of the city of Shoshone until such person or entity has registered
with the city clerk's office, located at Shoshone City Hall, as described in
this chapter. (Ord. 537, 2013)
5.01.040: PAYMENT OF FEES; REGISTRATION, ISSUANCE:
To benefit trade, business, and professions, optional fees should be paid in
advance to the city clerk as adopted by resolution of the city council. The
optional fee will be in place to help with the administration of the website
and for future beautification. (Ord. 537, 2013)
5.01.050: CONTENTS AND AUTHORITY OF REGISTRATIONS:
Every registration issued pursuant to this chapter shall contain and set forth
the name, location, and type of each trade, business, or profession for which
such registration is granted. Said registration shall authorize the continuance
of the business named therein for the term of such registration, unless the
place registered shall be closed. In such cases, the city clerk shall be
notified of the change and shall note the same in the register of
registrations. (Ord. 537, 2013)
5.01.060: TERM OF REGISTRATION:
All registrations shall expire the last day of each year, and shall be dated
from the first day issued until the last day of the current year. Each such
general business registration may be renewed before the end of each calendar
year by notice to the city clerk in writing, and payment of the registration
fee. (Ord. 537, 2013)
5.01.070: BUILDING AND PREMISES:
   A.   No registration shall be issued for the conduct of any business and no
registration shall be issued for any thing or act if the premises and building
to be used for the purpose do not fully comply with the international building
code requirements.
   B.   In every case where more than one business, trade, or profession shall
be pursued or carried on in the same place by the same person or other persons
at the same time, a registration must be taken out for each business
accordingly.
   C.   In the absence of any provision to the contrary, the location of any
registered business or occupation or of any permitted act may be changed,
provided ten (10) days' notice thereof is given to the city clerk's office, and
provided the building requirements of this code are complied with.
   D.   It shall be the responsibility of commercial building and premises'
owners to install and maintain all backflow preventers, vacuum breakers, grease
traps, etc., within the building or on the premises in good working order and
to make no piping or other arrangements for the purpose of bypassing these
devices. All assemblies must be tested upon installation by a tester licensed
in the state of Idaho to test these assemblies. The test report must be sent to
city hall.
      1.   All assemblies must be tested annually by a tester who is licensed
in the state of Idaho to test these assemblies and maintained to ensure proper
operation on a continuing basis. Annual test reports shall be sent to city
hall. All testing procedures shall be in accordance with the manufacturer's
instructions. (Ord. 537, 2013)
5.01.080: INSPECTIONS:
At the request of any new business or existing business, the city clerk will
help facilitate any inspections needed within the city limits, all buildings,
premises and public thoroughfares, except interior of private dwellings, for
the purposes of ascertaining any conditions liable to cause fire, or health and
safety issues or violations of regulations promulgated by the city for the
purpose of reducing fire hazards or injury to the public. (Ord. 537, 2013)
CHAPTER 5.04
ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES
SECTION:
5.04.010: State Statutes Adopted
5.04.020: Copies On File
5.04.030: City Licensing Requirements And Restrictions; License Fees
5.04.010: STATE STATUTES ADOPTED:
There is adopted, for the purpose of governing the licensing, sale, and use of
alcoholic beverages within the city, the laws of the state, being particularly
title 23, Idaho Code, as presently in effect or as may hereafter be amended by
the legislature and as contained in that certain volume "Idaho liquor and beer
laws", revised through the acts of the 1969 legislature, published by authority
of the department of law enforcement, liquor law division, as the same may be
revised by the legislature or by the governing body of the city. The same are
adopted and incorporated as an ordinance of the city as fully as though set
forth at length in this chapter. (Ord. 306 § 1, 1971)
5.04.020: COPIES ON FILE:
Three (3) copies of the Idaho liquor and beer laws, together with all
amendments thereto, all duly certified by the city clerk, shall be kept on file
in the office of the city clerk for use and examination of and by the public.
(Ord. 306 § 2, 1971)
5.04.030: CITY LICENSING REQUIREMENTS AND RESTRICTIONS; LICENSE FEES:
   A.   It is a misdemeanor for any person to sell beer, wine, or any other
beverage containing any alcohol whatsoever without first securing a retailer's
license from the city.
   B.   The following fee schedule is adopted by this chapter:
 
1. Beer, bottled or canned and consumed on premises  $ 50.00
2. Beer, bottled or canned not consumed on premises  25.00
3. Draft and bottled or canned or draft only         100.00
4. Retail liquor                                     375.00
5. Retail wine                                       25.00
6. Wine by the drink                                 25.00
 
   C.   All applications for retail alcohol licenses, transfers and renewals
must be submitted to the city clerk at the Shoshone city hall during normal
working hours with the appropriate fees in cash.
Blank applications may be acquired from the city clerk. Applications must be
submitted on or before the Wednesday just preceding the next council meeting.
The city clerk shall cause said application to be investigated and then shall
present such application to the city council for deliberation at the next
timely council meeting along with preliminary recommendations and testimony of
witnesses if any. The chief of police shall assist the clerk in the
investigation into the applicant's background and a criminal history check
shall be secured in all cases. Anyone convicted of a felony shall not receive a
license unless the felony is removed from the applicant's record by legal
process or governor pardon.
   D.   The city council shall have a period of thirty five (35) days to
examine the application before a decision must be made on granting or denying
the license, or the transfer or renewal thereof. If the council fails to make a
decision within thirty five (35) days of receiving the application, not
counting the day of reception, then the license shall be granted by law with no
further action by the council.
   E.   Whenever the city council denies an application the council must within
fifteen (15) days refund all fees submitted and specify the grounds for denial
in writing, explaining the following:
      1.   The statutes, ordinances and standards used in evaluating the
application;
      2.   The reasons for denial;
      3.   The actions, if any, that the applicant could take to obtain the
license, transfer, or renewal thereof.
   F.   All current licenses must be prominently displayed in the place of
business of licensee.
   G.   All licenses shall expire at one o'clock (1:00) A.M. on January 1
following the license issuance and shall be subject to renewal upon proper
application.
   H.   Where any word, phrase, clause, sentence, paragraph, section, provision
or other part of this chapter or of this code and subdivision or zoning
ordinances are held to be invalid by a court of competent jurisdiction, such
judgment shall affect only that specific part held invalid and all other parts
shall be presumed to survive and be valid. (Ord. 408 §§ 1 – 8, 1991)
CHAPTER 5.08
WINE
SECTION:
5.08.010: License Required
5.08.020: License Application
5.08.030: License Revocation
5.08.040: License Fee
5.08.050: License Transferability
5.08.060: Compliance With Provisions
5.08.070: Hours Of Sale Restricted
5.08.010: LICENSE REQUIRED:
Licenses for the retail sale of wine as defined in chapter 13, title 23, of the
Idaho Code are issued in the city to applicants having licenses from the state
and the county therefor. (Ord. 314, 1971)
5.08.020: LICENSE APPLICATION:
Each applicant shall file application with the city clerk showing that the
applicant possesses a state and county license. (Ord. 314 § 1, 1971)
5.08.030: LICENSE REVOCATION:
The violation of any law of the state with respect to handling or retail sale
of wine by a licensee shall subject the city license to revocation. (Ord. 314 §
3, 1971)
5.08.040: LICENSE FEE:
   A.   Retailers who possess a valid license for the retail sale of liquor by
the drink may sell wine by the drink for consumption on the licensed premises
only without further city license. Retailers who do not have a license to sell
liquor by the drink may obtain a city license to sell wine by the drink or a
license to sell wine in unbroken containers; the annual fee for each license
issued shall be such fee as city council shall by resolution set from time to
time.
   B.   All licenses issued on or after July 1 of any year shall be issued for
a fee of one-half (1/2) the annual charge for the license. (Ord. 375, 1985:
Ord. 314 § 5, 1971)
5.08.050: LICENSE TRANSFERABILITY:
No transfer of license shall be made until transferee has obtained a transfer
for the state and county license and has paid an accompanying transfer fee of
five dollars ($5.00). A license shall be issued only to be used upon the
premises for which state and county licenses were issued. (Ord. 314 § 5, 1971)
5.08.060: COMPLIANCE WITH PROVISIONS:
The obedience to all laws of the state pertaining to the sale and handling of
wine shall be and are a prerequisite to obtaining and holding a valid license
by the city. (Ord. 314 § 2, 1971)
5.08.070: HOURS OF SALE RESTRICTED:
The hours and days of sale shall be the same as provided for sale of beer in
the city. (Ord. 314 § 4, 1971)
CHAPTER 5.12
CARD TABLES
(Rep. by Ord. 500, 2006)
CHAPTER 5.16
CIRCUS
SECTION:
5.16.010: Definitions
5.16.020: License Required
5.16.030: License Fee
5.16.040: Applicability Of Provisions
5.16.010: DEFINITIONS:
A "circus" as defined by this chapter means a performance or exhibition held
under a tent in which riding or acrobatic feats are performed for profit.
(Prior code § 2-302)
5.16.020: LICENSE REQUIRED:
It is unlawful to carry on or exhibit any circus within the city without first
obtaining a license therefor as provided in this chapter. (Prior code § 2-301)
5.16.030: LICENSE FEE:
The city clerk shall issue licenses for such entertainments as are mentioned in
this chapter and shall charge therefor fifteen dollars ($15.00) for each day
such exhibitions are given. (Prior code § 2-304)
5.16.040: APPLICABILITY OF PROVISIONS:
It is unlawful for a vendor of medicine or other commodities to give
entertainments on the public streets or elsewhere within the corporate limits
of the city to give such entertainments without first procuring a license.
(Prior code § 2-303)
CHAPTER 5.20
VENDORS, SOLICITORS, AND TEMPORARY MERCHANTS
SECTION:
5.20.010: Purpose
5.20.020: Definitions
5.20.030: Registrations Required
5.20.040: Exceptions
5.20.050: Application For Registration
5.20.060: Registration Fees
5.20.070: Registration Issuance And Exhibition
5.20.080: Restrictions
5.20.090: Nuisance; Declaration
5.20.100: Nuisance Abatement
5.20.110: Penalty
5.20.120: Suspension, Revocation Of Registration
5.20.010: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter shall be to protect the health, safety and welfare
of residents of the city of Shoshone and to protect its citizens by means of
registration of vendors, peddlers, solicitors, and temporary merchants. (Ord.
535, 12-18-2012)
5.20.020: DEFINITIONS:
CITY CLERK: The licensing officer.
HAWKER: Each and every person or persons, corporation, copartnership, or
association or agent of such person or persons, corporation, copartnership, or
association, who offers any article for sale from a stand, wagon, truck, or
automobile or upon any street, public or open ground or private ground or
enclosure within the limits of the city.
MOBILE FOOD CONCESSIONS: Carts or like devices from which food and beverages
are sold which are designated to be moved and designed to be propelled by human
power.
NONMOBILE FOOD CONCESSIONS: Stands from which food and beverages are sold that
are not designed to be moved during operation. Includes semipermanent
structures open seasonally and permanent structures.
PEDDLER: Any person, whether a resident of the city or not, traveling by foot,
motor vehicle or any other type of conveyance, however propelled, drawn, pushed
or moved, from place to place, from house to house or from street to street,
carrying, conveying or transporting goods, wares, merchandise, food or farm
products or provisions, offering and exposing the same for sale or making sales
and delivering articles to purchasers, or who, without traveling from place to
place shall sell or offer the same for sale from a wagon, vehicle, railroad
car, or any other type of conveyance. The word "peddler" shall include the
words "hauler" and "hucksters".
PUBLIC SAFETY OFFICER: Licensing officer, code enforcement personnel, fireman
and police officer.
SOLICITOR: An individual, including an employee or agent of a group of
individuals, partnership, or corporation, whether a resident of the city or
not, who is taking or attempting to take, whether in person or by telephone,
orders for sale of food, beverages, goods, merchandise or services to be
furnished or performed in the future, whether he is collecting advance payments
on such sales or not. Such definitions shall include any person who, for
himself or for another person, hires, leases, uses or occupies any building,
structure, or motor vehicle within the city for the sole purpose of exhibiting
samples and taking orders for future delivery.
SPECIAL EVENT: The temporary use, with a valid permit, of public property,
including streets, beaches, parks, community centers and waterways, for the
purpose of conducting certain short term events such as art shows, music
concerts, fundraising events, sidewalk sales, amusement attractions, circuses,
carnivals, rodeos, swap meets, sporting events, including, but not limited to,
organized float trips, contests, street dances, tournaments, walk-a-thons,
marathons, races, exhibitions or related activities.
TEMPORARY: Six (6) months or less.
TEMPORARY MERCHANT: Any person whether owner or otherwise, whether a resident
of the city or not, who engages in a temporary business of selling and
delivering goods, wares, merchandise and services within the city.
VENDOR STANDS: A nonpermanent, immobile structure, booth, stall, counter or the
like operated by a vendor standing on or within the frame of the structure,
booth, stall, counter or the like. Goods sold from a stand may include, but are
not limited to, perishable and nonperishable food items, merchandise, and
sundries. (Ord. 535, 2012)
5.20.030: REGISTRATIONS REQUIRED:
It shall be unlawful for any vendor, solicitor or temporary merchant to engage
in such business or to employ another in such business within the corporate
limits of the city without first obtaining a registration from the city clerk's
office therefor in compliance with the provisions of this chapter. (Ord. 544,
2013)
5.20.040: EXCEPTIONS:
The provisions of this chapter shall not apply to:
   A.   The sale of farm or garden products grown within Lincoln County;
   B.   The sale of newspaper subscriptions in which the seller is a person
engaged in both the delivery and sale of the newspaper;
   C.   The occasional sale of admission by local school students to a function
of their school; or fundraising sales by local service clubs or groups such as
Elks, Kiwanis, Lions, Boy or Girl Scouts;
   D.   Any political group seeking funds or membership;
   E.   Garage, yard, or similar sales by individuals at their residence or
place of business not exceeding two (2) separate sales in one calendar year,
not to exceed three (3) days each, which sales shall not include business
inventory or items that have been purchased for the purpose of resale at
another garage sale;
   F.   Farmers' market. (Ord. 535, 2012)
5.20.050: APPLICATION FOR REGISTRATION:
Applicants for a registration under this chapter must file with the city clerk
an application furnished by the city clerk, which shall contain, but not
necessarily be limited to, the following information:
   A.   Name and description of the applicant; if the applicant is an
association, company or corporation, then it shall state its name along with
the names and descriptions of the persons who will be soliciting in the city;
   B.   Address - both legal and local;
   C.   A brief description of the nature of the business and the goods to be
sold, and in the case of products of farm or orchard, whether produced or grown
by the applicant;
   D.   If employed, the name and address of the employer, together with
credentials establishing the exact relationship between the employer and the
applicant;
   E.   The proposed method of operation, length of time for which the right to
do business is desired and if a motor vehicle is to be used, a description of
the same, together with a registration number or other means of identification;
   F.   Whether a permit or registration issued to the applicant has been
revoked during the past five (5) years, and if so, where and when;
   G.   Social security and/or driver's registration number, or FEIN of
applicant;
   H.   A statement as to whether or not the applicant has been convicted of a
violation of any federal, state or municipal law, the nature of the offense and
the date, and the punishment or penalty assessed therefor;
   I.   The place where the goods or property proposed to be sold, or orders
taken for the sale thereof, are manufactured or produced, where such goods or
products are located at the time said application is filed, and the proposed
method of delivery;
   J.   When the applicant proposes to peddle any prepared food product for
human consumption, a certification by South Central district health department
shall be required prior to issuance of a registration;
   K.   No registration issued hereunder shall be transferable. (Ord. 535,
2012)
5.20.060: REGISTRATION FEES:
The registration fee for any vendors, peddlers, hawkers, and/or temporary
merchants in one location within the boundaries of the city of Shoshone shall
be twenty five dollars ($25.00) per day for mobile food vendors, the fees will
be seventeen dollars ($17.00) per month for a business license, and thirteen
dollars ($13.00) per month for garbage service. Future fees and changes to fees
pertaining to this section will be set by resolution. (Ord. 538, 2013)
5.20.070: REGISTRATION ISSUANCE AND EXHIBITION:
   A.   No registration issued for the purpose designated in this chapter shall
be issued unless the amount required for the registration has first been paid
to the city clerk and until a registration permitting such sale has been issued
by the city clerk.
   B.   Such registration shall show the name, address, the type of
registration issued, and the kind of goods to be sold or type of sales to be
solicited thereunder, the amount of fee paid, the date of issuance and the date
of expiration.
   C.   The registration issued to the register hereunder by the city clerk
shall be exhibited in a conspicuous place if the register is using a vehicle or
a building in his business, and otherwise must be displayed on the outside
garment of the individual during hours of operation. (Ord. 535, 2012)
5.20.080: RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Location: No register hereunder shall have any exclusive right to any
location in a public street, nor shall he/she be permitted to operate in any
congested area where his operations might impede or inconvenience the public.
For the purpose of this chapter, the judgment of a public safety officer,
exercised in good faith, shall be deemed conclusive as to whether the area is
congested or the public impeded or inconvenienced. No business activity shall
be carried on in any area of the city by any register that is not registered
pursuant to this chapter, where such business activity is prohibited by the
city of Shoshone zoning ordinance. This registration does not preclude the
issuance of other permits by the parks department in public parks or the
granting of permission to sell and/or operate on private property by its
owners.
   B.   Hours Of Operation: Vendors, canvassers, solicitors shall be allowed to
engage in their registered business only between nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. and
nine thirty o'clock (9:30) P.M. unless located in a commercially zoned area.
All vending stands, carts or vehicles must be removed from public property
during nonvending hours. For special events, the city may make an exception to
the usual hours of operation.
   C.   Removal Of Trash: All trash or debris accumulating within twenty feet
(20') of any vending stand shall be collected by the vendor and deposited in
trash containers. All vendors selling food or beverages must provide trash
receptacles adjacent to or as a part of their stands.
   D.   Prohibited Areas: Any duly authorized public safety officer shall
prohibit vendors from selling on specified public ways if he determines such
prohibitions are necessary for the protection of public health and safety.
Vendor carts, stands, and motor vehicles are prohibited within fifteen feet
(15') of a fire hydrant, fire escape, bus stop, loading zone, or driveway of a
fire station, police station, or hospital.
   E.   Written Approval: All vendors and temporary merchants must receive
written approval from the Shoshone city planning and zoning commission for the
proposed site, design and signage pursuant to the conditions herein prior to
submittal of their application.
   F.   Additional Regulations For Vendors And Temporary Merchants: In
addition, the following criteria shall apply to all vendors and temporary
merchants:
      1.   A stand, cart, mobile food concession, or nonmobile food concession
must be designed and built meeting normal building industry standards, used in
a safe manner, and meet all requirements of the South Central district health
department as may be necessary.
      2.   A stand, cart, mobile food concession, or nonmobile food concession
shall not exceed sixty four (64) gross square feet in size and no more than
twelve feet (12') in height.
      3.   Support equipment and accessories, other than a generator, must not
extend more than two feet (2') from the edge of the stand, cart, mobile food
concession, or nonmobile food concession in any direction and shall not be
placed so as to impede pedestrian or vehicle traffic. Canopies or other covers,
whether stand alone or used on a stand, cart, mobile food concession, or
nonmobile food concession, must be securely fastened. Such covers shall have a
minimum vertical clearance of eight feet (8') and must not extend more than
four feet (4') from the edge of the stand, mobile food concession, or nonmobile
food concession in any direction.
      4.   A stand, cart, mobile food concession, or nonmobile food concession
shall maintain a clear pedestrian passage on the public sidewalk of no less
than five feet (5') wide; shall not block any vehicle travelway; shall not be
positioned within a driveway or within ten feet (10') of either side of the
driveway; shall not be positioned within a doorway or within five feet (5') of
either side of the doorway; nor in a manner that impedes movement or visually
obstructs pedestrians and vehicles using the public rights of way.
      5.   Stands, carts, mobile food concessions, and nonmobile food
concessions shall not be locked or chained to a tree, streetlight, or other
street furnishings.
      6.   Stands, carts, mobile food concessions, support equipment, canopies
or covers, and nonmobile food concessions shall be designed to be aesthetically
pleasing and maintained to have a neat and clean appearance at all times.
      7.   A stand, or nonmobile food concession may be permitted to have
tables and chairs and umbrellas provided they are contained within a twenty
foot (20') radius of the main service window. All tables and chairs and
accessories shall be stored either within the stand or nonmobile food
concession or off site during nonbusiness hours.
      8.   Overhead utility service connections are not permitted. Electrical
lines are not allowed overhead or lying in the pedestrian portion of the
sidewalk, in a vehicle travelway or parking lot, or within any landscaping.
City streetlight facilities shall not be used in any way to supply electrical
service to a vendor site.
      9.   Vendors must provide trash receptacles and waste removal adjacent to
or as a part of their operations. All spilled food, beverages, grease, or other
trash or debris resulting from the operation of any stand, cart, mobile food
concession, or nonmobile food concession shall be cleaned and collected by the
vendor and deposited in the vendor's trash receptacle. The vendor is prohibited
from depositing waste, ice, and any gray or waste water into sidewalk waste
receptacles, privately owned dumpsters, city planters, parking lot drains or
the street drainage system.
      10.   Stands, carts, mobile food concessions, and nonmobile food
concessions shall be maintained in such a manner that prevents the spilling or
splattering of grease, water, food, or trash on any ground where the cart,
trailer, or vehicle is located. The stand, mobile food concession, or nonmobile
food concession owner shall be responsible for the cleaning and repair of any
ground soiled, stained, or damaged by the placement and operation of their
business. (Ord. 546, 2013: Ord. 544, 2013: Ord. 535, 2012)
5.20.090: NUISANCE; DECLARATION:
The practice of going in and upon private residence property or properties in
the city by peddlers, solicitors, hawkers, temporary merchants, and transient
vendors of merchandise not having been requested to do so by the owner or
owners, occupant or occupants of the private residence property or properties
for the purpose of soliciting orders for the sale of goods, wares, and
merchandise or for the purpose of taking orders for subscriptions for
newspapers and magazines or for the purpose of disposing of or peddling or
hawking the same is a nuisance and punishable as such nuisance as an offense as
set forth in section
5.20.110 of this chapter. (Ord. 544, 2013)
5.20.100: NUISANCE ABATEMENT:
The chief of police of the city is required and directed to suppress all such
nuisances and to abate any such nuisances as described in section
5.20.090 of this chapter. (Ord. 535, 2012)
5.20.110: PENALTY:
Any person, business, firm, company or corporation who shall violate any of the
provisions of this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction
shall be punished by a fine not to exceed three hundred dollars ($300.00), or
by imprisonment in the county jail for a period not to exceed thirty (30) days
or both such fine and imprisonment. Each day a violation continues shall be a
separate offense, punishable as hereinabove described. (Ord. 535, 2012)
5.20.120: SUSPENSION, REVOCATION OF REGISTRATION:
   A.   Cause For Suspension Or Revocation: The city council may suspend or
revoke any registration for fraud and misrepresentation in its procurement, for
violations of this chapter, or for any conduct or act of the register or their
employees or any conduct or act permitted by them on the premises where such
business is conducted, or in connection therewith or adjacent thereto, tending
to render such business or such premises where the same is conducted as a
public nuisance or a menace to the health, peace, safety or general welfare of
the city, or in the event of the conviction of a registered vendor, solicitor,
or temporary merchant under the provisions of any city or county ordinance, or
of any law of the state or of the United States, regulating, governing, or
prohibiting the activities regulated under this chapter.
   B.   Registration Revocation: The city council shall proceed in accordance
with the notice and hearing provisions of title 67, chapter 52, Idaho Code, in
considering the revocation of a registration pursuant to subsection A of this
section. The city council shall cause to be kept minutes and make a transcribed
verbatim record of any revocation proceeding. If a registration is revoked, the
city council shall keep the transcribed verbatim record of the proceeding for a
period of not less than six (6) months after a written decision on the matter
is transmitted to the register.
   C.   Judicial Review: An applicant or register aggrieved by a decision of
the city council may, within sixty (60) days, seek judicial review under the
procedures provided in sections 67-5270 and 67-5271, Idaho Code. (Ord. 535,
2012)
CHAPTER 5.25
DEBT TO CITY
SECTION:
5.25.010: Debt To City Prohibited
5.25.020: Payment
5.25.010: DEBT TO CITY PROHIBITED:
It is the policy and intent of the mayor and city council to require by this
chapter that no business license will be issued when the applicant owes any
debt to the city. Business license includes, but is not limited to, business
license, beer license or liquor license. Debt to the city includes, but is not
limited to, water bills, sewer bills and garbage bills. (Ord. 545, 2013)
5.25.020: PAYMENT:
Payment for any license must be in the form of cash, money order or cashier's
check. Payment may be made only during normal business hours at the Shoshone
City Hall on business days. (Ord. 431, 1995)
TITLE 6
ANIMALS
Dogs   6.04
Animal Regulations   6.08
Fowl   6.12
CHAPTER 6.04
DOGS
SECTION:
6.04.010: Purpose
6.04.020: Definitions
6.04.030: License And Registration
6.04.040: Kennel Regulations
6.04.050: Running At Large Prohibited And Penalty
6.04.060: Provisions Regulating Suspected Or Actual Rabid Animals
6.04.070: Police Department And Poundmaster
6.04.080: Vicious Or Dangerous Dogs
6.04.090: Impounded Animals
6.04.100: Violations And Penalties
6.04.010: PURPOSE:
   A.   The purpose of this chapter is to promote public health, safety, and
general welfare and to minimize public and private losses due to dogs at large,
vicious dogs, and/or unlicensed dogs:
      1.   Protect human life, health, and property;
      2.   And to provide particularized standards for the keeping of dogs in
the limits of the City of Shoshone. (Ord. 559, 2019)
6.04.020: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, terms are defined as follows:
COMMERCIAL DOG KENNEL: A kennel where dogs are bred and/or raised specifically
for sale to the public.
DOG: Any male, female, spayed female or neutered male dog of any age.
DOG AT LARGE: Any dog which is not confined within a fenced or completely
enclosed area or on a chain or leash.
DOG KENNEL: A premises where more than three (3) dogs over the age of six (6)
months are raised, kept, housed or boarded at any point in time.
DOG OF LICENSING AGE: Any dog which has attained the age of six (6) months.
IMPOUNDED: Having been received into the custody of the poundmaster/pound or
into the custody of the Police Department or any authorized agent or
representative thereof.
OWNER: Any person or persons, firm, association or corporation owning, keeping
or harboring a dog.
POUND: An animal shelter, lot, premises or building maintained by the City for
the confinement and care of dogs seized either under the provisions of this
chapter or otherwise.
POUNDMASTER: A person, persons, or entity designated by the City for the
confinement and care of dogs seized under the provisions of this chapter.
UNLICENSED DOG: A dog for which the license for the current year has not been
paid, or to which the tag provided for in this chapter is not attached.
VICIOUS DOG: A dog that has bitten, clawed or otherwise harmed, or constitutes
a physical threat, to persons, other animals, and/or property or a dog who
endangers or menaces any person, property, or other animal without provocation
by such person or animal. (Ord. 559, 2019)
6.04.030: LICENSE AND REGISTRATION:
   A.   License And Registration Required: Every dog that has reached the age
of six (6) months or older, kept, harbored or maintained by any person in the
City, shall be licensed and registered. Dog licenses shall be issued by the
City Clerk upon payment of a license fee as herein provided in this chapter.
Payment of the license fee shall be made to the City Clerk at the City Hall
during regular business hours. A violation of this section shall be an
infraction punished by a fine of one hundred dollars ($100.00).
   B.   Licensing Requirements; Fees:
      1.   The owner, possessor or keeper of any dog six (6) months of age or
over shall make application for and obtain a license and registration tag for
such dog.
      2.   At the time of making application the owner, possessor or keeper of
any dog shall:
         a.   State his name and address and the sex, breed and color of each
dog owned or kept by him.
         b.   Pay a license fee for each dog licensed. The fee for licenses is
the sum of five dollars ($5.00) for each and every neutered male dog and every
spayed female dog, and the sum of ten dollars ($10.00) for every unspayed
female dog and unneutered male dog. Proof of the dog having been spayed or
neutered must be presented before issuance of the license.
         c.   Provide proof of a current rabies vaccination for the animal
being licensed.
         d.   All licenses are for one year and shall expire on April 1 of each
year and no notices will be sent by the City concerning expiration of licenses.
   C.   License Exemptions: The following dogs need not be licensed:
      1.   Any dog not yet six (6) months of age.
      2.   Any dog whose owner, keeper or possessor is a nonresident of the
City and who is temporarily within the City for thirty (30) days or less.
      3.   Any dog which has been duly or properly trained to assist the blind,
physically or mentally disabled and is acting in that capacity shall be
licensed without fee.
   D.   Owner's Certificate; Dog Collar And Tag: Upon payment of the license
fee, the City Clerk shall issue to the owner a certificate and a metallic tag
for each dog so licensed. The tag shall have stamped thereon the words
"Shoshone dog tag" and the license number corresponding with the tag number of
the certificate. Every owner shall be required to provide each dog with a
collar and tag which are constantly worn by the dog.
   E.   Dog Tags:
      1.   Duplicate dog tags shall be issued upon payment of one dollar
($1.00) for each tag so issued to replace the original tag that was lost or
destroyed.
      2.   Dog tags shall not be transferable from one dog to another and no
refunds shall be made on any dog license fee for any reason whatsoever.
      3.   The original receipt shall be retained by the owner or harborer of
the licensed dog for inspection by the Police Department or agent thereof.
(Ord. 559, 2019)
6.04.040: KENNEL REGULATIONS:
   A.   Kennel Regulations:
      1.   Kennel Fees: Any person conducting, operating or maintaining a
"commercial dog kennel" or "dog kennel" as herein defined shall pay to the City
Clerk's Office, for the privilege of conducting, operating or maintaining such
dog kennel, an annual license fee of one hundred dollars ($100.00). All license
fees are renewable each year on the anniversary date of issuance.
      2.   Qualifications For Issuance Of Dog Kennel License:
         a.   The City Clerk may issue a kennel license only after receiving a
positive recommendation from the Police Department and/or an agent thereof who
has made a personal investigation into each application including an on site
visit to the kennel area. The Clerk must also receive the proper fee amount. No
license may be issued until the police have certified to the City Clerk that
all requirements of this chapter have been complied with. The City Clerk may
deny the issuance of a license if fraudulent or untrue representations have
been made by the applicant, or if the applicant is in violation of any of the
provisions of this chapter. All licenses that are issued based upon fraudulent
statements are null and void as if they had never been issued.
         b.   At least fifteen (15) days before applying for a license the
applicant shall circulate a petition among all households located within three
hundred feet (300') of any part of the applicant's property. The petition shall
state the number and types of dogs the applicant wishes to keep and shall give
the legal location of the property on which the applicant wishes to keep the
dogs. The applicant must obtain the written approval of seventy five percent
(75%) of the homeowners located within three hundred feet (300') of his
property before a kennel license application may be considered.
         c.   Prior to the license issuance hearing police must inspect places
and premises in the City where any dogs are to be housed under the license
applied for and, if a violation of this chapter is found to exist, the police
shall not recommend to the City Clerk that a license be issued. Kennel licenses
shall expire after every year from the date of issuance and may be reissued by
the City Clerk upon written certification by the police that the kennel
operator has complied with the kennel rules and conditions contained in this
chapter for the entire preceding year.
      3.   Revocation Of License:
         a.   The City police may recommend to the City Clerk the revocation of
any kennel license upon evidence that any of the conditions set forth in this
chapter as a prerequisite to the issuance of a license have been violated, or
that the license was issued upon fraudulent or untrue representations by
applicant, or seventy five percent (75%) of the homeowners located within three
hundred feet (300') of the property of the kennel location, file a petition for
such revocation, or that the person holding the license has violated any of the
material provisions of this chapter.
         b.   All places and premises upon which any of the dogs are kept or
housed shall be open at all reasonable times for inspection by the City police.
If, upon inspection, there is found to exist any violation of any provision of
this chapter, the police shall give the person responsible for such violation a
written notice specifying the violation in particular and requiring such
offender to abate or correct such problem within the following twenty four (24)
hour period. If not abated or corrected, the police shall recommend to the City
Council that the license of such person be revoked.
         c.   The City Clerk may revoke any kennel license issued under this
chapter for violation of any of the provisions of this chapter or ordinance of
the City or laws of the State of Idaho. Prior to revocation by the Clerk, the
Clerk shall notify the applicant in writing, setting forth specifically the
grounds for the complaint and the time and place of the hearing. Such notice
shall be personally served upon the licensee, or mailed certified mail return
receipt requested to the licensee at his/her last known address at least ten
(10) days prior to the date set for the hearing. The notice should set out
appeal rights as outlined below.
         d.   The aggrieved person may file a request for appeal with the City
Council by submitting a written request for a hearing with the City Clerk in
person at the City Hall or by mailing a written request by first class mail to
the City Clerk at the City Hall. Said request must be received within fifteen
(15) days of the Clerk's denial. The Clerk shall schedule a hearing as part of
the next regular City Council meeting. The Mayor shall chair the hearing and
the City shall be represented by the City Attorney. The appellant may be
represented by an attorney of choice or by the appellant personally. The rules
for administrative hearings under Idaho shall be followed. The decision shall
be made by the Council in the same manner as it makes all other decisions with
the Mayor having the tiebreaking vote. The order of the City Council shall be
final, however appeal rights to the District Court may exist.
      4.   Penalty: A violation of this section shall be punished as a
misdemeanor with a maximum penalty of one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) and six
(6) months of jail. (Ord. 559, 2019)
6.04.050: RUNNING AT LARGE PROHIBITED AND PENALTY:
   A.   Running At Large:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any owner or keeper of any licensed or
unlicensed dog to permit such dog at any time to run at large within the City
limits.
      2.   Any person violating this section shall be served with a citation
signed by a police officer, or citizen.
         a.   The penalty for conviction is as follows:
            (1)   The first violation: Fifty dollars ($50.00) plus court costs;
            (2)   The second violation committed, within twelve (12)
consecutive months of the date that the first violation was committed: One
hundred dollars ($100.00) plus court costs;
            (3)   The third and all subsequent violations within twelve (12)
consecutive months of the first and second violations shall be a misdemeanor
and shall upon conviction be fined not more than three hundred dollars
($300.00) or imprisoned in the County Jail for a period of not more than six
(6) months, or by both fine and imprisonment.
         b.   It shall not be required that the subsequent violations be with
the same animal. (Ord. 559, 2019)
6.04.060: PROVISIONS REGULATING SUSPECTED OR ACTUAL RABID ANIMALS:
   A.   Reports Required: Anyone having knowledge of the animal known to have
or suspected of having rabies shall report the fact immediately to the Police
Department. The Police Department shall likewise be notified of any person or
animal bitten by a rabid or suspected rabid animal. It shall be the duty of all
physicians who treat any person bitten, while within the City limits, by any
animal to report immediately the name and address of such person to the Police
Department.
   B.   Quarantine Of Animal: It is hereby made the duty of the owner of a dog
or other animal showing symptoms of rabies or which has bitten or otherwise
attacked any person causing an abrasion of the skin, to surrender the dog or
animal for confinement at the City Pound or a veterinarian hospital for a
period not less than ten (10) days. Any dog or animal showing the symptoms of
rabies or which has bitten or otherwise attacked any person causing an abrasion
of the skin shall be placed in confinement as provided in this section. Any
animal of a species subject to rabies shall in like circumstances be confined
as herein provided. If a dog or other animal is determined to be free of
rabies, the dog or animal shall be returned to the owner upon payment of the
regular impoundment fee and board as provided in this chapter. If such fee is
not paid, the dog or animal shall be subject to disposal as provided by this
chapter. At the discretion of the City police, the quarantine of a dog or
animal may be upon the premises of the owner or the person in charge of the
same if securely confined, kept from contact with other animals and submitted
to a veterinarian for examination at the owner's expense to determine if rabid.
If an animal dies or has been killed, its head shall be removed and immediately
taken to the State Health Laboratory to be examined for rabies.
No person shall fail, refuse or neglect to allow the City police and/or an
agent of the City police to make an inspection or examination at any time
during this period. No dog or animal shall be removed from the place of
quarantine without written permission of the Chief of Police.
   C.   Contact With Rabid Animal: Any animal of a species subject to rabies
which has been bitten by a known rabid animal or has been in intimate contact
with a rabid animal shall be isolated in a suitable place approved by the
Police Department for a period of one hundred twenty (120) days or destroyed.
   D.   Violation: A violation of this section shall be punished as a
misdemeanor with a maximum penalty of one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) and six
(6) months of jail. (Ord. 559, 2019)
6.04.070: POLICE DEPARTMENT AND POUNDMASTER:
   A.   Police Department Duties: It shall be the duty of the Police
Department:
      1.   To carry out and enforce all the provisions of this chapter, and any
amendments hereto, any other ordinance later enacted relating to dogs and as
permitted by law.
      2.   To enforce the licensing and the control of all dogs in the City as
herein provided.
      3.   To file complaints and/or issue citations in a court of competent
jurisdiction against any person failing to license any dog as herein provided,
or who otherwise fails to comply with any of the provisions of this chapter.
      4.   To capture and secure all dogs found running at large contrary to
the provisions of this chapter and to remove such dogs in a humane manner to
the pound.
      5.   To pick up, collect the destruction fee and secure the euthanasia
record for all dogs to be destroyed at the owner's request.
      6.   To be responsible for posting notices concerning impounded dogs as
herein provided.
   B.   Rights Of Police Department Regarding Dogs:
      1.   Any dog found running at large or dog that is to be impounded,
which, in the opinion of any police officer cannot be safely taken without
tranquilizing, may be tranquilized for the purpose of impounding, by any police
officer.
      2.   In the enforcement of any provisions of this chapter, any police
officer and assistants are authorized to enter the premises of any person to
take possession of licensed or unlicensed, fierce, dangerous or vicious dogs
when in fresh pursuit of such dog at the time the dog goes onto private
property.
   C.   Poundmaster Duties: It shall be the duty of the poundmaster to hold all
dogs delivered by the Police Department and to provide suitable bedding, food
and water for such dogs for the period impounded. (Ord. 559, 2019)
6.04.080: VICIOUS OR DANGEROUS DOGS:
Any dog, defined as vicious by this chapter, the Chief of Police may order that
the violators post a bond or certificate of insurance in the amount of one
hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) or more and/or that the owner of the dog
prove financial responsibility for the dog's actions.
In any case where a person has been charged or cited with the offense of owning
or having custody of a vicious or dangerous dog or other animal pursuant to the
provisions of this chapter, the City Attorney may file a motion requesting
destruction of the animal prior to a final adjudication of the criminal
charges. The animal shall remain confined at the animal shelter pending a final
decision on the motion. The court may order the destruction of the animal upon
making a finding that the animal is "vicious", as defined in this chapter, and
that it poses a danger to the public if allowed to be released from
confinement. (Ord. 559, 2019)
6.04.090: IMPOUNDED ANIMALS:
   A.   Unclaimed Impounded Animals: If the owner, harborer, or keeper of the
dog impounded can be ascertained, then notice shall be promptly given the
owner, harborer or keeper stating that unless the dog is reclaimed according to
this chapter within seventy two (72) hours after such notice, the dog will be
given to a local dog rescue group designated by resolution of the City Council.
   B.   Reclamation Of Impounded Animals: A dog may be reclaimed by payment of
an impounding fee and costs of keeping the animal until it is reclaimed as
follows: For the first occurrence during the license year, a City impound fee
of fifteen dollars ($15.00), plus costs. For each subsequent impoundment during
the license year the City impound fee shall increase by five dollars ($5.00)
over the first fee paid for such dog, plus cost of keeping. Persons reclaiming
an unlicensed dog must purchase the required license in addition to all other
charges. The fees under this section shall be collected by the City Clerk and
costs paid to the persons/entity housing the animal. Receipt for all necessary
fees must be obtained from the City Clerk before an impounded dog can be
reclaimed. (Ord. 559, 2019)
6.04.100: VIOLATIONS AND PENALTIES:
   A.   Removing A Collar Or Tag: For any person to remove or cause to be
removed the collar or metallic tag from any licensed dog without the consent of
the owner. A violation of this subsection is an infraction punishable with a
one hundred dollar ($100.00) fine plus court costs.
   B.   Barking Dog: For any person to own, keep or harbor any dog which by
loud, continued or frequent barking, howling or yelping shall annoy or disturb
any neighborhood or person. This subsection shall not apply to the Municipal
dog pound or veterinary hospitals. A violation of this subsection is an
infraction punishable with a one hundred dollar ($100.00) fine plus court
costs. A subsequent violation and every violation thereafter within a 12-month
period shall be punishable as a misdemeanor with up to a three hundred dollar
($300.00) fine and six (6) months in jail.
   C.   Vicious Or Dangerous Dog: For any person to own, have custody of or
control of any dog or any other animal which is vicious or dangerous. A
violation of this subsection shall be punished as a misdemeanor with up to a
one thousand dollar ($1,000.00) fine and six (6) months in jail in addition to
the consequences as outlined above.
   D.   Failure To Exhibit Registration Or License: For any person keeping or
harboring a dog for which a license is required by this chapter to fail or to
refuse to exhibit the registration certificate or license tag upon demand by a
police officer. A violation of this subsection is an infraction punishable with
a one hundred dollar ($100.00) fine plus court costs.
   E.   Torture Or Mistreating Dogs: For any person to maltreat or torture any
dog or to willfully and maliciously administer or cause to be administered
poison of any sort whatsoever to any animal that is the property of another,
with the intent to injure or destroy such dog, or to willfully or maliciously
place any poison or poisoned food where the same is accessible to any such
animal. A violation of this subsection shall be punished as a misdemeanor with
up to a one thousand dollar ($1,000.00) fine and six (6) months in jail.
   F.   Hindering Or Delaying Police In Duties Pursuant To This Chapter: For
any person to hinder, delay, interfere with or obstruct a police officer while
said official is performing animal control duties and for any person to break
open or in any manner directly aid, counsel or advise the breaking open of any
dog pound or ambulance, wagon or vehicle used for the collecting or conveying
of dogs. A violation of this subsection shall be punished as a misdemeanor with
up to a one thousand dollar ($1,000.00) fine and six (6) months in jail.
   G.   Leaving A Dog In An Unattended Vehicle: For any person to leave or
confine in any unattended motor vehicle under conditions that may endanger the
health or well-being of an animal due to heat, cold, lack of adequate
ventilation, or lack of food or water, or under such other circumstances as
could reasonably be expected to cause suffering, disability, or death to the
animal. A violation of this subsection shall be punished as an infraction with
a one hundred dollar ($100.00) fine, plus court costs.
City police officers may use reasonable force under the above circumstances to
enter a vehicle and remove the animal after first making a reasonable attempt
to contact the animal's owner. The officer removing the animal shall use
reasonable means to contact the owner of the animal to arrange for its return
home. Absent contact with the owner, the animal will be taken to a veterinary
clinic if emergency care is needed and after a reasonable amount of time to an
animal shelter. (Ord. 559, 2019)
CHAPTER 6.08
ANIMAL REGULATIONS
SECTION:
6.08.010: Running At Large Prohibited
6.08.020: Impoundment; Authority
6.08.030: Impoundment; Repossession
6.08.040: Impoundment; Fees
6.08.050: Sale; Notice
6.08.060: Sale; Procedure
6.08.070: Sale; Proceeds; Redemption
6.08.080: Livestock Restrictions
6.08.090: Porcine Restrictions
6.08.100: Slaughtering Of Animals Prohibited
6.08.101: Definitions
6.08.102: Exceptions
6.08.103: Penalties
6.08.010: RUNNING AT LARGE PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful for any person or persons, or the agents or employees of such
person or persons to keep or maintain any cattle, horses, mules, jacks, sheep,
goats, hogs, poultry (more than five (5) hen chickens) or rabbits (more than
three (3) rabbits), or any other animals except dogs, cats or other animals
kept inside a residence or place of business at all times. No such stock shall
be driven through or upon any of the streets, alleys, or other public places
within the corporate limits of the city. No stock shall be kept within the city
limits overnight unless the stock is confined within a barn or enclosure. (Ord.
570, 2023: Prior code § 4-101)
6.08.020: IMPOUNDMENT; AUTHORITY:
It is the duty of city law enforcement to take up and impound any stock
mentioned in this chapter found in violation of any of its provisions. The city
law enforcement shall notify the owner or person entitled to the possession of
the stock, if known to him, and request such person to pay all reasonable
charges and take the stock away. (Ord. 570, 2023: Prior code § 4-102)
6.08.030: IMPOUNDMENT; REPOSSESSION:
If any owner or person entitled to possession of an animal appears before the
city law enforcement at any time prior to sale and makes out his right to such
animal or animals, he shall be entitled to the possession thereof upon payment
of all lawful charges which have incurred in relation to the same ; provided
that he need not pay for the keeping of the animals more than one day prior to
the posting of notices of sale. (Ord. 570, 2023: Prior code § 4-104)
6.08.040: IMPOUNDMENT; FEES:
It is lawful for city law enforcement to make the following charges authorized
by section
6.08.020 of this chapter and this section:
 
For taking up stock   $1.00 per head
For keeping stock     $10.00 per day
For posting 3 notices $1.50 per head
 
(Ord. 570, 2023: Prior code § 4-106)
6.08.050: SALE; NOTICE:
If at the expiration of twenty four (24) hours after the impounding of any such
animal as provided in section
6.08.020 of this chapter, the animal is not redeemed, it is the duty of the
city law enforcement to post three (3) notices in conspicuous places in the
city advertising the animals for sale and giving a thorough description of the
animal together with the time and place of sale, which time shall not be less
than seven (7) days from the day of posting the notices. (Ord. 570, 2023: Prior
code § 4-103)
6.08.060: SALE; PROCEDURE:
If any person entitled to possession of an animal or animals does not appear
and substantiate his title thereto prior to the time fixed in the notices for
the sale thereof, city law enforcement shall sell the animal or animals at
public auction. City law enforcement shall within five (5) days from the day of
making the sale deposit the proceeds thereof, after deducting all lawful
charges against the animal or animals, with the city treasurer and shall
furnish the city treasurer with an itemized statement of the charges against
the animal or animals. (Ord. 570, 2023: Prior code § 4-105)
6.08.070: SALE; PROCEEDS; REDEMPTION:
At any time within six (6) months after receiving the money by the city
treasurer, any person claiming to be the owner of the animal or animals may
recover the money from the treasurer upon proof to the city council that the
animal or animals were his property at the time the city law enforcement sold
the same. (Ord. 570, 2023: Prior code § 4-107)
6.08.080: LIVESTOCK RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Keeping Without Permit Unlawful:
      1.   Violation: It is unlawful, a violation of this chapter, and a
misdemeanor for any person, firm, corporation to keep or permit to be kept one
or more horses, cows, mules, ponies, sheep, goats, rabbits (more than three
(3)), hen chickens (more than two (2) or other four (4) footed animals, except
cats and licensed dogs upon premises owned or occupied by said person or
persons or upon any of the streets or alleys or other public grounds within the
corporate limits of the city without having a valid, unrevoked permit therefor.
Rooster chickens are prohibited.
      2.   To maintain or keep any animal except dogs and cats, fences
enclosing such animals must be so constructed so as to prevent the animals from
going upon the property of adjoining property owners in any manner whatsoever.
      3.   Permit Issuance: The city clerk, upon advice and consent of the city
council and subject to the restrictions hereinafter provided, may issue to a
person applying therefore a permit to keep one or more of the aforesaid animals
within the city limits. All permits so issued shall expire on March 31 in the
year next following the year of issue. Renewal of the permit shall be subject
to the conditions in existence at the time renewal is requested.
      4.   Permit Issuance Restrictions: A permit shall not be granted for
keeping any aforesaid four (4) footed animals within one hundred feet (100') of
a residence now in existence or which may hereafter be constructed other than
that occupied by permittee or owner.
      5.   Revocation Of Permit: Any permit issued shall be revoked by the city
council any time that the keeper of any four (4) footed animals:
         a.   Fails to confine the same upon his or her property;
         b.   Fails to keep the enclosure where the four (4) footed animal is
in a clean and sanitary condition in a manner that flies will not accumulate,
offensive odors emit or the premises upon which such animal or animals are kept
becomes offensive.
      6.   Offensive Defined: "Offensive" is defined as that condition which,
in the opinion of a majority of the residents living with in three hundred feet
(300') of the place where such four (4) footed animal, except cats and dogs, is
kept, is offensive to their senses.
      7.   Exceptions: The term "exception" is defined as that not needing a
permit. Exceptions are organized parades, county 4-H fair, county rodeo grounds
and Shoshone veterinary hospital. (Ord. 570, 2023: Ord. 371 §§ 1 – 7, 1985:
prior code § 4-111)
6.08.090: PORCINE RESTRICTIONS:
It is unlawful for any person or persons to keep, either on his own premises or
the premises of another, any hog or hogs, pig or pigs, shoat or shoats within
the limits of the city. (Prior code § 4-109)
6.08.100: SLAUGHTERING OF ANIMALS PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful and a violation of this chapter and a misdemeanor for any
person, firm, or corporation to slaughter or permit to be slaughtered any
animal within the city limits. (Ord. 448, 1997 1 )
 
Notes
1 1. This ordinance shall be effective June 17, 1997.
6.08.101: DEFINITIONS:
COMMERCIAL PROCESSOR: Any individual or company which specializes in the
slaughter and dressing of animals for business purposes. Commercial processor
shall include, but is not limited to, those individuals for business purposes
that operate, maintain a mobile butchering, or slaughter business.
DRESSING: The removal from the slaughtered animal of the internal organs and
body fluids.
RESIDUE: Internal organs, body fluid, and body parts.
SLAUGHTER, SLAUGHTERING, AND BUTCHERING: The killing, and/or dressing of
animals. (Ord. 448, 1997 1 )
 
Notes
1 2. This ordinance shall be effective June 17, 1997.
6.08.102: EXCEPTIONS:
   A.   Commercial meat processors shall be exempted from section
6.08.100 of this chapter provided that such processor is responsible for the
disposal of all slaughter residue of the animal in a safe, healthy manner. A
commercial processor shall not be exempt and shall be subject to the provisions
and penalties hereof in the event it fails to safely dispose of any slaughter
residue or in any way creates a public nuisance or health hazard.
   B.   Sections
6.08.100 through
6.08.103 of this chapter shall not regulate or prohibit the processing of wild
game by residential homeowners not for commercial purposes. (Ord. 448, 1997 3 )
 
Notes
3 3. This ordinance shall be effective June 17, 1997.
6.08.103: PENALTIES:
Any person, firm or corporation violating any provisions of this chapter shall,
upon conviction, be guilty of a misdemeanor and punishable by a fine of up to
three hundred dollars ($300.00) or one hundred eighty (180) days in jail or
both. (Ord. 448, 1997 1 )
 
Notes
1 4. This ordinance shall be effective June 17, 1997.
CHAPTER 6.12
FOWL
SECTION:
6.12.010: Intent
6.12.020: Definitions
6.12.030: Prohibited Acts
6.12.040: Excluded Birds
6.12.050: Penalty
6.12.060: Existing Permits
6.12.010: INTENT:
It is the intent of this chapter to prevent the possession, or attempted
possession, of birds which are not commonly considered as pets. (Ord. 503,
2006)
6.12.020: DEFINITIONS:
All definitions contained in this section come from "The Random House College
Dictionary Revised Edition", copyright 1984, by Random House, Inc.
BIRD: Any warm blooded vertebrate of the class Aves having a body covered with
feathers and forelimbs modified into wings.
COCKATIEL: Any of numerous crested parrots of the genera Cacatua, having
chiefly white plumage tinged with yellow, pink, or red.
COCKATOO: Small crested long tailed Australian parrot; of the genera Cacatua
galerita.
FINCHES: From the family Fringillidae; birds with a short conical bill adapted
for eating seeds; includes buntings, sparrows, crossbills, linnets, and
grosbeaks.
PARAKEETS: Small slender parrots usually having a long graduated tail and noted
for their ability to mimic human speech.
PARROT: Any of numerous hook billed, often brilliantly colored birds of the
order Psittaciformes, including the lory and the macaw, having the ability to
mimic speech.
POSSESS: The act of enclosing, controlling, containing, sheltering, and
restraining and/or otherwise preventing the leaving of one's property without
permission of the owner and/or renter of such property. (Ord. 503 § 2, 2006)
6.12.030: PROHIBITED ACTS:
It shall be unlawful for any person, persons, or business to possess or attempt
to possess any bird(s) within the boundaries of the city of Shoshone which is
not specifically included in section
6.12.020 of this chapter. Hen chickens as allowed in Chapter 6.08 are except
from this prohibition. (Ord. 570, 2023: Ord. 503 § 2, 2006)
6.12.040: EXCLUDED BIRDS:
   A.   This chapter specifically exempts the feeding/sheltering of any wild
bird.
   B.   This chapter specifically exempts any bird, the possession of which is
required to be licensed by state and/or federal statute, rule, and/or
regulation. (Ord. 503 § 2, 2006)
6.12.050: PENALTY:
Violation of this chapter is punishable by an infraction of fifty dollars
($50.00), plus court costs, per bird, per day. (Ord. 503 § 2, 2006)
6.12.060: EXISTING PERMITS:
Any birds currently allowed within the boundaries of the city of Shoshone by
license or permit shall be considered lawfully possessed until the ending date
of said license or permit. When said permit expires, and said bird or birds are
still alive, said bird(s) shall be immediately removed from within the
boundaries of the city of Shoshone. (Ord. 503 § 2, 2006)
