CHAPTER 8.04
GARBAGE
SECTION:
8.04.010: Deposits Prohibited
8.04.020: Privy Restrictions
8.04.030: Unsanitary Debris Prohibited
8.04.040: Drainage Restrictions
8.04.050: Water Pollution Prohibited
8.04.060: Container Requirements
8.04.061: Compulsory Municipal Garbage And Refuse Collection And Disposal
Service
8.04.062: Restrictions On Container Use
8.04.063: Storing Of Refuse
8.04.064: Construction Debris
8.04.070: Rates And Charges; Designated
8.04.080: Rates And Charges; Alteration
8.04.090: Rates And Charges; Payment
8.04.100: Rates And Charges; Unusual Amounts
8.04.110: Rates And Charges; Use
8.04.120: Rates And Charges; Responsibility
8.04.130: Penalties
8.04.010: DEPOSITS PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful to put, throw, dump, or unload any trash, manure, garbage,
scraps, slops, or rubbish of any description into the streets, ditches, or
alleys of the city or deposit the same into the waters or upon the banks of
Little Wood River within the limits of the city. (Prior code § 7-101)
8.04.020: PRIVY RESTRICTIONS:
It is unlawful for any person or persons to have or maintain any privy,
cesspool, sinkhole, or privy vault within a distance less than forty feet (40')
of the waters of Little Wood River. (Prior code § 7-102)
8.04.030: UNSANITARY DEBRIS PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful for any person or persons to permit garbage or refuse of any
kind, of a perishable or fermentive nature which may decay or cause a stench,
to remain within his or their yard or yards or upon his or their premises
within the city or to use or maintain any barn, stable, sink, cesspool,
outhouse, privy, or garbage, or scavenger box or barrel in any unsanitary
condition. (Prior code § 7-103)
8.04.040: DRAINAGE RESTRICTIONS:
It is unlawful for any person or persons to have or maintain any stable, barn,
hog pen, barnyard, or corral for the keeping or confining of hogs, cattle,
horses, mules, or sheep so that the drainage from the buildings or enclosures
passes into the waters of Little Wood River or that the livestock confined in
the buildings or enclosures shall in any manner pollute the waters of said
stream. (Prior code § 7-104)
8.04.050: WATER POLLUTION PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful for any person or persons to sweep or deposit anything
whatsoever into the water ditches or gutters of the city. (Prior code § 7-105)
8.04.060: CONTAINER REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   The city of Shoshone shall furnish one 65-gallon or 95-gallon container
to all residences. The city of Shoshone shall furnish containers to all
commercial properties equivalent to the number of dumpsters being removed. The
property owner accepting the container shall be responsible for its condition.
If it is damaged, abused or destroyed, the property owner who received the
container shall be required to replace and pay for another container. No other
type of container shall be used. Any residence or commercial properties needing
more containers or dumpsters than originally provided shall be charged for the
container and for the extra garbage disposal at the same rate as the charge for
the garbage disposal of the first container.
   B.   All containers are the responsibility of the property owner and any
damage, abuse, or destruction will require the owner to replace the container
at his or her own expense. (Ord. 469 § 2, 2000: Ord. 318, 1972: prior code § 7-
105-A)
8.04.061: COMPULSORY MUNICIPAL GARBAGE AND REFUSE COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL
SERVICE:
No person shall be permitted to refuse to accept the collection and disposal
service herein provided. (Ord. 469 § 3, 2000)
8.04.062: RESTRICTIONS ON CONTAINER USE:
   A.   Items that are too large to fit in a container, with the lid completely
shut, will not be accepted for collection.
   B.   Containers that exceed the manufacturer's maximum weight specifications
will not be accepted for collection.
   C.   Broken concrete, rocks, plaster, discarded building material, trees,
shrubs, flammable liquids, tires, and/or hazardous materials, shall not be
placed in a container.
   D.   A container that contains any of the items listed in subsection C of
this section will not be accepted for collection.
   E.   Cardboard boxes and containers shall be flattened to reduce volume
before being placed in a container. (Ord. 469 § 4, 2000)
8.04.063: STORING OF REFUSE:
   A.   No person shall place any garbage, rubbish or refuse in any street,
alley or other public place within the city limits unless the garbage, rubbish
or refuse is placed in the proper container for collection.
   B.   Any unauthorized accumulation of garbage, rubbish or refuse on any
premises is hereby declared to be a nuisance and is prohibited.
   C.   Failure to remove an existing accumulation of refuse within twenty four
(24) hours after notice from the city clerk and/or the city maintenance
supervisor shall be deemed a violation of this chapter.
   D.   The city may authorize storage of refuse on streets and alleys for city
clean up days. The city, by resolution, shall designate such places and times
where such accumulation is allowed. (Ord. 469 § 5, 2000)
8.04.064: CONSTRUCTION DEBRIS:
Debris resulting from the construction, reconstruction or repairs of premises
shall not be placed with other refuse for collection but shall be disposed of
directly by the person or persons owning, occupying, or leasing the premises.
(Ord. 469 § 6, 2000)
8.04.070: RATES AND CHARGES; DESIGNATED:
Each party within the city using city water shall pay an additional fee of one
dollar fifty cents ($1.50) per month for the use of the city garbage collecting
service; there shall be paid for each business the sum of three dollars ($3.00)
per month for such service, and for each apartment having two (2) or more
apartments there shall be paid the sum of three dollars ($3.00) per month for
such service. (Ord. 339 § 1, 1977)
8.04.080: RATES AND CHARGES; ALTERATION:
The city council may, in regular session as economic circumstances dictate,
alter or raise charges to a reasonable amount by resolution duly adopted. (Ord.
339 § 2, 1977)
8.04.090: RATES AND CHARGES; PAYMENT:
All fees shall be paid in advance from and after October 1, 1977, at the same
time and in the same manner that fees are paid for city water service. (Ord.
339 § 3, 1977)
8.04.100: RATES AND CHARGES; UNUSUAL AMOUNTS:
Should any user consistently have a larger amount of garbage than other users
in the same class, the city has the right to fix a larger fee based upon the
amount of garbage so disposed of by the city, and such fees shall be collected
as provided for other users. (Ord. 339 § 4, 1977)
8.04.110: RATES AND CHARGES; USE:
The funds collected for garbage service shall be used to pay for such service
and the equipment used therein, the repair of equipment and/or the purchase of
new equipment for garbage collection and/or disposal. (Ord. 339 § 5, 1977)
8.04.120: RATES AND CHARGES; RESPONSIBILITY:
The property owner shall be held responsible for the payment of all services
requested and/or used. All persons having water service shall be required to
pay the additional fees and if they are not paid, water service may be
discontinued to the customer; provided, however, when such charges appear to
the city council to be inequitable, the city may, by contract, provide a
different fee arrangement with the applicant who, in the opinion of the city
council, establishes such inequity. (Ord. 339 § 6, 1977)
8.04.130: PENALTIES:
Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall be deemed
guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall be fined in a sum not
to exceed three hundred dollars ($300.00) and may be confined in the county
jail for a period not more than six (6) months or any combination of such fine
and jail. (Ord. 469 § 7, 2000: Ord. 318, 1972: prior code § 7-106)
CHAPTER 8.08
WEEDS
SECTION:
8.08.010: Nuisance Declaration
8.08.020: Destruction; Cost Assessment
8.08.030: Destruction; By City
8.08.010: NUISANCE DECLARATION:
Whenever there is found in or on any lot or piece of ground including all
spaces within the curb line of the street adjoining such lot or piece of ground
within the corporate limits of the city any growth of weeds the same is a
nuisance and shall be removed or abated upon reasonable notice being given as
provided in this chapter. (Prior code § 7-201)
8.08.020: DESTRUCTION; COST ASSESSMENT:
   A.   The city council has power to give notice of abatement of any nuisance
mentioned and described in section 8.08.010 of this chapter in the following
manner: They shall prepare or cause to be prepared a written notice specifying
and describing the property upon which the growth of weeds is situated and
demanding that the weeds be cut or destroyed within a period of ten (10) days
from the date of the notice, then the city authorities will cause the same to
be done and that the costs and expenses thereof shall be assessed against the
property on which the nuisance existed and that the costs and expenses shall be
levied and collected as taxes.
   B.   The notice may be served in any one of the following manners: It may be
sent by registered mail to the owner or occupant of the premises at his last
known address or it may be given and served by posting the notice or copy
thereof upon the premises in question; provided, however, that the notices
shall be mailed to such parties or posted at least ten (10) days prior to the
time the city is authorized to abate the nuisance or nuisances. (Ord. 485,
2003: prior code § 7-202)
8.08.030: DESTRUCTION; BY CITY:
If, at the end of ten (10) days after notices have been given as provided in
section 8.08.020 of this chapter, the owner or occupant of the premises has
failed to cut or destroy the weeds or cause the nuisances to be abated, then
the city council or its agents may enter upon the premises and cut and destroy
the weeds and assess the costs against the property, which costs shall be
assessed and collected as taxes. (Prior code § 7-202)
CHAPTER 8.12
JUNK
SECTION:
8.12.010: Junk Defined
8.12.020: Deposit Prohibited
8.12.030: Nuisance Declaration And Abatement
8.12.010: JUNK DEFINED:
"Junk" is defined to be any used material or any parts of material units which
have become useless for the purpose for which the material was originally
fabricated or manufactured and includes, but is not limited to, automobiles not
licensed for the current year and any unsightly accumulation of garbage,
rubbish, or debris. (Ord. 287 § 2, 1968)
8.12.020: DEPOSIT PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful and a misdemeanor for any person to keep, or to permit to be
kept, or to place or cause to be placed, any junk upon premises owned or
occupied by him or upon any of the streets or alleys or other public grounds of
the city. (Ord. 287 § 1, 1968)
8.12.030: NUISANCE DECLARATION AND ABATEMENT:
The keeping by any person of junk on premises owned or occupied by him or the
placing thereof on streets, alleys, or public places is a nuisance. The city
may remove or abate such nuisance at the expense of the property upon which the
same exists after giving the owner thereof notice to remove the same within
fifteen (15) days from the date of the notice and the failure of the owner to
remove or cause to be removed the nuisance within the prescribed time and the
expense thereof to the city constitutes a lien upon the property and the amount
thereof may be certified to the proper officer of Lincoln County for collection
in the same manner as other taxes as provided by law. The city may at its
option institute a civil action for the removal of and the abatement of such
nuisance. (Ord. 287 § 3, 1968)
CHAPTER 8.16
NUISANCES
SECTION:
8.16.010: Definitions
8.16.020: Examples
8.16.030: Liability
8.16.040: Abatement By Property Owner
8.16.050: City Abatement Option
8.16.055: Violation Citation Option
8.16.060: Unlawful Burning
8.16.062: Yard Sale Exception
8.16.064: Yard Sale Definition
8.16.066: Personal Property Offered For Sale
8.16.070: Saving Clause
8.16.010: DEFINITIONS:
For the purposes of this chapter, the words set out in this section shall be
defined as follows:
NUISANCE: Anything which is injurious to the health, safety or welfare of
individuals, or is offensive to the senses of individuals, or is an obstruction
of the free use of property, so as to interfere with the comfortable enjoyment
of life or property.
PUBLIC NUISANCE: A nuisance which affects at the same time an entire community
or neighborhood, or any considerable number of persons, although the extent of
the annoyance or damage inflicted upon individuals may be unequal. (Ord. 445,
1996)
8.16.020: EXAMPLES:
Examples of public nuisances representing a serious hazard to the public
health, safety and welfare include, but are not limited to:
   A.   Deposits of any offensive, unwholesome, noxious or injurious substances
including paper, litter of any kind, garbage, trash, ashes, rubbish, debris,
carcasses, animal feces or any other waste material anywhere within the city;
   B.   Abandoned, unattended or discarded iceboxes, refrigerators or other
containers which have a door or lid, snap lock or other locking device which
may not be released from the inside, left outside of a building, dwelling or
other structure or within any unoccupied or abandoned building, dwelling or
other structure in a place accessible to children; the nuisance may be remedied
by removing the door or lid, snap lock or other locking device or by first
fastening, bolting or locking the same in a manner which would make the inside
inaccessible to children;
   C.   Accumulations of junk of any kind, including used merchandise, building
materials and automobile parts in any area unfenced and unscreened from public
view;
   D.   Junked, abandoned or partially dismantled vehicles, whether licensed or
unlicensed, in any area of the city, without permit, with the exception of
vehicles at commercial repair shops and wrecking yards in areas where such
operations are authorized under the zoning ordinance of the city;
   E.   Any building which is so dilapidated or in such condition as to menace
the public health or safety of persons or property; violations of various
building codes adopted by the city related to buildings shall be prima facie
evidence that a nuisance is being maintained on the property;
   F.   Burning rags, leather, hair or other substances of any kind which cause
or produce an offensive smell, smoke or odor which annoys or is offensive to
persons living in the vicinity or to persons passing on any public
thoroughfare;
   G.   Defecation or urination upon the streets, alleys, public places or
other places that may be seen from a private residence or by any person passing
on public thoroughfares;
   H.   Open or unprotected trap doors, cellars, or gratings, including those
adjacent to any sidewalk;
   I.   All yards, grounds, premises, cellars, unprotected foundations for
basements, vaults, drains, pools, cesspools, privies and sewers, which for any
cause have become foul, nauseous or injurious to the health, safety or welfare
of the citizens or which give forth odors which are offensive to the general
public, adjacent residents or persons passing on public thoroughfares;
   J.   Accumulations of stagnant or impure water, refuse, vegetable decay,
garbage, or filth of any kind in, or upon any yard, lot, place or premises or
upon any street or sidewalk adjacent to or abutting upon any lot, block, place
or premises or in any building or shed within the limits of the municipality,
so as to cause or create a nuisance or offensive smell or to pollute or render
unhealthful the atmosphere or the premises or thereby to be, become, cause or
create a public nuisance;
   K.   Parties, private gatherings, meetings and socials, whether indoors or
out of doors, held between the hours of eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. and six
o'clock (6:00) A.M., where music, laughter, conversation and other noises are
loud enough to disturb the neighbors, where the failure of participants to
respond to reasonable requests to reduce those noise levels shows a lack of
cooperation, or where destruction or disturbance of neighboring property by the
participants is occurring or has occurred, so as to indicate that the party,
private gathering, meeting, or social is an intentional harassment of the
surrounding neighborhood.
Special exceptions to this section for bona fide activities may be granted by
the mayor and city council through the chief of police; provided, that an
application in writing must be submitted sixteen (16) days prior to the event
applied for and that any resulting permit must be in written form and filed
with the chief of police before such activity may commence. The permit
application shall specifically state the hours, date, time and place for the
activity as well as the type of activity being conducted, names of the people
who are to be in charge of the activity and such other information. The
application, permit and guidelines are to be on a form which must be approved
by the Shoshone city attorney and which must be available at the Shoshone city
hall during all regular business hours. (Ord. 445, 1996)
8.16.030: LIABILITY:
It is unlawful for any person to create or maintain any nuisance, or cause the
same to exist, and for any person to knowingly permit a nuisance to be created,
maintained or to exist on premises owned by him or under his control. (Ord.
445, 1996)
8.16.040: ABATEMENT BY PROPERTY OWNER:
It shall be the duty of any owner of any lot, building or premises where any
nuisance exists to remove, abate or destroy the nuisance without delay. (Ord.
445, 1996)
8.16.050: CITY ABATEMENT OPTION:
Nuisances which remain unabated after notice, may, at the option of the city,
be removed, abated or destroyed by the city or its agents, after the following
steps have been taken:
   A.   If after seven (7) calendar days from the date a written notice is
personally delivered to the property owner, or mailed via first class mail,
postage prepaid, to the property owner, no abatement of the nuisance has
occurred, the mayor's designated enforcement officer shall provide a second ten
(10) day notice to be delivered to the property owner by certified mail or
personal service, which shall include the following:
      1.   If the property owner fails to abate the nuisance, the city shall
take steps to abate the same;
      2.   The property owner may contract with the city to abate the nuisance
and pay costs of the same;
      3.   If the city abates the nuisance, all costs and expenses of abatement
shall be billed and assessed against the property owner and if unpaid shall
become collectable as a special assessment with property taxes;
      4.   The property owner has a right to appear before the city council to
show cause as to why he or she should not be forced to abate or pay for
abatement of the nuisance; furthermore, that if the property owner desires such
a hearing, a request for hearing, in writing, shall be given to the city clerk
prior to expiration of the ten (10) day notice, and that abatement by the city
will proceed if the property owner has not exercised this option to request a
hearing;
      5.   If said certified notice is returned as undeliverable, or is
unclaimed by the property owner, nothing shall preclude the city from
exercising its abatement option as specified herein;
   B.   When the ten (10) day notice has expired without a request for hearing,
the mayor's designated enforcement officer is authorized to remove, abate or
destroy the nuisance. The mayor's designated enforcement officer is authorized
to utilize city personnel to abate the nuisance or to contact the mayor in
regard to contracting for an outside party to abate the nuisance;
   C.   If the city abates any nuisance under the provisions of this chapter, a
statement of charges billed to the property owner shall be mailed or personally
delivered to the property owner;
   D.   If the payment is not received from the property owner within thirty
(30) days, the amount billed shall, in accordance with state law, be assessed
as a special assessment collectible against the subject property as other
state, county and municipal taxes;
   E.   If the property owner requests a hearing to show cause before the city
council, the hearing shall, if feasible, be placed on the agenda of the next
regularly scheduled city council meeting. The decision of the city council
shall be final. A ten (10) day period shall be given the property owner after
the council decision so that the property owner shall have additional
opportunity to abate the nuisance or to pursue any legal remedies or defenses
at the district court level. (Ord. 486 § 1, 2003: Ord. 445, 1996)
8.16.055: VIOLATION CITATION OPTION:
The mayor's enforcement officer may issue, or cause to be issued, a violation
citation to any person who maintains, creates, causes to exist or allows the
maintenance, creation, or existence of any nuisance. The citation may be issued
concurrently with, or in addition to, any other procedures set out in this
section or any other law or ordinance application within the city limits. In
the event the person or persons maintaining, creating or causing the nuisance
is a guest or invitee of the resident landowner or leaseholder, then the
resident landowner or leaseholder may be cited for the nuisance caused by their
guests or invitees. In this event, the complaining party or parties shall not
be required to prove which guest or invitee caused or maintained the nuisance,
but must only prove that the person or persons causing or creating the nuisance
is a guest or invitee of the resident landowner or leaseholder. Landowners not
occupying or residing on/in the premises which is in violation of this chapter
shall be issued a warning citation prior to being issued a violation citation.
If the nuisance, which is the basis for the warning citation, is not abated by
the nonresident owner within five (5) business days, then a violation citation
may be issued. Upon an admission of guilt by alleged violating party or a
finding of guilt by a court of law, the bond or fine, respectively, for each
offense excluding court costs shall be as follows:
 
First offense                                                 $ 50.00
Second offense within 12 months of the first offense          75.00
Each subsequent offense within 12 months of the first offense 100.00
 
(Ord. 445, 1996)
8.16.060: UNLAWFUL BURNING:
It shall be unlawful for any person to suffer, cause, or permit any open
burning within the city of Shoshone except as allowed by a permit issued by the
Shoshone city and rural fire protection district. Fire burning permits are not
required for open fires used for the preparation of food. Fires for
recreational purposes must be under the control of a responsible person and
enclosed in a manner, form, and place, as approved by the Shoshone city and
rural fire protection district.
   A.   Permits: Permit shall be issued by the Shoshone city and rural fire
protection district if the proposed burning is in compliance with the Idaho
department of health and welfare regulations for air pollution, the
international fire code, and will not endanger life and/or property.
   B.   Hours: Open burning (with a permit) shall be allowed only from the
hours of six o'clock (6:00) A.M. to five o'clock (5:00) P.M.
   C.   Penalties: The penalties for violating this section are increased with
the frequency and time period. A violation of this section shall be an
infraction and punished as shown in the fine schedule below:
 
First offense                                                 $ 50.00
Second offense within 12 months of the first offense          75.00
Each subsequent offense within 12 months of the first offense 100.00
 
Each offense for which a person is found in violation shall include, in
addition to the fine listed above, any and all applicable court costs.
(Ord. 534, 12-18-2012)
8.16.062: YARD SALE EXCEPTION:
Nothing herein shall prohibit the owners and occupants of residential lots from
conducting or allowing to be conducted one yard sale during the period from
January 1 to June 30 and another during the period from July 1 to December 31
on said lots. (Ord. 445, 1996)
8.16.064: YARD SALE DEFINITION:
Accumulations of personal property on residential lots constitute yard sales,
and are therefore not nuisances as defined herein, if, and only if:
   A.   The personal property consists of surplus household property,
regardless of ownership;
   B.   The personal property is publicly offered for sale;
   C.   The personal property is neatly displayed for sale, either within or
without an enclosure;
   D.   The personal property is neatly secured within an enclosure during
those periods when it is not offered for sale;
   E.   The personal property is offered for sale over a period of not longer
than five (5) consecutive calendar days; and
   F.   No property salvaged from any garbage dump, refuse heap, sanitary
landfill or other disposal facility shall be included in the definition of
surplus personal property, or offered for sale in a yard as defined herein.
(Ord. 445, 1996)
8.16.066: PERSONAL PROPERTY OFFERED FOR SALE:
For the purposes of the exceptions to this chapter found in sections 8.16.062
and 8.16.064 of this chapter, personal property is offered for sale through any
method of informing or soliciting buyers of goods, including, but not limited
to, use of signs, handbills, newspaper advertisements, and direct personal
contacts. Nothing in section 8.16.062 or 8.16.064 of this chapter or this
section shall permit the littering of streets and alleys, or the posting of
signs on public property, telephone and electric poles, or private property
without permission. (Ord. 445, 1996)
8.16.070: SAVING CLAUSE:
If any section, paragraph, sentence or provision hereof or the application
thereof to any particular circumstances shall ever be held invalid or
unenforceable by a court of competent jurisdiction, such decision shall not
affect the remainder hereof, which shall continue in full force and effect and
applicable to all circumstances to which it may validly apply. (Ord. 445, 1996)
CHAPTER 8.20
NOISE
SECTION:
8.20.010: Short Title
8.20.020: Declaration Of Findings And Policy; Scope
8.20.030: Definitions
8.20.040: Powers And Duties Of The Shoshone City Council
8.20.041: Powers And Duties Of The Noise Control Officer (Shoshone Police Or
Any Other Law Enforcement Officer Of Lincoln County)
8.20.050: Duties And Responsibilities Of City Of Shoshone Departments
8.20.060: Prohibited Acts
8.20.070: Exceptions And Variances
8.20.080: Sound Levels By Receiving Land Use
8.20.090: Motor Vehicle Maximum Sound Levels
8.20.100: Enforcement
8.20.010: SHORT TITLE:
This chapter may be cited as the NOISE CONTROL ORDINANCE OF THE CITY OF
SHOSHONE, COUNTY OF LINCOLN, STATE OF IDAHO. (Ord. 526, 2011)
8.20.020: DECLARATION OF FINDINGS AND POLICY; SCOPE:
   A.   Declaration Of Findings And Policy: Whereas excessive sound and
vibration are a serious hazard to the public health and welfare, safety, and
quality of life; and whereas a substantial body of science and technology
exists by which excessive sound and vibration may be substantially abated; and,
whereas the people have a right to and should be ensured an environment free
from excessive sound and vibration that may jeopardize their health and welfare
or safety or degrade the quality of life; and now therefore, it is the policy
of the city of Shoshone, county of Lincoln, state of Idaho to prevent excessive
sound and vibration which may jeopardize the health and welfare or safety of
its citizens or degrade the quality of life.
   B.   Scope: This chapter shall apply to the control of all sound and
vibration originating within the geographical limits of the city of Shoshone.
(Ord. 526, 2011)
8.20.030: DEFINITIONS:
   A.   Terminology: All terminology used in this chapter not defined below,
shall be in conformance with applicable publications of the American National
Standards Institute (ANSI) or its successor body.
   A-WEIGHTED SOUND LEVEL: The sound pressure level in decibels measured on a
sound level meter using the A-weighting network. The level so read is
designated dB(A) or dBA.
   CITY COUNCIL: The city council of the city of Shoshone.
   COMMERCIAL AREA: All areas within the following zones as specified in the
city of Shoshone comprehensive plan: neighborhood business (NB), central
business district (CB), light commercial (C1), and heavy commercial (C2).
   CONSTRUCTION: Any site preparation, assembly, erection, substantial repair,
alteration, or similar action, but excluding demolition, for or of public or
private rights of way, structures, utilities or similar property.
   COUNTY: The county of Lincoln, state of Idaho.
   DECIBEL (dB): A unit for measuring the volume of a sound, equal to twenty
(20) times (the logarithm to the base-10 of the ratio of the pressure of sound
measured to the reference pressure, which is 20 micropascals [20 micronewtons
per square meter]).
   DEMOLITION: Any dismantling, intentional destruction or removal of
structures, utilities, public or private right of way surfaces, or similar
property.
   EMERGENCY: Any occurrence or set of circumstances involving actual or
imminent physical trauma or property damage that demands immediate action.
   EMERGENCY WORK: Any work performed for the purpose of preventing or
alleviating the physical trauma or property damage threatened or caused by an
emergency.
   EQUIVALENT A-WEIGHTED SOUND LEVEL (Leq): The constant sound level that in a
given situation and time period, conveys the same sound energy as the actual
time varying A-weighted sound. (For purposes of this chapter, a time period of
24 hours shall be used, unless otherwise specified.)
   IMPULSIVE SOUND: Sound of short duration, usually less than one second, with
an abrupt onset and rapid decay. Examples of sources of impulsive sound include
explosions, drop forge impacts, and the discharge of firearms.
   INDUSTRIAL AREA: All areas within the following zones as specified in the
city of Shoshone comprehensive plan: light manufacturing (M1), alternatively
described as light industrial; or heavy manufacturing (M2), alternatively
described as heavy industrial.
   MOTOR VEHICLE: As defined in the motor vehicle code of the state of Idaho.
(Any vehicle which is propelled or drawn on land by a motor, such as, but not
limited to, passenger cars, trucks, truck-trailers, semi-trailers, campers, go-
carts, off-road vehicles, amphibious craft on land, racing vehicles, or
motorcycles.)
   MOTORBOAT: Any vessel which operates on water and is propelled by a motor.
   MOTORCYCLE: As defined in the motor vehicle code of the state of Idaho. (An
unenclosed motor vehicle having a saddle for the use of the operator and two or
three wheels in contact with the ground, including, but not limited to, motor
scooters and mini-bikes.)
   MUFFLER OR DISSIPATIVE DEVICE: A device for abating sound of escaping gases
of an internal combustion engine.
   NCO: Noise control officer.
   NOISE: Any sound which annoys or disturbs humans or causes or tends to cause
an adverse psychological or physiological effect on humans.
   NOISE CONTROL OFFICER: The person or department appointed by the Shoshone
city council.
   NOISE DISTURBANCE: Any sound which: 1) endangers the safety or health of
humans or animals; or 2) annoys or disturbs a reasonable person of normal
sensitivities; or 3) endangers or injures personal or real property.
   NOISE SENSITIVE ZONE: Any area designated pursuant to subsection 8.20.040B8a
of this chapter for the purpose of ensuring exceptional quiet.
   PERSON: Any individual, association, partnership, or corporation, and
includes any officer, employee, department, agency or instrumentality of a
state or any political subdivision of a state.
   POWERED MODEL VEHICLE: Any self-propelled airborne, waterborne, or landborne
plane, vessel, or vehicle, which is not designed to carry persons, including,
but not limited to, any model airplane, boat, car, or rocket.
   PUBLIC RIGHT OF WAY: Any street, avenue, boulevard, highway, sidewalk or
alley or similar place which is owned or controlled by a governmental entity.
   PUBLIC SPACE: Any real property or structures thereon which are owned or
controlled by a governmental entity.
   PURE TONE: Any sound which can be distinctly heard as a single pitch or set
of single pitches. For the purpose of this chapter, a pure tone shall exist if
the one-third (1/3) octave band sound pressure level in the band with the tone
exceeds the arithmetic average of the sound pressure levels of the two (2)
contiguous one-third (1/3) octave bands by five (5) dB for center frequencies
of five hundred (500) Hz and above and by eight (8) dB for center frequencies
between one hundred sixty (160) and four hundred (400) Hz and by fifteen (15)
dB for center frequencies less than or equal to one hundred twenty five (125)
Hz.
   RMS SOUND PRESSURE: The square root of the time averaged square of the sound
pressure, denoted Prms.
   REAL PROPERTY BOUNDARY: An imaginary line along the ground surface, and its
vertical extension, which separates the real property owned by one person from
that owned by another person, but not including intrabuilding real property
divisions.
   RESIDENTIAL AREA: All areas within the following zones as specified in the
city of Shoshone comprehensive plan: R1, R2, R3 and R4, along with any and all
lands designated as residential within any planned unit development or
subdivision located within the limits of the city of Shoshone.
   SOUND: An oscillation in pressure, particle displacement, particle velocity
or other physical parameter, in a medium with internal forces that causes
compression and rarefaction of that medium. The description of sound may
include any characteristic of such sound, including duration, intensity and
frequency.
   SOUND LEVEL: The weighted sound pressure obtained by the use of a sound
level meter and frequency weighting network, such as A or C, as specified in
the American National Standards Institute specifications for sound level meters
(ANSI S1.4-1971), or the latest approved revision thereof. If the frequency
weighting employed is not indicated, the A-weighting shall apply.
   SOUND LEVEL METER: An instrument which includes a microphone, amplifier, RMS
detector, integrator or time averaging device, output meter, and weighting
networks used to measure sound pressure levels.
   SOUND PRESSURE: The instantaneous difference between the actual pressure and
the average or barometric pressure of a given point in space, as produced by
sound energy.
   SOUND PRESSURE LEVEL: Twenty (20) times the logarithm to the base-10 of the
ratio of the RMS sound pressure to the reference pressure of twenty (20)
micropascals (20 x 10mN/m). The sound pressure level is denoted Lp, or SPL and
is expressed in decibels.
   STATE: The state of Idaho, United States Of America.
   VIBRATION: An oscillatory motion of solid bodies of deterministic or random
nature described by displacement, velocity, or acceleration with respect to a
given reference point.
   WEEKDAY: Any day Monday through Friday which is not a legal holiday. (Ord.
528, 2012: Ord. 526, 2011)
8.20.040: POWERS AND DUTIES OF THE SHOSHONE CITY COUNCIL:
   A.   Lead Agency: The noise control program established by this chapter
shall be administered by the city council of the city of Shoshone.
   B.   Powers Of The Shoshone City Council: In order to implement and enforce
this chapter and for the general purpose of sound and vibration abatement and
control, the city council shall have, in addition to any other authority vested
in it, the power to:
      1.   Studies: Conduct, or cause to be conducted, research, monitoring,
and other studies related to sound and vibration.
      2.   Education:
         a.   Conduct programs of public education regarding:
            (1)   The causes, effects, and general methods of abatement and
control of noise and vibration; and
            (2)   The actions prohibited by this chapter and the procedures for
reporting violations.
         b.   Encourage the participation of public interest groups in related
public information efforts.
      3.   Coordination And Cooperation:
         a.   Coordinate the noise and vibration control activities of all city
of Shoshone departments;
         b.   Cooperate to the extent practicable with all state and federal
agencies;
         c.   Cooperate or combine to the extent practicable with appropriate
county and municipal agencies; and
         d.   Enter into contracts for the provision of technical and
enforcement services.
      4.   Review Of Public And Private Projects:
         a.   Review public and private projects, subject to mandatory review
or approval by other departments, for compliance with this chapter, if such
projects are likely to cause sound or vibration in violation of this chapter.
      5.   Records: Require the owner or operator of any commercial or
industrial activity to establish and maintain records and make such reports as
the city council may reasonably prescribe.
      6.   Designate Noise Sensitive Zones: Designate noise sensitive zones
which contain noise sensitive activities. Existing quiet zones shall be
considered noise sensitive zones until otherwise designated. Noise sensitive
activities include, but are not limited to, operation of schools, libraries
open to the public, churches, hospitals, convalescent centers and/or nursing
homes.
      7.   Delegation Of Authority: Delegate functions, where appropriate under
this chapter, to planning and zoning commission, police department, building
inspector, or other city of Shoshone employees or outside contractors.
      8.   Truck Routes And Transportation Planning:
         a.   Study the existing transportation systems, such as truck routes
within the community; determine areas with sensitivity to sound and vibration
caused by transportation; recommend and/or implement modifications to
transportation systems to minimize the sound and vibration impact on
residential areas and noise sensitive zones.
         b.   Assist in or review the total transportation planning of the
community, including planning for new roads and highways, bus routes, airports,
and other systems for public transportation, to ensure that the impact of sound
and vibration receives adequate consideration.
      9.   Administer Grants, Funds And Gifts: Administer noise program grants
and other funds and gifts from public and private sources, including state and
federal governments. (Ord. 526, 2011)
8.20.041: POWERS AND DUTIES OF THE NOISE CONTROL OFFICER (SHOSHONE POLICE OR
ANY OTHER LAW ENFORCEMENT OFFICER OF LINCOLN COUNTY):
   A.   Duties Of Noise Control Officer: In order to implement and enforce this
chapter effectively, the NCO shall within a reasonable time after the effective
date hereof:
      1.   Standards, Testing Methods, And Procedures: Develop, and promulgate
standards, testing methods and procedures.
      2.   Investigate And Pursue Violations: In consonance with subsection
8.20.040B5, section
8.20.100, and other provisions of this chapter, investigate and pursue possible
violations of this chapter.
      3.   Inspections:
         a.   Upon presentation of proper credentials, enter and inspect any
private property or place, and inspect any report or records at any reasonable
time when granted permission by the owner, or by some other person with
apparent authority to act for the owner. When permission is refused or cannot
be obtained, a search warrant may be obtained from a court of competent
jurisdiction upon showing of probable cause to believe a violation of this
chapter may exist. Such inspection may include administration of any necessary
tests.
         b.   Stop any motor vehicle, motorcycle, or motorboat operated on a
public right of way, public space, or public waterway reasonably suspected of
violating any provision of this chapter, and issue a notice of violation or
abatement order which may require the motor vehicle, motorcycle, or motorboat
to be inspected or tested as the NCO may reasonably require.
      4.   Measurement By The Owner Or Operator: Require the owner or operator
of any commercial or industrial activity to measure the sound level of or the
vibration from any source in accordance with methods and procedures prescribed
by the NCO and at such locations and times as the NCO may reasonably prescribe
and to furnish reports of the results of such measurements to the NCO. The NCO
may require the measurements and tests to be conducted in the presence of its
enforcement officials. (Ord. 526, 2011)
8.20.050: DUTIES AND RESPONSIBILITIES OF CITY OF SHOSHONE DEPARTMENTS:
   A.   Departmental Actions: All departments and agencies shall, to the
fullest extent consistent with other law, carry out their programs in such a
manner as to further the policy of this chapter.
   B.   Departmental Cooperation: All departments and agencies shall cooperate
with the NCO to the fullest extent in enforcing this chapter.
   C.   Departmental Compliance With Other Laws: All departments and agencies
shall comply with federal and state laws and regulations and the provisions and
intent of this chapter respecting the control and abatement of noise to the
same extent that any person is subject to such laws and regulations.
   D.   Project Approval: All departments, commissions or individuals whose
duty it is to review and approve new projects that result, or may result, in
the production of sound or vibration shall consult with the NCO prior to any
such approval.
   E.   Contracts: Any written contract, agreement, whereby the city of
Shoshone is committed to the expenditure of one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) or
more in return for goods or services shall contain provisions requiring
compliance with this chapter. (Ord. 526, 2011)
8.20.060: PROHIBITED ACTS:
   A.   Noise Disturbances Prohibited: No person shall unreasonably make,
continue, or cause to be made, or continued, any noise disturbance.
Noncommercial public speaking and public assembly activities conducted on any
public space or public right of way shall be exempt from the operation of this
section.
   B.   Specific Prohibitions: The following acts, and causing thereof, are
declared to be in violation of this chapter:
      1.   Radios, Television Sets, Musical Instruments, And Similar Devices:
Operating, playing or permitting the operation or playing of any radio,
television, phonograph, drum, musical instrument, sound amplifier, or similar
device which produces, reproduces, or amplifies sound:
         a.   Between the hours of eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. and seven
o'clock (7:00) A.M. the following day in such a manner as to create a noise
disturbance across a real property boundary or a noise sensitive zone (except
for activities specifically excluded in subsection 8.20.070B of this chapter).
         b.   In such a manner as to create a noise disturbance to any person
other than the operator of the device, when operated by a passenger on a common
carrier.
         c.   This section will not apply to noncommercial spoken language
covered under subsection B2 of this section.
      2.   Loudspeakers/Public Address Systems:
         a.   Using or operating for any noncommercial purpose any loudspeaker
public address system, or similar device between the hours of eleven o'clock
(11:00) P.M. and seven o'clock (7:00) A.M. the following day, such that the
sound therefrom creates a noise disturbance across a residential real property
boundary or within a noise sensitive zone.
         b.   Using or operating for any commercial purpose any loudspeaker,
public address system, or similar device such that the sound therefrom creates
a noise disturbance across a real property boundary or within a noise sensitive
zone; or between the hours of eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. and seven o'clock (7:
00) A.M. the following day on a public right of way or public space.
      3.   Street Sales: Offering for sale or selling anything by shouting or
outcry within any residential or commercial area of the city of Shoshone
(except by permit issued by the city of Shoshone which specifies the times of
operation and noise limits).
      4.   Animals And Birds: Owning, possessing or harboring any animal or
bird which frequently or for continued duration, howls, barks, squawks, or
makes other sounds which create a noise disturbance across a residential real
property boundary or within a noise sensitive area.
      5.   Loading And Unloading: Loading, unloading, opening, closing, or
other handling of boxes, crates, containers, building materials, garbage cans,
or similar objects between the hours of eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. and seven
o'clock (7:00) A.M. the following day in such a manner as to cause a noise
disturbance across a residential real property boundary or within a noise
sensitive zone.
      6.   Construction: Operating or permitting the operation of any tools or
equipment used in construction, drilling or demolition work:
         a.   Between the hours of nine o'clock (9:00) P.M. and seven o'clock
(7:00) A.M. the following day on weekdays or between the hours of nine o'clock
(9:00) P.M. and eight o'clock (8:00) A.M. the following day on weekends and
holidays, such that the sound therefrom creates a noise disturbance across a
residential real property boundary or within a noise sensitive zone, except for
emergency work of public service utilities or by special variance issued by the
city of Shoshone city council.
         b.   This subsection shall not apply to the use of domestic power
tools subject to subsection B15 of this section.
      7.   Use Of Compression Brakes: The use of compression brakes, commonly
referred to as "jake" brakes, is hereby prohibited within the geographical
limits of the city of Shoshone. Conspicuous signs identifying said prohibition
shall be placed and maintained at all entries to the city of Shoshone on U.S.
Highways 26 and 93; and State Highways 24, 26 and 75.
      8.   Vehicle Or Motorboat Repair Or Testing: Repairing, rebuilding,
modifying, or testing any motor vehicle, motorcycle, or motorboat in such a
manner as to cause a noise disturbance across a residential real property
boundary or within a noise sensitive zone.
      9.   Places Of Public Entertainment: Operating, playing or permitting the
operation or playing of any radio, television, phonograph, drum, musical
instrument, sound amplifier or similar device which produces, reproduces, or
amplifies sound in any place of public entertainment at a sound level greater
than ninety five (95) dBA as read by the slow response on a sound level meter
at any point that is normally occupied by a customer, unless a conspicuous and
legible sign is located outside such place, near each public entrance, stating:
            WARNING: SOUND LEVELS WITHIN MAY CAUSE PERMANENT HEARING
IMPAIRMENT.
      10.   Explosives And Similar Devices: The use or firing of explosives or
similar devices which create impulsive sound so as to cause a noise disturbance
across a real property boundary or on a public space or right of way, without
first obtaining a special variance permit from the city of Shoshone.
      11.   Powered Model Vehicles: Operating or permitting the operation of
powered model vehicles so as to create a noise disturbance across a residential
real property boundary, in a public space, or in a noise sensitive zone between
the hours of nine o'clock (9:00) P.M. and nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. the
following day.
      12.   Vibration: Operating or permitting the operation of any device that
creates vibration which is above the vibration perception threshold of an
individual at or beyond the property of the source if on private property or at
fifty feet (50') (15 meters) from the source if on public space or public right
of way. For purposes of this section, "vibration perception threshold" means
the minimum ground or structureborne vibratory motion necessary to cause a
normal person to be aware of the vibration by such direct means as, but not
limited to, sensation by touch or usual observation of moving objects.
      13.   Motorboats: Operating or permitting the operation of any motorboat
in the Little Wood River in such manner as to exceed a sound level of one
hundred (100) dBA at fifty feet (50') (15 meters).
      14.   Noise Sensitive Zones:
         a.   Creating or causing the creation of any sound within any noise
sensitive zone designated pursuant to subsection
8.20.040B8 of this chapter, so as to disrupt the activities normally conducted
within the zone, provided that conspicuous signs are displayed indicating the
presence of the zone; or
         b.   Creating or causing the creation of any sound within any noise
sensitive zone designated pursuant to subsection
8.20.040B8 of this chapter, containing a hospital, nursing home, or similar
activity, so as to interfere with the functions of such activity or disturb or
annoy the patients in the activity, provided that conspicuous signs are
displayed indicating the presence of the zone.
      15.   Domestic Power Tools: Operating or permitting the operation of any
mechanically powered saw, sander, drill, grinder, lawn or garden tool,
snowblower, or similar device used outdoors in residential areas between the
hours of eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. and seven o'clock (7:00) A.M. the
following day so as to cause a noise disturbance across a residential real
property boundary. (Ord. 526, 2011)
8.20.070: EXCEPTIONS AND VARIANCES:
   A.   Emergency Exception: The provisions of this chapter shall not apply to:
      1.   The emission of sound for the purpose of alerting persons to the
existence of an emergency, or
      2.   The emission of sound in the performance of emergency work.
      3.   Catastrophic events or acts of God.
   B.   Exempted Events:
      1.   All events that have received a written permit from the city of
Shoshone, Lincoln County, or the Lincoln County fair board provided that:
         a.   The event has specified days and hours of operation and generated
noise limits that conform to the intent of this chapter, and
         b.   The event promoter has been advised in writing of this chapter
and the enforcement thereof.
      2.   A "fast track" procedure shall be established and utilized by the
NCO to provide for review of event permits for unexpected events with very
short planning cycles.
      3.   Typical events expected to be exempted after appropriate review and
approval are:
         a.   Lincoln County Fair,
         b.   Lincoln County Rodeo,
         c.   High school rodeos,
         d.   "Arts In The Park",
         e.   Events held at the Lincoln County Community Center building,
         f.   Parades,
         g.   Events held at city parks or the county courthouse grounds,
         h.   Other events held at the Lincoln County Fairgrounds and Rodeo
Grounds.
   C.   Special Variances:
      1.   Granting Of Special Variances: The city council shall have
authority, consistent with this section, to grant special variances which may
be requested pursuant to subsections
8.20.060B6, "Construction", and B10, "Explosives And Similar Devices", of this
chapter.
      2.   Application Filed: Any person seeking a special variance pursuant to
this section shall file an application with the city council. The application
shall contain information which demonstrates that bringing the source of sound
or activity for which the special variance is sought into compliance with this
chapter would constitute an unreasonable hardship on the applicant. (Notice of
an application for a special variance shall be published according to city of
Shoshone procedure.) Any individual who claims to be adversely affected by the
allowance of the special variance may file a statement with the city council
containing any information supporting his claim. If the city council finds that
a sufficient controversy exists regarding an application, a public hearing may
be held.
      3.   Determination: In determining whether to grant or deny the
application, the city council shall balance the hardship to the applicant, the
community, and other persons of not granting the special variance against the
adverse impact on the health, safety, and welfare of persons affected, and any
other adverse impacts of granting the special variance. Applicants for special
variances and persons contesting special variances may be required to submit
any information that the city council shall reasonably require. In granting or
denying an application, the city council shall place on public file a copy of
the decision and the reasons for denying or granting the special variance.
      4.   Conditions; Time Limit: Special variances shall be granted by notice
to the applicant containing all necessary conditions, including a time limit on
the permitted activity. The special variance shall not become effective until
all conditions are agreed to by the applicant. Noncompliance with any condition
of the special variance shall terminate it and subject the person holding it to
those provisions of this chapter regulating the source of sound or activity for
which the special variance was granted, including enforcement actions.
      5.   Extension Of Time Limit: Application for extension of time limit
specified in special variances or for modification of other substantial
conditions shall be treated like applications for initial special variances
under subsection C2 of this section.
      6.   Guidelines: The city council may issue guidelines defining
procedures to be followed in applying for a special variance and the criteria
to be considered in deciding whether to grant a special variance.
      7.   Appeals: Appeals of an adverse decision of the city council shall be
made to the magistrate court, county of Lincoln, state of Idaho. Review of the
court shall be limited to whether the decision is supported by substantial
evidence. (Ord. 526, 2011)
8.20.080: SOUND LEVELS BY RECEIVING LAND USE:
   A.   Maximum Permissible Sound Levels: No person shall operate or cause to
be operated on private property any source of sound in such a manner as to
create a sound level which exceeds the limits set forth for the receiving land
use category in table 1 of this section when measured at or within the property
boundary of the receiving land use.

                               next day

   B.   Correction For Character Of Sound: For any source of sound which emits
a pure tone or impulsive sound, the maximum sound level limits set forth in
table 1 of this section shall be reduced by five (5) dBA.
   C.   Exemptions: The provisions of this section shall not apply to:
      1.   Subsections
8.20.060B6, "Construction", B10, "Explosives And Similar Devices", and B15,
"Domestic Power Tools", of this chapter;
      2.   The unamplified human voice;
      3.   Interstate railway locomotives and cars;
      4.   Nonstationary farm equipment;
      5.   Sewer plant; and
      6.   Twelve o'clock (12:00) noon and ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. whistle.
(Ord. 528, 2012: Ord. 526, 2011)

   A.   Motor Vehicles And Motorcycles On Public Rights Of Way: No person shall
operate or cause to be operated a public or private motor vehicle or motorcycle
on a public right of way at any time in such a manner that the sound level
emitted by the motor vehicle or motorcycle exceeds the level set forth in table
2 of this section.

      1.   Adequate Mufflers Or Sound Dissipative Devices:
         a.   No person shall operate or cause to be operated any motor vehicle
or motorcycle not equipped with a muffler or other sound dissipative device in
good working order and in constant operation;
         b.   No person shall remove or render inoperative, or cause to be
removed or rendered inoperative, other than for purposes of maintenance,
repair, or replacement, any muffler or sound dissipative device on a motor
vehicle or motorcycle;
         c.   The city of Shoshone city council may list those acts which
constitute violation of this section.
      2.   Motor Vehicle Horns And Signaling Devices: The following acts and
the causing thereof are declared to be in violation of this chapter:
         a.   The sounding of any horn or other auditory device on or in any
motor vehicle on any public right of way or public space, except as a warning
or as provided in the state of Idaho vehicle code.
         b.   The sounding of any horn or other auditory device which produces
a sound level in excess of one hundred five (105) dBA when measured at a
distance of fifty feet (50') or fifteen meters (15 m) or more. (Ord. 526, 2011)
8.20.100: ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Penalties:
      1.   Any person who violates any provision of this chapter shall be
guilty of an infraction and fined a minimum of ninety five dollars ($95.00).
      2.   Each occurrence of violation of any provision of this chapter shall
constitute a separate offense. (Ord. 526, 2011)
CHAPTER 8.24
SMOKING IN PUBLIC PLACES
SECTION:
8.24.010: Authority
8.24.020: Purpose
8.24.030: Definitions
8.24.040: Application To City Owned Facilities And Areas
8.24.050: Prohibition Of Smoking In Or On Public Property
8.24.060: Violation; Penalty
8.24.070: Other Applicable Laws
8.24.010: AUTHORITY:
This chapter is adopted pursuant to the authority granted by the Idaho
Constitution and Idaho Code, including without limitation sections 39-5511 and
50-302. (Ord. 555, 2018)
8.24.020: PURPOSE:
The conclusions of public health officials concerning secondhand tobacco smoke
are sufficient to warrant measures that regulate smoking in public places in
order to protect the public health. The purpose of this chapter is to protect
the public health and the rights of nonsmokers to breathe clean air by
prohibiting smoking in public places. (Ord. 555, 2018)
8.24.030: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter:
E-CIGARETTE: Any electronic oral device, such as one composed of a heating
element, battery, and/or electronic circuit, which provides a vapor of nicotine
or any other substances, and the use or inhalation of which simulates smoking.
The term shall include any such device, whether manufactured, distributed,
marketed, or sold as an e-cigarette, e-cigar, e-pipe, or under any other
product name or descriptor.
PUBLIC PLACE: An area to which the public is invited or in which the public is
permitted for any purpose.
PUBLIC PROPERTY: Any and all lands owned, leased, or operated by the City of
Shoshone including all City parks and open spaces.
SMOKING: Inhaling, exhaling, burning, carrying, or possessing any lighted or
heated cigar, cigarette, or pipe, or any other lighted or heated tobacco or
plant product intended for inhalation, in any manner or in any form. "Smoking"
also includes the use of an e-cigarette which creates vapor, in any manner or
any form, or the use of any oral smoking device for the purpose of
circumventing the prohibition of smoking in this chapter.
SPECIAL EVENT ZONE: Any outdoor area delineated through a special permit to
accommodate people in a smoke free space for such activities as concerts,
movies, or other entertainment in a space. (Ord. 555, 2018)
8.24.040: APPLICATION TO CITY OWNED FACILITIES AND AREAS:
All public property and indoor and outdoor areas owned, leased, or operated by
the City of Shoshone shall be subject to the provisions of this chapter. (Ord.
555, 2018)
8.24.050: PROHIBITION OF SMOKING IN OR ON PUBLIC PROPERTY:
Smoking shall be prohibited on all public property, and indoor and outdoor
public places within the limits of the City of Shoshone that are owned, leased,
or operated by the City of Shoshone, including, but not limited to, the
following places:
   A.   Within any buildings or structures owned, leased or operated by the
City of Shoshone.
   B.   Within fifty feet (50') of entrances, exits, windows or air intakes to
buildings or structures owned, leased or operated by the City of Shoshone.
   C.   On any public property as defined herein.
   D.   Within any designated special event zone as defined herein. (Ord. 555,
2018)
8.24.060: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
   A.   Smoking Where Prohibited: A person who smokes in or on any public place
where smoking is prohibited by the provisions of this chapter shall be guilty
of an infraction, punishable by a fine of one hundred dollars ($100.00), plus
court costs.
   B.   Violations Declared Public Nuisance: Violation of this chapter is
hereby declared to be a public nuisance, which may be abated by the City of
Shoshone by restraining order, preliminary and permanent injunction, or other
means provided for by law, and the City of Shoshone may take action to recover
attorney fees and/or costs of the nuisance abatement. (Ord. 555, 2018)
8.24.070: OTHER APPLICABLE LAWS:
This chapter shall not be interpreted or construed to permit smoking where it
is otherwise restricted by other applicable laws or by the owner, operator,
manager, or other person in control of such facility or area. (Ord. 555, 2018)
TITLE 9
PUBLIC PEACE, MORALS, AND WELFARE
Disorderly Conduct   9.04
Weapons   9.08
Spitting   9.12
Curfew      9.16
CHAPTER 9.04
DISORDERLY CONDUCT
SECTION:
9.04.010: Designated
9.04.010: DESIGNATED:
The following persons are guilty of committing a misdemeanor:
   A.   Any person who unlawfully fights in a public place or challenges
another person in a public place to fight;
   B.   Any person who maliciously and wilfully disturbs another person by loud
and unreasonable noise;
   C.   Any person who uses offensive words in a public place which are
inherently likely to provide an immediate violent reaction;
   D.   Any person who makes any open and lewd exposure of his person or the
person of another, or who urinates or defecates, in the sense of excreting
waste matter from the bowels or bladder, on public streets, sidewalks or other
public places or in view or in potential view of other persons, knowing that
such conduct is likely to cause reasonable affront or alarm to any other
persons;
   E.   Any person, not an officer in the discharge of his duty, who discharges
within the limits of the city, unless in the defense of the person, life or
property, any firearm loaded with a bullet or dangerous missile. (Ord. 392,
1989: Ord. 359, 1981)
CHAPTER 9.08
WEAPONS
SECTION:
9.08.010: Concealed Weapons Prohibited (Rep. by Ord. 406, 1990)
9.08.020: Slingshots, Air Guns Prohibited
9.08.010: CONCEALED WEAPONS PROHIBITED:
(Rep. by Ord. 406, 1990)
9.08.020: SLINGSHOTS, AIR GUNS PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful for any person to use within the city an instrument commonly
known as a slingshot, being a small piece of leather or other tough substance
with long leather thongs attached to each end by means of which stones, rocks,
buckshot or other missiles may be expelled and discharged at great speed; or an
instrument commonly known as a flipper, being two (2) bands of rubber or other
elastic substance attached to the two (2) extremities of a forked stick by
means of which stones, rocks, buckshot or other missiles may be expelled or
discharged at great speed; or any instrument commonly known as an air gun,
being an instrument resembling a gun out of which leaden bullets or shot are
expelled with great force by the use of springs or compressed air. (Prior code
§ 9-201)
CHAPTER 9.12
SPITTING
SECTION:
9.12.010: Prohibited
9.12.010: PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful for any person to spit upon any of the sidewalks or crosswalks
within the corporate limits of the city. (Prior code § 7-301)
CHAPTER 9.16
CURFEW
SECTION:
9.16.010: Definitions
9.16.020: Regulation Of Minors
9.16.030: Exceptions To The Regulation Of Minors
9.16.040: Parental Responsibility
9.16.050: Operator Of An Establishment
9.16.060: Operator Or Owner Of A Motor Vehicle
9.16.070: Required Information
9.16.080: Enforcement
9.16.090: Penalties
9.16.010: DEFINITIONS:
The terms as used in this chapter shall have the following meanings:
EMERGENCY: An unforeseen circumstance or combination of circumstances that
requires immediate action to safeguard life, limb, or property. Emergencies
shall include, but shall not be limited to, fires, natural disasters,
automobile crashes, or other similar circumstances.
ESTABLISHMENT: Any privately owned place of business operated for a profit to
which the public is invited, including, but not limited to, places for
amusement or entertainment. The operator of an establishment shall include the
person(s) authorized with management responsibilities who is on the premises of
the establishment at the time in which a minor is located on the premises, the
person with overall authority for managing the establishment, and the person(s)
or entity who owns the establishment.
GUARDIAN: A person who has been judicially appointed as the legal guardian, or
a person over the age of eighteen (18) who has been authorized by the legal
guardian or parent to assume care, control and responsibility for the minor for
a definitive period of time.
MINOR: Any person under the age of eighteen (18).
PARENT: A minor's biological, adoptive or stepparent.
PUBLIC PLACE: Any place to which the public or a substantial group of the
public has access, including, but not limited to, streets, highways,
thoroughfares, sidewalks, alleys, parking lots, parks, and the common areas of
schools, hospitals, apartment complexes, office buildings, transportation
facilities, entertainment facilities, and shops.
REMAIN: To stay or linger at or upon a place; or to fail to depart when
requested to do so by a police officer or a person with authority to act in the
interest of the establishment or public place at which the minor is located.
(Ord. 527, 2012)
9.16.020: REGULATION OF MINORS:
It shall be unlawful for any minor to remain in or upon any public place, to
remain in any motor vehicle operating or parked in or upon a public place or
establishment, or to remain in or upon the premises of any establishment,
between the hours of twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight and five o'clock (5:00)
A.M., unless their presence is explained by one of the enumerated exceptions.
Any person to be found in violation of this section shall be guilty of an
infraction and fined one hundred dollars ($100.00) (plus required court costs).
(Ord. 550, 2015: Ord. 527, 2012)
9.16.030: EXCEPTIONS TO THE REGULATION OF MINORS:
   A.   The minor is accompanied by a parent or guardian.
   B.   An emergency situation exists.
   C.   The minor is engaged in an employment activity, or is going to or
returning home from such activity without detour or stop, except for purposes
of obtaining fuel for transportation.
   D.   The minor is on a sidewalk directly abutting the place in which they
reside; or within three hundred feet (300') of their residence and the
neighboring residents have not issued a complaint about the minor's presence.
   E.   The minor is attending an activity sponsored by a school, religious, or
civic organization, by a public organization or entity, or by another similar
organization or entity, which activity is supervised by adults; or is going to
or returning from such activity without detour or stop, except for purposes of
obtaining fuel for transportation.
   F.   The minor is on an errand and has in their possession written parental
authorization for the errand to include the destination(s) of the errand, time
allotted for the errand, and a contact telephone number to verify parental
authorization.
   G.   The minor is involved in interstate travel through or beginning or
terminating in, the City of Shoshone.
   H.   The minor is exercising first amendment rights protected by the United
States Constitution, such as the free exercise of religion, freedom of speech,
and the right of assembly. (Ord. 527, 2012)
9.16.040: PARENTAL RESPONSIBILITY:
It is the responsibility of the parent or legal guardian to ensure that a minor
complies with this chapter. It shall be unlawful for a parent or legal guardian
to knowingly permit, allow, or encourage a violation of this chapter. (Ord.
527, 2012)
9.16.050: OPERATOR OF AN ESTABLISHMENT:
It shall be unlawful for any operator of an "establishment", as defined within
this chapter, to knowingly permit, allow or encourage a minor to remain at or
upon the premises of the establishment in violation of this chapter. It shall
be a defense to this violation that the operator or an employee of the
establishment promptly notified police that a minor was present at the
establishment and refused to leave when requested. (Ord. 527, 2012)
9.16.060: OPERATOR OR OWNER OF A MOTOR VEHICLE:
It shall be unlawful for the owner or operator of a motor vehicle to knowingly
permit, allow or encourage a violation of this chapter. (Ord. 527, 2012)
9.16.070: REQUIRED INFORMATION:
Every person suspected of a curfew violation shall provide their name and age
to a police officer upon request. Any person who refuses to provide such
information, or who knowingly gives false information regarding their name or
age, or another person's name or age to any police officer conducting an
investigation under this chapter shall be in violation of this chapter. (Ord.
527, 2012)
9.16.080: ENFORCEMENT:
Before taking any enforcement action under this chapter, a police officer shall
investigate whether the minor's presence in a public place, motor vehicle, or
establishment falls within one of the enumerated exceptions to minor
regulations. If the officer cannot reasonably determine the existence of one of
the enumerated exceptions, and probable cause otherwise exists, the officer may
take appropriate enforcement action. (Ord. 527, 2012)
9.16.090: PENALTIES:
Any person found to be in violation of any of the provisions of this chapter
shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, and upon conviction thereof, shall be
punished by a fine no greater than three hundred dollars ($300.00) or
imprisonment in the County Jail for no more than six (6) months or by both such
fine and imprisonment. (Ord. 527, 2012)
