CHAPTER 10.04
VEHICLE CODE
SECTION:
10.04.010: Purpose Of Provisions
10.04.020: Adopted
10.04.030: Amendments
10.04.040: Copies On File
10.04.050: Adoption, New Amendments; Restrictions
10.04.060: Speed Limits
10.04.070: The Term "Infraction" Changed To "Violation"
10.04.010: PURPOSE OF PROVISIONS:
It is the intent of the governing body of the city to aid and assist by
whatever means possible for the utmost consistency in traffic regulation among
and between agencies of Idaho having such jurisdiction. Toward that end,
adoption of the Idaho motor vehicle laws by the cities of Idaho is a necessary
means of assuring maximum uniformity within the state. (Ord. 307 § 1, 1971)
10.04.020: ADOPTED:
There is adopted for the purpose of establishing rules and regulations for the
use of all streets and public thoroughfares of the city, that certain code
identified as the 1969 revised edition, Idaho motor vehicle laws, more
particularly title 49, Idaho Code, published by the department of law
enforcement, and as the same may hereafter be revised by the Idaho legislature
or amended by the governing body, and the same is adopted and incorporated as
an ordinance of the city as fully as though set forth at length in this
chapter. (Ord. 357, 1981: Ord. 307 § 2, 1971)
10.04.030: AMENDMENTS:
The 1969 revised edition, Idaho motor vehicle laws, more particularly title 49,
Idaho Code, published by the department of law enforcement, and as the same may
hereafter be revised by the Idaho legislature or amended by the governing body,
is amended by adding to section 49-662(1) of said code the phrase "or where
appropriate signs are erected prohibiting such turns", as permitted by the
Idaho Code 49-582(1)h. (Ord. 357, 1981)
10.04.040: COPIES ON FILE:
Three (3) copies of the Idaho motor vehicle laws, together with any revisions
or amendments duly certified by the city clerk, are kept on file in his office
for use and examination of and by the public. (Ord. 307 § 3, 1971)
10.04.050: ADOPTION, NEW AMENDMENTS; RESTRICTIONS:
Notwithstanding any and all other provisions of this code, the council hereby
adopts title 49 of the Idaho Code dealing with motor vehicles insofar as the
title pertains to the city, but specifically excluding those provisions that
are the sole domain of the state of Idaho, and that as new amendments of title
49 are adopted by the state, if any, then this section adopts the same
amendments in an identical fashion subject to the restriction noted above. Any
conflicting Shoshone city ordinance shall be removed from this code at its next
printing. (Ord. 396, 1989)
10.04.060: SPEED LIMITS:
See
chapter 10.06 of this title for speed limit regulations. (Ord. 491, 2004: Ord.
396, 1989)
10.04.070: THE TERM "INFRACTION" CHANGED TO "VIOLATION":
The word "infraction" wherever found throughout this code, except where it
occurs in relation to a traffic infraction, shall be replaced with the word
"violation". (Ord. 396, 1989)
CHAPTER 10.06
SPEED LIMIT
SECTION:
10.06.010: Definitions
10.06.020: Maximum Speed Limit
10.06.030: Exemption
10.06.040: Violations And Penalties
10.06.010: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
HIGHWAY: The entire width between the boundary lines of every way publicly
maintained when any part is open to the use of the public for vehicular travel,
with jurisdiction extending to the adjacent property line. The terms "street"
and "road" are interchangeable with highway.
VEHICLE: Every device in, upon, or by which any person or property is or may be
transported or drawn upon a highway, excepting devices used exclusively upon
stationary rails or tracks. (Ord. 491 § 3, 2004)
10.06.020: MAXIMUM SPEED LIMIT:
The maximum speed limits for vehicles within the corporate limits of the city
of Shoshone shall be twenty (20) miles per hour. (Ord. 491 § 1, 2004)
10.06.030: EXEMPTION:
This chapter shall not apply to any highway within the corporate limits of the
city of Shoshone which is controlled by the federal and/or state governments,
unless the authority to set maximum speed limits is ceded to the city of
Shoshone by said governments. (Ord. 491 § 2, 2004)
10.06.040: VIOLATIONS AND PENALTIES:
Any person who violates this chapter shall be guilty of an infraction and fined
in a manner the same as a violation of Idaho Code section 49-654. (Ord. 491 §
4, 2004)
CHAPTER 10.08
IMPOUNDMENT
SECTION:
10.08.010: Overtime Parking
10.08.020: Notice
10.08.030: Removal; Cost Assessment
10.08.040: Violation; Penalty
10.08.050: Towing And Impounding Fees
10.08.060: Sale Of Impounded Vehicles
10.08.010: OVERTIME PARKING:
   A.   It is unlawful for any owner or any person having control or custody of
any vehicle to allow the vehicle to remain permanently stored or placed in dead
car storage on the streets of the city or any alley or public driveway of the
city.
   B.   This section shall not be construed so as to prohibit the mere parking
of an automobile overnight on the streets of the city and shall not interfere
with any right to leave an unattended vehicle on the streets. (Ord. 303, 1970:
prior code § 8-114)
10.08.020: NOTICE:
In the event it is determined that a vehicle has been left unattended for an
unreasonable length of time, the city clerk shall cause to be issued a notice
in writing and served by certified mail, or in lieu thereof, by affixing the
notice on the vehicle in a conspicuous place and advising the owner or party in
charge of the vehicle that unless the vehicle is removed it shall be subject to
impounding by police officials. (Ord. 303, 1970: prior code § 8-114)
10.08.030: REMOVAL; COST ASSESSMENT:
In the event the owner, or those persons in custody or control of the vehicle,
fails to remove same after due notice, as described in section 10.08.020 of
this chapter, is given, then, twenty four (24) hours thereafter, the vehicle
shall be impounded by the city police by those means reasonable and necessary
and safely stored in those places designated by the chief of police and the
vehicle shall not be released except upon his order. The person or persons
claiming the vehicle shall pay any fees associated including the initial towing
fees, plus any storage and costs as deemed appropriate by such company before
the chief of police shall be required to order the release of the vehicle.
(Ord. 543, 2013)
10.08.040: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person who leaves a vehicle permanently stored or in dead car storage or on
the streets, alleys or public ways of the city for a period of twenty four (24)
hours after the notice has been posted in a conspicuous place on the vehicle or
mailed, as provided in this chapter, is guilty of a misdemeanor. (Ord. 303,
1970: prior code § 8-114)
10.08.050: TOWING AND IMPOUNDING FEES:
The owner or person in charge of any vehicle confiscated by the city police or
those left permanently stored, abandoned, or placed in dead storage on the
streets, alley, or public driveway of the city and impounded by the police
shall pay any fees associated including the initial towing fees, plus any
storage and costs as deemed appropriate by such company. (Ord. 532, 2012)
10.08.060: SALE OF IMPOUNDED VEHICLES:
Any vehicle so impounded may be sold for storage and/or impoundment upon
agreement with the owner; and any vehicle abandoned may be sold for the
aforesaid fees upon following the procedures set forth in chapter 36 of title
49 of the Idaho Code as it now exists and as it may be hereafter amended. (Ord.
383, 1986)
CHAPTER 10.12
PARKING
SECTION:
10.12.010: Prohibited Generally
10.12.020: Private Drive; Fire Station
10.12.030: Crosswalk
10.12.040: School Area
10.12.050: Truck Restrictions
10.12.060: Theater Entrance
10.12.070: Violation; Penalty
10.12.010: PROHIBITED GENERALLY:
At all places on the streets of the city where the streets are marked with
lines extending at an angle from the gutter out into the street, vehicles must
be parked parallel with and between the lines with the right front wheel
touching the curb. At all other places, vehicles must be parked parallel with
the gutter and there shall not be more than eighteen inches (18") distance
between the gutter and wheels of the vehicle; provided, however, that on the
portion of North Rail Street and South Rail Street where there are no concrete
curb lines, vehicles must park off the paved portion of the street. (Prior code
§ 8-101)
10.12.020: PRIVATE DRIVE; FIRE STATION:
No person shall park a vehicle or permit it to stand upon any street of the
city in front of a private driveway or within fifteen feet (15') in either
direction of the entrance of the fire station or within twenty five feet (25')
of the intersection of the curb lines of any street. (Prior code § 8-101)
10.12.030: CROSSWALK:
No person shall park any vehicle within ten feet (10') on either side of the
crosswalks. (Prior code § 8-101)
10.12.040: SCHOOL AREA:
No person shall park any vehicle on the easterly side of South Apple Street
between West C Street and West D Street, that being the western side of the
high school block, or on the north side of West 4th Street between North Apple
Street and North Birch Street, that being the south side of the Lincoln School
block, between the hours of eight o'clock (8:00) A.M. and five o'clock (5:00)
P.M. of all school days for a period longer than three (3) minutes. (Prior code
§ 8-101)
10.12.050: TRUCK RESTRICTIONS:
No person shall park any truck or vehicle with a trailer attached on any of the
following streets:
   A.   On South Rail Street from the intersection of South Birch Street to its
intersection with Greenwood Street;
   B.   On North Rail Street from its intersection with North Birch Street to
its intersection with Greenwood Street;
   C.   Providing, however, that trucks may park on the south side of North
Rail Street between North Apple Street and Greenwood Street. (Prior code § 8-
101)
10.12.060: THEATER ENTRANCE:
No person shall park any vehicle in front of the entranceway of any theater.
(Prior code § 8-101)
10.12.070: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter is guilty of a
misdemeanor. (1981 Code)
CHAPTER 10.16
RAILROADS
SECTION:
10.16.010: Crossing Hazard
10.16.020: Speed Limit
10.16.030: Blocking Intersections
10.16.040: Prosecution
10.16.050: Operator Determination
10.16.010: CROSSING HAZARD:
It is recognized by the city council in behalf of the city that a hazardous
condition exists on the intersection of Apple Street and the railroad crossing
located between South and North Rail Streets and at the intersection of
Greenwood Street and the railroad crossing located between South and North Rail
Streets and that the public policy of this state and the public policy of the
city requires that in the exercise of their police powers every precaution be
taken which will be reasonable and necessary for the preservation of life and
property by reason of accidents at such intersections so as to provide the
maximum safety for pedestrians and vehicular traffic on said streets without
unduly or unreasonably interfering with the railroad companies and their right
and use of the trackage which intersects said streets. (Ord. 258 § 1, 1957)
10.16.020: SPEED LIMIT:
It is unlawful for any railroad company, person, partnerships, associations, or
corporations, or persons working by and through such entities, to permit or
allow any rolling stock, including engine or attached cars, to travel upon any
railroad track within the corporate limits of the city at a speed in excess of
thirty five (35) miles per hour, excepting, however, this section shall have no
application to an engine or attached cars which have come to a complete halt
within the corporate limits; the purpose and intent of this section being to
restrict the speed of engines and attached cars entering the corporate limits
of the city and not to restrict the speed of the engine or attached cars when
leaving the corporate limits. Any person, persons, partnerships, associations,
or corporations which drive, propel, permit, or allow any rolling stock whether
the engine or propelling vehicle of the rolling stock or any cars attached
thereto, to proceed or travel upon railroad tracks within the corporate limits
of the city at a speed in excess of thirty five (35) miles per hour shall upon
conviction be guilty of a misdemeanor. (Ord. 333 § 2, 1976: Ord. 258 § 2, 1957)
10.16.030: BLOCKING INTERSECTIONS:
It is unlawful for any railroad company, person, persons, partnerships,
associations, or corporations, or any agent or person acting in behalf of such
railroad company, person, persons, partnerships, associations, or corporations,
to stop or park, or permit to park, any rolling stock of any railroad company
within three hundred feet (300') of the intersection of Apple Street and South
Rail Street and North Rail Street and/or the intersection of Greenwood Street
and South and North Rail Streets where the railroad presently intersects those
intersections; saving and excepting, however, that the provisions of this
section relating to the parking or stopping of vehicles shall not apply to
rolling stock designated as passenger trains or mail trains of the railroad.
Any person, persons, partnerships, associations, or corporations which stop or
permit to stop or park or permit to park any rolling stock of any railroad
company saving and excepting passenger and mail trains within three hundred
feet (300') of the intersection of Apple Street and South and North Rail
Streets and/or Greenwood Street and South and North Rail Streets where the
railroad presently intersects those intersections shall upon conviction be
guilty of a misdemeanor. (Ord. 258 § 3, 1957)
10.16.040: PROSECUTION:
It is the duty of the chief of police, his assistants, or marshals of the city
to enforce the provisions of this chapter in accordance with the laws of the
state and the ordinances of this municipal government to cause to be brought
before the police judge of the city, or such other appropriate magistrate as
the law may provide, all persons who violate the provisions of this chapter,
including the engineers or conductors of the rolling stock or other persons
responsible and under whose authority the rolling stock is being operated at
the time and place of the violation. (Ord. 258 § 4, 1957)
10.16.050: OPERATOR DETERMINATION:
If the identity of the responsible party or parties operating rolling stock in
violation of the terms and provisions of this chapter cannot be determined
after reasonable and diligent inquiry on the part of the officer or officers
seeking to enforce the provisions of this chapter, then it is the duty of the
officers to issue or cause to be issued a complaint against the officers of any
company, partnership, association, or corporation who owns or operates the
railroad and the rolling stock within the corporate limits of the city, causing
a copy of the complaint, together with a summons and other legal process, to be
served upon the stationmaster or other person in charge of the railroad or
rolling stock who may be found within the corporate limits of the city. (Ord.
258 § 4, 1957)
CHAPTER 10.20
BICYCLES
(Rep. by Ord. 548, 2014)
CHAPTER 10.24
SEAT BELT USE POLICY
SECTION:
10.24.010: Policy
10.24.020: Procedure
10.24.010: POLICY:
To assure safety of all personnel, safety belts shall be worn by drivers and
passengers in all vehicles owned, leased or rented by the departments at all
times. This also applies to the operation of privately owned or other vehicles,
if used on duty.
Research shows the use of safety belts has a significant effect in reducing the
number of deaths and the severity of injury resulting from traffic crashes. A
law enforcement officer's or fireman's chance of being involved in a motor
vehicle crash is two (2) to ten (10) times greater than that of the general
public. The use of safety restraints reduces this risk and assists officers in
maintaining proper control of their vehicles in pursuit and/or emergency high
speed operations. (Ord. 459, 1998)
10.24.020: PROCEDURE:
   A.   Department personnel shall use the safety belts installed by the
vehicle manufacturer properly adjusted and securely fastened when operating or
riding in any vehicle so equipped if used while on duty.
   B.   Lap belts shall be properly secured in those vehicles equipped with
automatic safety belt systems that require the lap portion of the belt be
manually secured.
   C.   The driver of the vehicle is responsible for ensuring compliance by all
occupants of the vehicle they are operating. Approved child safety restraints
shall be used for all children of age, size or weight for which such restraints
are prescribed by law.
   D.   No person shall operate a departmental vehicle in which any safety belt
in the driver's seating position is inoperable. No person shall be transported
in a seating position in which the safety restoring is inoperable.
   E.   No person shall modify, remove, deactivate or otherwise tamper with the
vehicle safety belts except for vehicle maintenance and repair and not without
the express authorization of the fire chief or the police chief.
   F.   Personnel who discover an inoperable restraint system shall report the
defect to the appropriate supervisor. Prompt action will be taken to replace or
repair the system.
   G.   Any person(s) under arrest and being transported in department vehicle
(s) are required to be secured in the vehicle by a safety belt in all seating
positions for which safety belts are provided by the vehicle manufacturer.
Caution: Prisoners that are handcuffed in front have the ability to release the
handcuffs using the safety restraint's latch plate.
   H.   An officer operating in an undercover capacity may be exempt only if
the officer believes use of the safety belt will compromise their identity.
   I.   When arriving at an emergency call or making a vehicle traffic stop,
the operator may remove the safety restraint just prior to stopping for quick
exit. Caution should be exercised in ensuring that the violator is in fact
going to stop. This prevents becoming involved in a pursuit without the use of
a safety belt. (Ord. 459, 1998)

TITLE 12
STREETS, SIDEWALKS, AND PUBLIC PLACES
Sidewalk Repair   12.04
Curb Lines   12.08

Mary L. Gooding Park   12.20
CHAPTER 12.04
SIDEWALK REPAIR
SECTION:
12.04.010: Authority
12.04.020: Notice
12.04.030: Materials And Methods Generally
12.04.040: Dimensions
12.04.050: Foundations
12.04.060: Concrete; Requirements
12.04.070: Concrete; Mixing Required
12.04.080: Concrete; Laying
12.04.090: Wearing Surface
12.04.100: Protection
12.04.110: Width
12.04.010: AUTHORITY:
The city council may at any time, by an order entered upon its minutes, direct
the construction or repair of any sidewalk within the limits of the city.
(Prior code § 5-101)
12.04.020: NOTICE:
The city clerk shall cause a notice in writing to be issued and served on the
person owning the property fronting upon the proposed improvement, or his
agent, notifying him to make the improvement within the time and in the manner
specified in this chapter. The notice shall direct the owner to construct or
repair the sidewalk within thirty (30) days from the date of service of the
notice; but in case the owner fails or refuses to construct or repair the
sidewalk within the time specified, then the improvements may be made by the
city under the direction of the street overseer who shall keep an account of
the costs of improvements in front of each lot or part of lots where parts of
lots are held in separate ownership and the costs shall be assessed against the
owners of the lots or parts of lots and collected as other taxes. (Prior code §
5-102)
12.04.030: MATERIALS AND METHODS GENERALLY:
All sidewalks shall be constructed so as to conform to the established street
lines and the established grade thereof as the grades are or may be established
by authority of the city. All sidewalks constructed within the limits of the
city shall be made of cement composed of materials and laid and constructed
according to the requirements of sections 12.04.040 through 12.04.100 of this
chapter. (Prior code § 5-103)
12.04.040: DIMENSIONS:
Sidewalks must be constructed with open joints of one-fourth inch (1/4") at
least every twelve feet (12'). They must be four inches (4") deep except on
crossings where they shall be six inches (6"). They shall be built four feet
(4') wide except as otherwise ordered. (Prior code § 5-103)
12.04.050: FOUNDATIONS:
Excavations must be compacted by rolling or ramming. (Prior code § 5-103)
12.04.060: CONCRETE; REQUIREMENTS:
Concrete must contain one part Portland cement, three (3) parts sand, and six
(6) parts broken stone or gravel, the maximum size of the latter to be such as
will pass one and one-half inch (11/2") screen and be rejected by one and one-
fourth inch (11/4") screen. (Prior code § 5-103)
12.04.070: CONCRETE; MIXING REQUIRED:
The sand shall be mixed evenly with the cement before adding the rock, gravel,
or water. (Prior code § 5-103)
12.04.080: CONCRETE; LAYING:
Concrete shall be laid expeditiously in the forms and rammed until free mortar
appears on the surface. No concrete shall be laid when the temperature is below
thirty five degrees Fahrenheit (35°F). (Prior code § 5-103)
12.04.090: WEARING SURFACE:
The wearing surface shall be three-fourths inch (3/4") in thickness on walks
and one and one-half inches (11/2") on crossings. It shall be composed of one
part Portland cement and two (2) parts of sand mixed dry before wetting. It
must be laid while the base is still adhesive and must be a uniform slate
color. It shall be creased in three foot (3') squares each third square to be
directly over the joint in the concrete and extending through it. Forms shall
be thoroughly set and shall not be removed until surface is dry. (Prior code §
5-103)
12.04.100: PROTECTION:
The finished walk must be protected from the weather for at least forty eight
(48) hours. (Prior code § 5-103)
12.04.110: WIDTH:
All sidewalks constructed on the south side of Rail Street between Greenwood
Street and Date Street and on the north side of Rail Street between Greenwood
Street and Birch Street shall be ten feet (10') wide; and on the west side of
Apple Street between Rail Street and the first alley south thereof shall be ten
feet (10') wide; and on the east side of Apple Street between Rail Street and A
Street shall be eight feet (8') wide. (Prior code § 5-104)
CHAPTER 12.08
CURB LINES
SECTION:
12.08.010: Established
12.08.020: Parking Designated
12.08.010: ESTABLISHED:
   A.   The curb lines in the residence district of the city lying south of
Rail Street are fixed and established as follows:
On both sides of the street, fifteen feet (15') from the property line.
   B.   In all residence districts within the city lying north of North Rail
Street the curb lines are fixed and established as follows:
On both sides of the street, thirteen feet (13') from the property line. (Prior
code § 6-101)
12.08.020: PARKING DESIGNATED:
The space on each side of the street lying and being between the curb line and
the property line with the exception of the space occupied by the sidewalk is
designated "the parking". (Prior code § 6-102)
CHAPTER 12.12
OBSTRUCTIONS
SECTION:
12.12.010: Streets, Sidewalks, And Alleys
12.12.020: Railroad Crossings
12.12.010: STREETS, SIDEWALKS, AND ALLEYS:
It is a misdemeanor for any person or persons to obstruct or cause to be
obstructed any of the sidewalks, streets, or alleys in the city by erecting or
maintaining fences, buildings, or other obstacles upon the street, sidewalk, or
alley and continuing the obstruction for the period of thirty (30) days after
written notice from the chief of police to remove same. (Prior code § 4-401)
12.12.020: RAILROAD CROSSINGS:
It is a misdemeanor for any person or persons or any railroad company to
obstruct or cause to be obstructed by cars, locomotive engines, or trains of
cars, any crossing within the city for a length of time greater than ten (10)
minutes. (1981 Code)
CHAPTER 12.16
SNOW REMOVAL
SECTION:
12.16.010: Sidewalk Clearing
12.16.010: SIDEWALK CLEARING:
It is unlawful for any owner of lots or real property within the city or any
tenant, householder, or lessee in possession of any lots or real property
within the city or any person or persons having charge or control of any
property within the corporate limits of the city to suffer, allow, or permit
any ice or snow to be and remain upon any concrete sidewalk which may abut upon
or be contiguous to any lots or real property for a period of time longer than
twenty four (24) hours after the snow has fallen or the ice has accumulated.
(Prior code § 5-201)

VACATION OF PROPERTY
SECTION:
12.17.010: Vacation; Westerly Ten Feet Of South Beverly Street

12.17.010: VACATION; WESTERLY TEN FEET OF SOUTH BEVERLY STREET:
The westerly ten feet (10') of South Beverly Street lying between East B Street
and the alley of block 14 which lies adjacent to Lot 20 in block 14 of the
original town site of Shoshone, the same being a strip ten feet (10') wide and
one hundred twenty feet (120') long, be and the same is hereby vacated and
annulled and all public rights therein renounced. (Ord. 363, 1982)
12.17.020: TITLE TO REVERT TO SANDRA CAMERON:
The title to the property thus vacated shall revert to and be established in
Sandra Cameron, a feme sole, who is the owner of Lot 20 adjacent thereto in
block 14 of the City of Shoshone. (Ord. 363, 1982)
12.17.030: DAMAGES AND PAYMENT; OWNER OF LOT 20 LIABLE:
Within thirty (30) days after the publication hereof, any person claiming to
have been damaged by the vacation of that portion of Beverly Street as
hereinabove stated may file claim for damages with the City Clerk, and any
claims so filed shall, within ten (10) days thereafter, be fixed and determined
by the Mayor and City Council, and if any damages are awarded the same shall be
paid by the owner of said Lot 20; that if no claims are asserted or none
allowed within the time herein fixed, thereafter all claims for damages shall
be without effect and shall not affect the vacation of that portion of Beverly
Street herein provided for. (Ord. 363, 1982)
12.17.040: CONVEYANCE TO SANDRA CAMERON:
The Mayor of the City of Shoshone is hereby authorized and empowered to execute
in the name of said City and deliver to Sandra Cameron, the owner of the
adjacent Lot 20, in block 14 of the City of Shoshone, Idaho, and covering the
property vacated by sections 12.17.010 and 12.17.020 of this chapter, a good
and sufficient deed of conveyance transferring and conveying title to said
vacated portion to the said Sandra Cameron. (Ord. 363, 1982)
12.17.050: VACATION; PORTIONS OF NORTH BEVERLY STREET AND ALLEY:
That portion of North Beverly Street lying north of Little Wood River and south
of a line drawn east and west across North Beverly Street and ten feet (10')
south of the center of the sewer manhole nearest to Little Wood River on North
Beverly, that alley between Little Wood River and a line projected east and
west across the alley which line is two feet (2') north of the south boundary
of Lot 21 in block 4 of Lincoln addition to Shoshone and that area between the
alley in said block 4 and the south portion of North Beverly shown as an alley
or roadway adjacent to Little Wood River on that certain plat of Lincoln
addition to Shoshone with deed of dedication thereon signed by O.J. Brennan,
Frank T. Disney and Fred W. Gooding on May 29, 1909, and recorded in the Office
of the Lincoln County Recorder, said area as shown in said plat adjoins at an
angle Lots 23 and 24 of block 4 in said plat otherwise described as all the
area between said Lots 23 and 24 and Little Wood River, be and the same are
hereby vacated and annulled and all public rights therein renounced. (Ord. 363,
1982)
12.17.060: TITLE TO REVERT TO HOWARD E. ADKINS:
The title to the property thus vacated, the same being generally described as
that portion of North Beverly Street lying between Little Wood River and a line
drawn due east and west across North Beverly Street ten feet (10') south of the
center of the sewer manhole nearest to Little Wood River on North Beverly, that
portion of the alley in block 4 of Lincoln addition to Shoshone lying between
Little Wood River and a line extended due west and two feet (2') north of the
south boundary of lot 21 in said block 4, that area lying between Little Wood
River and lots 23 and 24 shown as a street or alley by that plat of Lincoln
addition to Shoshone on which deed of dedication was signed by O.J. Brennan,
Frank T. Disney and Fred W. Gooding on May 29, 1909, as recorded in the office
of Lincoln County recorder. (Ord. 363, 1982)
12.17.070: DAMAGES AND PAYMENT; OWNER LIABLE:
Within thirty (30) days after the publication hereof any person claiming to
have been damaged by the vacation of that property described in section
12.17.060 of this chapter as herein recited may file claim for damages with the
city clerk, and any claims so filed shall, within ten (10) days thereafter, be
fixed and determined by the mayor and city council, and if any damages are
awarded the same shall be paid by the owner of the area so described; that if
no claims are asserted or none allowed within the time herein fixed, thereafter
all claims for damages shall be without effect and shall not affect the
vacation of the areas so described. (Ord. 363, 1982)
12.17.080: CONVEYANCE TO HOWARD E. ADKINS:
The mayor of the city is hereby authorized and empowered to execute in the name
of said city and deliver to Howard E. Adkins, the owner of the adjacent area in
block 4, Lincoln addition of Shoshone, Idaho, and covering the property vacated
by section 12.17.050 of this chapter, a good and sufficient deed of conveyance
transferring and conveying title to said vacated portion to the said Howard E.
Adkins. (Ord. 363, 1982)
12.17.090: EXPENSES INCIDENT TO VACATED PROPERTY:
All expenses incident to the passage of the ordinance codified herein, the
vacation of lands described therein, and the conveyance as herein provided for,
shall be paid for by the said Howard E. Adkins and Sandra Cameron in equal
shares. (Ord. 363, 1982)
12.17.100: VACATION; PORTION OF WEST F STREET:
The portion of West F Street lying between South Greenwood and South Apple
Street, the same being a strip three hundred feet (300') long and eighty feet
(80') wide be and the same is hereby vacated and annulled and all public rights
therein renounced. (Ord. 454, 1997)
12.17.110: TITLE TO REVERT TO HERSHEL AND SHARON KERNER, ET AL.:

the following parties:
   A.   Hershel And Sharon Kerner: That portion of West F Street adjacent to
lots 11, 12, 13, 14 of block 46 or approximately one hundred twenty feet (120')
long and forty feet (40') to the south of said lots or to the center of West F
Street.
   B.   Idaho Power: That portion of West F Street adjacent to lots 15, 16, 17,
18, 19, 20 of block 46, or approximately one hundred eighty feet (180') long

Street.
   C.   Harrel Thorne: Adjacent to real property owned by Harrel Thorne, three
hundred feet (300') long and forty feet (40') to the north or to the center of
West F Street. (Ord. 454, 1997)
12.17.120: CONVEYANCE TO HERSHEL AND SHARON KERNER, ET AL.:
The mayor is hereby authorized and empowered to execute in the name of said

above vacated property. (Ord. 454, 1997)
12.17.200: VACATION; TRIANGLE PORTION OF SOUTH BEVERLY:
The triangle portion of South Beverly Street as described in schedule A
attached to the ordinance codified herein, and shown on the map in schedule B
attached to the ordinance codified herein, is hereby vacated and annulled and
all public rights therein renounced. (Ord. 489, 2004)
12.17.210: TITLE TO REVERT TO JOHN MCBRIDE:
The title to the property thus vacated shall revert to John McBride or future
owners of said property. Said property shall be attached to lot 1 in block 14
of the original town site. (Ord. 489, 2004)
12.17.220: CONVEYANCE TO JOHN MCBRIDE:
The mayor of the city of Shoshone is hereby authorized and empowered to execute
in the name of said city and deliver to John McBride a good and sufficient deed
of conveyance transferring and conveying title to the above vacated property.
(Ord. 489, 2004)
12.17.230: CONVEYANCE TO LINCOLN COUNTY RECREATIONAL DISTRICT:
Conveyance of real property by quitclaim deed from the City to the Lincoln
County Recreational District for use as a public pool without consideration.
(Ord. 556, 2018)
CHAPTER 12.20
MARY L. GOODING PARK
SECTION:
12.20.010: Hours Of Operation
12.20.020: Vehicles And Animals Prohibited
12.20.030: Violation; Penalty
12.20.010: HOURS OF OPERATION:
The Mary L. Gooding park in the city is open to the lawful and orderly use and
enjoyment of the public between the hours of seven o'clock (7:00) A.M. and
eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. each day of the year and it is closed to use or
occupancy by any person or persons between the hours of eleven o'clock (11:00)
P.M. and seven o'clock (7:00) A.M. unless the person or persons have prior
thereto secured from the city clerk a permit in writing for occupying the park
during other hours. (Ord. 348 § 1, 1980)
12.20.020: VEHICLES AND ANIMALS PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful for any person to bring into the park or to keep or have therein
at any time any animal or vehicle unless authorized by the city council. (Ord.
348 § 2, 1980)
12.20.030: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person in the park between the hours of eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. and
seven o'clock (7:00) A.M. without a written permit from the city clerk or any
person bringing into or having an animal or vehicle in the park without
permission of the city council is guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction
shall be punished by a fine of not less than twenty five dollars ($25.00) or
more than three hundred dollars ($300.00). (Ord. 348 § 3, 1980)
TITLE 13
PUBLIC SERVICES
Water   13.04
Cross Connections   13.06

CHAPTER 13.04
WATER
SECTION:
13.04.010: Connection; Application
13.04.020: Service Determination
13.04.030: Commercial Determination
13.04.040: Meter; Separate Required
13.04.050: Meter; Commercial
13.04.060: Meter; Sale Outside City
13.04.070: Meter; Installation
13.04.080: Transfer
13.04.090: Rates; Meter
13.04.100: Rates; Flat Fee
13.04.110: Rates; Irrigation
13.04.111: Domestic Rates For Water; Adjustment
13.04.112: Water And Sewer Vacation Fee
13.04.120: Rates; Adjustment
13.04.130: Owner Responsibility
13.04.140: Charges; Payable When
13.04.150: Charges; Delinquent
13.04.160: Charges; Deposit
13.04.170: Charges; Turnon And Turnoff
13.04.180: Water Conservation
13.04.010: CONNECTION; APPLICATION:
   A.   Application: Any person, firm or corporation occupying or using
premises abutting any street, avenue or alley along which are laid water mains,
but not connected with water, shall make and sign a written application
therefor on forms furnished by the city clerk, and present the same to the city
clerk or appointed deputies. The charges for making the connection shall be
deposited with the city clerk at the time of making the application and the
rates shall be in the amount of two thousand five hundred dollars ($2,500.00)
plus all costs for labor, materials, and machinery incurred by the city in
connecting such property to the city water system.
   B.   Contents Of Application: The application form provided shall specify
the purpose for which water is required and the location of the premises with
reference to abutting streets, avenues, or alleys; and the applicant shall
therein agree to abide by and conform to the provisions of this chapter and
amendments thereto, and shall agree that the officers and agents of the city
shall have the right at all reasonable times to enter upon the premises of the
applicant for the purpose of inspection of service pipes and equipment and
reading and testing, repairing pipes and meters of the city installed thereon;
provided, however, that if the applicant is not the owner of the premises, the
applicant shall secure the consent of the owner and require the owner to
guarantee the payment of the water rentals and charges.
   C.   Description, Other Information: In addition to the location of the
premises by lot and block number, the applicant shall furnish a description
relative to character of and location of pipes, fixtures, the number of taps,
and other information set forth by the water department.
   D.   Service Pipes: Upon the approval and filing of the application with the
water superintendent and the approval of the connections used therewith, the
applicant is entitled to have service pipes on his premises, if approved by the
water department, and all charges paid, connected with the water main by a
lateral extending from the water main to the property line, and a stopcock,
service box, meter, and meter box installed at convenient places in the street
or upon the premises; all service pipes shall be laid at least four feet (4')
below the surface of the ground.
   E.   Deposit Required: Every person desiring to apply for water service to
the premises occupied by the applicant or under the control of the applicant,
shall deposit with the city an amount not to exceed two (2) months' billing for
water prior to the delivery of water so requested or resuming delivery of water
to said premises if the same has been disconnected for nonpayment of a prior
bill.
In addition to the charges required by sections
8.04.070 and
8.04.080 of this code for the collection of garbage, an amount not to exceed
two (2) months' billing for garbage collection shall be deposited with the city
by every person desiring to apply for water service to the premises occupied by
the applicant or under the control of the applicant prior to the delivery of
water requested or resuming delivery of water to said premises if the same has
been discontinued for nonpayment of a prior bill.
   F.   Deposit Applied To Unpaid Bill: Said sums shall be collected as a
deposit to ensure the timely payment for water and garbage services and may be
applied to payment of any unpaid bill for water delivery to premises or garbage
collected therefrom after the date that such bill becomes delinquent. (Ord. 505
§ 1, 2006: Ord. 475 § 1, 2001: Ord. 388, 1987: Ord. 290 § 1, 1969: prior code §
1-905)
13.04.020: SERVICE DETERMINATION:
The rate to be charged for water furnished through a meter to buildings
occupied and used for both residence and business purposes shall be determined
by the city council upon proper investigation and classification under one or
the other of the meter rates specified in this chapter; provided, that all
rates shall be uniform and that the council shall ascertain whether water is
used chiefly for domestic or business purposes on the premises and shall be
governed accordingly. (Prior code § 1-906)
13.04.030: COMMERCIAL DETERMINATION:
The definition of "commercial buildings" or "businesses" as used in this
chapter for the purposes of this chapter includes all businesses or business
buildings occupied by businesses which are required to obtain federal, state,
county, or municipal licenses, or any one of the licenses, or any other
business which is being conducted within the city for profit, including public
and private hotels and apartment houses. In addition to the foregoing
definition, all state, county, school district, or any other taxing unit under
the laws of the state is deemed to be a commercial business within the
definition of this section but reserving and specifically excluding churches
within the corporate limits of the city which shall not in any event be charged
for use of water excepting, however, such exemption of churches shall be
applied only to the land and immediate area wherein a church is situated or
located. (Prior code § 1-909)
13.04.040: METER; SEPARATE REQUIRED:
Every building and its necessary outbuildings supplied with water shall have a
separate tap and service pipe connected with the main and the owner thereof is
liable for the tapping fees and other charges to become due or due thereon;
provided, that if the applicant for the water tap and service is not the owner
of the premises, the owner shall agree in writing to abide by the provisions of
this chapter. (Prior code § 1-907)
13.04.050: METER; COMMERCIAL:
Every commercial building or commercial business within the corporate limits of
the city shall be furnished water by the city, upon request of the owners,
renters, or lessees of the commercial buildings or of the businesses, by the
use of a water meter installed in accordance with the provisions of this
chapter and at the rate as defined in the schedule attached as exhibit A to the
ordinance codified herein and water will not be furnished by the city to any
commercial buildings or businesses except by and through the use of a water
meter as specified in this section; where the business or commercial buildings
need or use water for irrigation purposes, then irrigation water shall be
provided by the city on the basis of a payment schedule, attached as exhibit A
to the ordinance codified herein, the purpose of this chapter being to require
the city to furnish water to commercial buildings and businesses by and through
the use of a water meter for any and all purposes of which a commercial
business or building would use water, save and except water used only for
irrigation purposes in order to grow plants or plant life. This section is not
exclusive of the right of resident owners to make application in accordance
with the provisions of section
13.04.010 of this chapter for a water meter to be placed on residential
dwellings for domestic use and the provisions of this section shall not in any
way limit or restrict the right of a residential owner in making application
for a meter to be installed at the owner's residence or dwelling within the
corporate limits of the city. The payment schedule attached as exhibit A to the
ordinance codified herein may be altered at any time by the Shoshone city
council by appropriate resolution. (Ord. 480, 2002: prior code § 1-908)
13.04.060: METER; SALE OUTSIDE CITY:
It is provided that in all instances where the city is selling water outside
its corporate limits or where waters sold by the city are being applied outside
of the corporate limits of the city, then such water shall be sold only by and
through the use of a water meter as specified and designated in this chapter.
The rates for furnishing water by the city to water users outside the corporate
limits of the city shall be an amount fixed by the city council at any regular
meeting as may be determined from time to time but in no event shall such water
charges to users outside the corporate limits of the city be lower than the
minimum schedule for water users within the city as specified in this chapter.
(Prior code § 1-910)
13.04.070: METER; INSTALLATION:
All meters shall be furnished by the city and shall not exceed three-fourths
inch (3/4") connections. When larger meters are demanded, the owner of the
property shall pay to the city forty dollars ($40.00) plus all the cost of
materials and labor over forty dollars ($40.00), but the ownership of the
meters always remains with the city along with their right of control. (Prior
code § 1-911)
13.04.080: TRANSFER:
In the event of transfer or change of possession of property, the transferee
shall make a new application for water or may have the water turned off if
service has not already been discontinued. The fee of fifty dollars ($50.00),
provided from section
13.04.010 of this chapter, is not payable when lateral connections have already
been installed under a previous application for the same service but new
applications thereon shall be accompanied by payment of the service fee of one
dollar ($1.00) for turning on the water if service has been discontinued, and
all unpaid water rates, rentals, fees, and charges against such service if the
same has previously been discontinued for nonpayment of bills. (Prior code § 1-
912)
13.04.090: RATES; METER:
Where water is furnished by the city by meter, the charge therefor against the
owner of the property is a minimum of two dollars ($2.00) for the first one
thousand (1,000) gallons. For water used in excess of one thousand (1,000)
gallons, and not exceeding ten thousand (10,000) gallons, the charge is seventy
five cents ($0.75) for each thousand gallons. For water used in excess of ten
thousand (10,000) gallons and not exceeding twenty thousand (20,000) gallons,
the charge is sixty cents ($0.60) for each thousand gallons. For all water used
in excess of twenty thousand (20,000) gallons but less than forty thousand
(40,000) gallons, the charge is forty five cents ($0.45) for every thousand
gallons. For all water used in excess of forty thousand (40,000) gallons but
less than sixty thousand (60,000) gallons, the charge is thirty five cents
($0.35) for every thousand gallons. For all water used in excess of sixty
thousand (60,000) gallons but less than one hundred thousand (100,000) gallons,
the charge is thirty cents ($0.30) for every thousand gallons. For all water
used in excess of one hundred thousand (100,000) gallons, the charge is twenty
five cents ($0.25) for each thousand gallons. (Prior code § 1-913)
13.04.100: RATES; FLAT FEE:
Water will be furnished by the city to single private dwellings at the rate of
three dollars seventy five cents ($3.75) per month and for each additional
family using water from a private dwelling, three dollars seventy five cents
($3.75) per month. All flat rate water charges are payable in advance;
provided, further, that when the water charge is due for private dwellings and
additional families using water from private dwellings and not paid before five
o'clock (5:00) P.M. on the tenth day of the month in advance, the city clerk
shall assess a ten percent (10%) penalty on each private dwelling and/or
additional family using water from a private dwelling. (Ord. 288 § 1, 1968:
prior code § 1-914)
13.04.110: RATES; IRRIGATION:
Where water is furnished by the city for irrigation from deep wells, there is a
charge therefor at the rate of five dollars ($5.00) per season per lot;
provided, however, that where lots are taxed for Shoshone ditch water, the
charge for deep well water delivered thereto for irrigation is three dollars
($3.00) per lot per season. The charges are effective for the 1975 irrigation
season and thereafter, until altered. For this chapter, a lot is deemed to be
three thousand six hundred (3,600) square feet. (Ord. 328 § 1, 1975: prior code
§ 1-915A)
13.04.111: DOMESTIC RATES FOR WATER; ADJUSTMENT:
The city council may in regular session hereafter alter or raise the charges
for city water used for domestic purposes to a reasonable amount by resolution
duly adopted. (Ord. 378, 1986)
13.04.112: WATER AND SEWER VACATION FEE:
   A.   A reduced fee for sewer and water service to residential properties in
the city is available for residential properties, which shall be vacant for a
period of time not less than three (3) months.
   B.   An individual requesting the vacation sewer and water rate shall make
application for said rate to the city on a form to be provided by the city
clerk.
   C.   Sewer and water vacation rate shall be fifteen dollars ($15.00) per
month.
   D.   All applicants for a vacation rate shall certify that the residential
property for which the vacation rate is requested will be vacated, and not used
by any individuals, during the period requested. Any individual who violates
the provisions of this section regarding the nonuse of the property for which
the vacation rate has been granted, shall result in the full water and sewer
and monthly fee being imposed for the period in which a violation has been
discovered.
   E.   If an application is made for a water and sewer vacation rate to begin
on a date other than the beginning of the normal monthly billing cycle, the
city clerk shall prorate the vacation fee for the period of time from the date
requested by the applicant to begin the vacation fee and the date of the next
normal monthly billing cycle.
   F.   The city clerk shall have the power to approve or deny all applications
for sewer and water vacation rates.
   G.   An individual whose application for sewer and water vacation has been
denied shall have the right to appeal such denial to the city council by filing
a written notice of appeal no later than ten (10) days after the date of the
denial of the application. The city council shall hear the applicant's appeal
no later than the next regularly scheduled meeting after the date of the
applicant's appeal being filed.
   H.   The sewer and water vacation rate may be amended by the city council by
resolution. (Ord. 461, 1999 1 )
 
Notes
1 1. This ordinance shall be effective August 15, 1999.
13.04.120: RATES; ADJUSTMENT:
The city council may in any regular session of the council hereafter alter or
raise charges to a reasonable amount by resolution duly adopted. (Ord. 328 § 1,
1975: prior code § 1-915B)
13.04.130: OWNER RESPONSIBILITY:
The property owner is held responsible for the payment of all water rentals and
for all bills, except for business, and in the event that any water bills or
statements are not paid within the required time as set out in section
13.04.150 of this chapter, then the water shall be cut off and a charge of one
dollar ($1.00) added to the delinquent charge before the water is turned on
again. (Prior code § 1-916)
13.04.140: CHARGES; PAYABLE WHEN:
All water charges are payable at the office of the city clerk in current lawful
money. (Prior code § 1-917)
13.04.150: CHARGES; DELINQUENT:
   A.   All water rates and other charges are due and payable at the office of
the city clerk during office hours between the first and tenth days of each and
every month for the last preceding month, excepting flat rates, which are
payable in advance at the same time and place. Such accounts become delinquent
at four thirty o'clock (4:30) P.M. on the tenth day of the month if not paid as
described in this section. If such delinquent charges become sixty (60) days
overdue, the water superintendent shall shut off the water from all premises on
which the charges for water, sewer or garbage collection have not been paid.
   B.   Failure to receive a monthly statement from the city clerk shall not
extend the time of payment as provided in this section, nor justify
postponement of the time for shutting off the water. The city officers charged
with the duty of collecting water rates under this chapter shall not be
required to make personal demand therefor; provided, that the services rendered
by the city shall not be discontinued until the city has complied with the
procedure for notice and hearing as specified in section 13.08.730 of this
title. (Ord. 388, 1987: Ord. 310A, 1981: prior code § 1-918)
13.04.160: CHARGES; DEPOSIT:
The city treasurer shall credit all sums received from the city clerk as
provided in this chapter in the fund known as the water works fund, and
disbursements shall be made therefrom for the office of superintendent of
waterworks on order of the city council by warrants as in other cases. (Prior
code § 1-919)
13.04.170: CHARGES; TURNON AND TURNOFF:
A turnoff fee in the amount of ten dollars ($10.00) shall be charged to the
customer whose water service is disconnected for violation of rules or
nonpayment of bills; and further service shall not be rendered to the customer
until ten dollar ($10.00) turnon fee and all delinquent bills and other charges
are paid in full and new and further deposits are placed with the city as a
guarantee of prompt payment of future bills. (Ord. 388, 1987: prior code § 1-
920)
13.04.180: WATER CONSERVATION:
   A.   Stage 1; Sprinkling: The city reserves the right to regulate the use of
water for sprinkling and irrigation purposes and the city council may at any
time hereafter, by resolution adopted in regular session, raise, alter or lower
the penalties herein provided for improper use of water for sprinkling and
irrigation purposes and the water superintendent shall give notice by
publication of any restrictions on the use of water for such purposes and
further notices shall be given thereof to consumers with the next monthly
statement rendered by the city clerk, and thereafter any consumer using or
permitting water to be used for sprinkling or irrigation purposes except as
permitted in such notice, shall be subject to a penalty.
It is the duty of the water superintendent, whenever the consumption of water
threatens to exceed the capacity of the pumping system, to report such
condition to the mayor and council in order that the use of water for
sprinkling and irrigation may be restricted.
   B.   Minimum Standards: The following minimum standards are considered the
foundation to "best practices of water use". These standards are in effect from
the adoption hereof:
      1.   Increase public awareness of the water supply situation and provide
educational materials about best practices of water use.
      2.   Encourage the entire community to conserve water wherever possible.
      3.   No eating establishment, restaurant, hotel, cafe, cafeterias, etc.,
shall serve drinking water unless expressly requested by a patron and will
display notice of such policy.
      4.   Hotels will provide notice of declared water conservation program
and encourage conservation practices.
      5.   All public facilities (includes city, county, state, federal and
schools) not on automated systems, will limit irrigation to three (3) days a
week.
      6.   Vehicles will be washed only on the scheduled irrigation day.
      7.   Landscape irrigation is restricted to the following schedule:
         a.   Even numbered addresses: Will water on even numbered calendar
days.
         b.   Odd numbered addresses: Will water on odd numbered calendar days.
No one will water on the thirty first day of a month.
         c.   Premises with no street address, such as a median: Monday,
Wednesday, Friday.
      8.   Watering will only be allowed on appropriate irrigation days from
six o'clock (6:00) A.M. to ten o'clock (10:00) A.M. and five o'clock (5:00)
P.M. to ten o'clock (10:00) P.M.
Automated sprinkler systems begin on scheduled day after ten o'clock (10:00)
P.M. and run through cycle.
      9.   Outdoor landscape watering with a drip irrigation system or handheld
container is allowed at any time.
      10.   All irrigation systems must be maintained in a manner that promotes
efficient watering and limits leaks or damage to the system that would allow
flow of water beyond property lines.
      11.   No open hoses are allowed.
   C.   Additional Stage 1-3 Restrictions: When deemed appropriate, the city
council may move to additional restrictions as outlined in stages 1-3.
      1.   Stage 1:
         a.   No water customer shall apply water to impervious surfaces such
as streets, sidewalks, patios, decks, etc.
         b.   Landscape irrigation two (2) days per week on designated days:
            (1)   Public facilities are restricted to two (2) days a week.
            (2)   Even numbered addresses: Tuesday, Saturday.
            (3)   Odd numbered addresses: Wednesday, Sunday.
            (4)   Premises with no street address, such as a median: Monday,
Friday.
      2.   Stage 2:
         a.   No water customer shall apply water to impervious surfaces such
as streets, sidewalks, patios, decks, etc.
         b.   Landscape irrigation one day per week on designated days:
            (1)   Public facilities are restricted to one day a week.
            (2)   Even numbered addresses: Tuesday.
            (3)   Odd numbered addresses: Friday.
            (4)   Premises with no street address, such as a median: Monday.
      3.   Stage 3:
         a.   No water customer shall apply water to impervious surfaces such
as streets, sidewalks, patios, decks, etc.
         b.   Indoor use may be reduced by a percentage to be determined by
city council.
         c.   Landscape irrigation two (2) days per month on designated days:
            (1)   Public facilities are restricted to one day a week during the
first and third weeks of the month.
            (2)   Even numbered addresses: Second and fourth Tuesday.
            (3)   Odd numbered addresses: First and third Friday.
            (4)   Premises with no street address, such as a median: Second and
fourth Monday.
   D.   Additional Restrictions During Any Stage: Based upon evaluations of the
expected yield and projected demands the city council may impose additional
restrictions on water use during any stage up to and including, but not limited
to, any of the following:
      1.   No additional water connections to the system allowed moratorium on
building permits.
      2.   Outdoor water prohibited except for large trees with trunks of at
least six inches (6") in diameter.
      3.   Operation of water features prohibited.
      4.   Filling or refilling of water features, pools or ponds prohibited.
   E.   Duration Of Restrictions: Regular evaluations of the expected yield and
projected demands to determine whether it is necessary to continue the water
use restrictions. If water supply conditions warrant, restrictions may be
either downgraded or withdrawn subject to city council approval by resolution.
   F.   Exceptions: Water customers may use water essential to protect the
general public health, safety, or welfare. Irrigation systems may be operated
at any time for maintenance purposes (not to exceed 10 minutes per station).
Customers may apply for relief from the water schedule for purposes of
establishing a new lawn not to exceed three (3) months.
   G.   Alternate Water Management Plans: A water customer may request relief
from applicable restrictions by filing an alternative water management plan
with the city council. The city will provide customers with the ability to
design water management alternatives that give customers flexibility in meeting
the restrictions while achieving maximum conservation goals. The city must give
approval to the plan and may require periodic reporting and posted notice of
alternate water management plan.
   H.   Violations And Fines:
      1.   Each water customer shall be responsible for compliance with this
section with respect to the water customer's premises, and shall be responsible
for applicable fines for noncompliance with this section. In the event of an
alleged violation of this section, proof of the existence of a declared water
shortage and proof of any violation of any restriction set forth in this
section, together with proof that the violation originated at any water
customer's premises, shall constitute a rebuttable presumption that the water
customer is responsible for the violation.
      2.   Fines through stage 2:
         a.   First violation: Written warning.
         b.   Second violation: Written notice and add a forty dollar ($40.00)
fine to the water bill for the premises.
         c.   Third violation: Written notice and add an eighty dollar ($80.00)
fine to the water bill for the premises.
         d.   Fourth violation and subsequent: Written notice and add a one
hundred twenty dollar ($120.00) fine to the water bill for the premises.
      3.   Fines through stage 3:
         a.   First violation: Written notice and add an eighty dollar ($80.00)
fine to the water bill for the premises.
         b.   Second violation: Written notice and add a one hundred sixty
dollar ($160.00) fine to the water bill for the premises.
         c.   Third violation and subsequent: Written notice and add a two
hundred forty dollar ($240.00) fine to the water bill for the premises.
      4.   Any fine assessed shall be added to the customer's water bill.
      5.   Any appeal of a fine imposed may be appealed within fifteen (15)
days of the billing date through the city council. Appeals must be in writing
addressed to the city clerk of Shoshone.
      6.   Written warning or notice shall be delivered in person to the
customer's premises by leaving it with a person at the premises or posted on
the front door if no one is present to accept it. (Ord. 540, 2013: Ord. 495 §
1, 2005: Ord. 378, 1986: prior code § 1-921)
CHAPTER 13.06
CROSS CONNECTIONS
SECTION:
13.06.010: Purpose Of Provisions
13.06.020: Definitions
13.06.030: Backflow Protection Required
13.06.040: Service Requirements
13.06.050: Categories Designated
13.06.060: Violation; Penalty
13.06.010: PURPOSE OF PROVISIONS:
The purpose of this chapter is to protect the public health of domestic water
users receiving their water supply from the city. (Ord. 352 § 1(A), 1981)
13.06.020: DEFINITIONS:
BACKFLOW: The flow of nonpotable water, liquids, gases, or other foreign
substances into the pipes of a potable water system from any source or sources.
BACKFLOW PREVENTION DEVICE: The device to counteract back pressure or to
prevent back siphonage.
CROSS CONNECTION: An actual or potential connection or structural arrangement
between a public or a consumer potable water system in any other source or
system through which it is possible to introduce into any part of the potable
system used water, industrial fluid, gas or substance other than the intended
potable water with which the system is supplied. Bypass arrangements, jumper
connections, removable sections, swivel or changeover devices, and any other
temporary or permanent devices which or because of which backflow can or may
occur are cross connections. (Ord. 352 § 1(B), 1981)
13.06.030: BACKFLOW PROTECTION REQUIRED:
No domestic water service connection shall be installed or maintained unless
the water supply is protected by backflow prevention devices as required by the
rules and regulations of the Idaho department of health and welfare, as the
same now exists or may hereafter be amended or supplemented. Any cross
connection now existing or hereafter installed is declared a public nuisance
and shall be abated. (Ord. 352 § 1(C), 1981)
13.06.040: SERVICE REQUIREMENTS:
Service to any property, landowner, or water consumer receiving a water supply
from the city's water system shall be contingent upon compliance with all the
requirements of the rules and regulations of the Idaho department of health and
welfare and of this chapter pertaining to cross connections. Service shall be
discontinued to any premises, water consumer, or property owner for failure to
comply with such regulations of the Idaho department of health and welfare and
of this chapter pertaining to cross connections, and any discontinued service
will not be reestablished until the city or its designated agent has approved
compliance by that particular premises or water consumer or landowner. (Ord.
352 § 1(D), 1981)
13.06.050: CATEGORIES DESIGNATED:
The following types of facilities will fall into one of the above categories
where a backflow prevention device is required to protect the city water
system. A backflow prevention device shall be installed at these facilities
unless the city supervisor and/or state health officer determine that no hazard
exists:
   A.   Hospitals, mortuaries, clinics;
   B.   Laboratories;
   C.   Sewage treatment plants;
   D.   Food or beverage processing plants;
   E.   Chemical plants using a water process;
   F.   Petroleum processing or storage plants;
   G.   Radioactive material processing plants and/or nuclear reactors;
   H.   Others as specified by the health officer;
   I.   Other premises where backflow prevention devices are reasonably
required to protect the municipal system. (Ord. 352 § 1(E), 1981)
13.06.060: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person who violates, disobeys, omits, neglects, refuses to comply with, or
resists the enforcement of any of the provisions of this chapter or chapter
13.08 of this title is guilty of a misdemeanor. (Ord. 352 § 1(F), 1981)
