I. GENERALLY
13.08.010: APPLICABILITY OF PROVISIONS:
These rules and regulations and rates are to be part of the contract between
the city and every individual, firm, or corporation using or applying for the
use of sewer service within the area to be served by the city, and every
individual, firm, or corporation agrees in making applications for sewer
service to be bound thereby. (Ord. 310, 1971)
13.08.020: RULES ADOPTED:
The rules and regulations and rates specified in this chapter are adopted by
the city council as of August 3, 1971, and in effect as of January 1, 1972, and
are promulgated in compliance and in conformance with this chapter and the
statutes of the state. (Ord. 310, 1971)
13.08.030: SYSTEM DESIGNATED:
   A.   The city owns and operates a municipal sewer system and lagoon type
sewage treatment plants composed of:
      1.   Concrete, cement-asbestos, or approved plastic service connection
lines from property lines discharging into collector sewer pipelines;
      2.   Concrete pipe and cement-asbestos collector sewer lines discharging
into;
      3.   Concrete or reinforced concrete pipe trunk sewer lines;
all provided with standard precast or cast in place concrete manholes using
cast iron rings and covers. Sewer trunk lines will discharge into aerated
lagoon type treatment facility with a design capacity of two thousand (2,000)
population equivalent.
   B.   Sewer enters the lagoons through an eight inch (8") pressure line.
   C.   The lagoons are interconnected and will be operated in series and
require very little maintenance or operation labor or cost other than
inspection, mowing weeds along the dikes, fence repair, and electric power for
aerators.
   D.   Sewer lines are laid mostly on self-cleaning grades with sewage lift
stations placed where necessary to provide sewage facilities for all homes and
businesses where feasible.
   E.   Monthly sewer service charges are based on the volume of sewage
actually discharged into the sewers, as estimated in relation to other metered
users. Sewage with other than normal domestic characteristics is evaluated and
monthly service charges are adjusted to conform to the equivalent of normal
domestic sewage.
   F.   The facilities specified in this section are designated as the sewer
system. (Ord. 310 Regulation I § 1, 1971)
13.08.040: PURPOSE:
The city owns and operates the sewer system for the purpose of supplying the
city and its inhabitants with:
   A.   An adequate and safe means of collecting and disposing of sanitary
sewage wastes;
   B.   A means of protecting health, welfare, and safety of the public by
providing such services in lieu of individual septic tanks and field drainage
systems or drilled drainage holes which do not function satisfactorily and
because of possible pollution of underground waters caused by individual sewer
septic tank systems. (Ord. 310 Regulation I § 2, 1971)
13.08.050: OPERATION AS A UTILITY:
It is deemed necessary and advisable and to the best interest of the city and
to the inhabitants that the sewer system be operated as one utility so that
revenues received from the operation will be available to pay indebtedness
against the sewer system. (Ord. 310 Regulation I § 3, 1971)
13.08.060: DEFINITIONS:
Unless the context specifically indicates otherwise, the meanings of the terms
used in this chapter are as follows:
BOD OR BIOCHEMICAL OXYGEN DEMAND: The quantity of oxygen utilized in the
biochemical oxidation of organic matter under standard laboratory procedure in
five (5) days at twenty degrees centigrade (20°C) expressed in milligrams per
liter.
BUILDING DRAIN: That part of the lowest horizontal piping of a drainage system
which receives the discharge from soil, waste, and other drainage pipes inside
the walls of the building and conveys it to the building sewer beginning five
feet (5') outside the inner face of the building wall.
BUILDING SEWER: The extension from the building drain to the point of
connection with the public sewer.
CITY: The city of Shoshone, Lincoln County, Idaho, or its authorized or
designated agent, representative, or deputy thereto.
GARBAGE: Solid waste from domestic and commercial preparation, cooking, and
dispensing of food, and from the handling, storage, or sale of produce.
INDUSTRIAL WASTES: The liquid wastes from industrial manufacturing processes,
trade, or business as distinct from sanitary sewage.
MULTIPLE BUILDING DEVELOPMENT: Includes the various types of developments that
would have common or joint ownership areas such as condominiums, townhouses,
mobile home parks or courts, shopping centers, etc.
NATURAL OUTLET: Any outlet into a watercourse, pond, ditch, lake, or other body
of surface or ground water.
PERSON: Any individual, firm, company, association, society, corporation, or
group.
pH: The logarithm of the reciprocal of the weight of hydrogen ions in grams per
liter of solution.
PROPERLY SHREDDED GARBAGE: The wastes from the preparation, cooking, and
dispensing of food that has been shredded to such a degree that all particles
will be carried freely under the flow conditions normally prevailing in public
sewers with no particle greater than one-half inch (1/2") in dimension.
PUBLIC SEWER: A sewer in which all owners of abutting properties have equal
rights and controlled by public authority.
SANITARY SEWER: A sewer which carries sewage and to which storm, surface, and
ground waters are not intentionally admitted.
SERVICE CONNECTION: The point at which the building sewer connects to the
public sewer.
SEWAGE: A combination of water carried wastes from residences, business
buildings, institutions, and industrial establishments.
SEWER: Any pipe or conduit for carrying sewage.
SEWER USER: Any individual, firm, company, association, society, corporation,
or group who has connected to the sewerage system.
SEWERAGE TREATMENT PLANT: Any arrangement of devices and structures used for
treating sewage.
SEWERAGE WORKS: All facilities for collecting, pumping, treating, and disposing
of sewage.
SHALL: Is mandatory; "may" is permissive.
SLUG: Any discharge of water, sewage, or industrial waste which in
concentration of any given constituent or in quantity of flow exceeds for any
period of duration longer than fifteen (15) minutes more than five (5) times
the average twenty four (24) hour concentration of flows during normal
operation.
SUSPENDED SOLIDS: Solids that either float on the surface of, or are in
suspension of, water, sewage, or other liquids and which are removable by
laboratory filtering. (Ord. 310 Regulation II, 1971)
II. USE
13.08.070: USE GENERALLY:
The use of the public sewers of the city shall be in accordance with the
regulations set out in sections
13.08.080 through 13.08.170 of this chapter. (Ord. 310 Regulation III, 1971)
13.08.080: DISCHARGE; UNPOLLUTED WATER:
No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any stormwater, surface
water, groundwater, roof water, subsurface drainage, uncontaminated cooling
water, or unpolluted industrial process waters to any sanitary sewer. (Ord. 310
Regulation III § A, 1971)
13.08.090: DISCHARGE; HAZARDOUS MATERIALS:
No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any of the following
described waters or waste to any public sewers:
   A.   Any gasoline, benzene, naphtha, fuel oil, or other flammable or
explosive liquid, solid, or gas;
   B.   Any waters or wastes containing toxic or poisonous solids, liquids, or
gases in sufficient quantity, either singly or by interaction with other
wastes, to injure or interfere with any sewage treatment process, constitute a
hazard to humans or animals, create a public nuisance, or create any hazard in
the receiving waters of the sewage treatment plant, including, but not limited
to, cyanides in excess of two milligrams per liter (2 mg/l) as CN in the wastes
as discharged to the public sewer;
   C.   Any waters or wastes having a pH lower than 5.5 or having any other
corrosive property capable of causing damage or hazards to structures,
equipment, or personnel of the sewage works;
   D.   Solids or viscous substances in quantities or of such size capable of
causing damage or hazards to the flow in sewers, or other interference with the
proper operation of the sewage works such as, but not limited to, ashes,
cinders, sand, mud, straw, shavings, metal, glass, rags, feathers, tar,
plastics, wood, unground garbage, whole blood, paunch manure, hair and
fleshings, entrails, and paper dishes, cups, milk containers, towels, clothes,
etc., either whole or ground by garbage grinders. (Ord. 310 Regulation III § B,
1971)
13.08.100: DISCHARGE; HARMFUL MATERIALS:
No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged the following described
substances, materials, waters, or waste if it appears likely in the opinion of
the city that the wastes can harm either the sewers, sewage treatment process
or equipment, have an adverse effect on the receiving stream, or can otherwise
endanger life, limb, public property, or constitute a nuisance. In forming its
opinion as to the acceptability of these wastes, the city will give
consideration to such factors as the quantities of subject wastes in relation
to flows and velocities in the sewers, nature of the sewage treatment process,
capacity of the sewage treatment plant, degree of treatability of wastes in the
sewage treatment plant, and other pertinent factors. The substances prohibited
are:
   A.   Any liquid or vapor having a temperature higher than one hundred fifty
degrees Fahrenheit (150°F) (65 degrees centigrade);
   B.   Any water or waste containing fats, wax, grease, or oils, whether
emulsified or not, in excess of one hundred milligrams per liter (100 mg/l) or
containing substances which may solidify or become viscous at temperatures
between thirty two (32) and one hundred fifty degrees Fahrenheit (150°F) (0 and
65 degrees centigrade);
   C.   Any garbage that has not been properly shredded; the installation or
operation of any garbage grinder equipped with a motor of three-fourths (3/4)
horsepower or greater shall be subjected to the review and approval of the
city;
   D.   Any water or wastes containing strong acid iron pickling wastes or
concentrated plating solutions, whether neutralized or not;
   E.   Any water or wastes containing iron, chromium, copper, zinc, and
similar objectionable or toxic substances; or wastes exerting any excessive
chlorine requirement, to such degree that any such material received in the
composite sewage at the sewage treatment works exceeds the limits established
by the city for such materials;
   F.   Any waters or wastes containing phenols or other taste or odor
producing substances in such concentration exceeding limits which may be
established by the city as necessary, after treatment of the composite sewage,
to meet the requirements of the state, federal, or other public agencies of
jurisdiction for such discharge to the receiving waters;
   G.   Any radioactive wastes or isotopes of such half-life or concentration
as may exceed limits established by the city in compliance with applicable
state or federal regulations;
   H.   Any waters or wastes having a pH in excess of 9.5;
   I.   Materials which exert or cause:
      1.   Unusual concentrations of inert suspended solids, such as, but not
limited to, fuller's earth, lime slurries, and lime residues or of dissolved
solids, such as, but not limited to, sodium chloride and sodium sulfate;
      2.   Excessive discolorations, such as, but not limited to, dye wastes
and vegetable tanning solutions;
      3.   Unusual BOD, chemical oxygen demand, or chlorine requirements in
such quantities as to constitute a significant load on the sewage treatment
works;
      4.   Unusual volume or flow or concentration of wastes constituting slugs
as defined in this chapter;
   J.   Waters or wastes containing substances which are not amenable to
treatment or reduction by the sewage treatment processes employed or are
amenable to treatment only to such a degree that the sewage treatment plant
effluent cannot meet the requirements of other agencies having jurisdiction
over discharge to the receiving water;
   K.   Crankcase oil and transmission grease from garages and service stations
and dirt from car washes. (Ord. 310 Regulation III § C, 1971)
13.08.110: DISCHARGE; DETERMINATION:
If any waters or wastes are discharged, or are proposed to be discharged, to
the public sewers, which waters contain the substances or possess the
characteristics enumerated in section 13.08.090 of this chapter, and which, in
the judgment of the city, may have a deleterious effect upon the sewage works,
processes, equipment, or receiving waters, or which otherwise create a hazard
to life or constitute a public nuisance, the city may:
   A.   Reject the wastes;
   B.   Require pretreatment to an acceptable condition for discharge to the
public sewers;
   C.   Require control over the quantities and rates of discharge;
   D.   If the city permits the pretreatment or equalization of waste flows,
the design and installation of the plants and equipment shall be subject to the
review and approval of the city and subject to the requirements of all
applicable codes, ordinances, and laws. (Ord. 310 Regulation III § D, 1971)
13.08.120: INTERCEPTORS REQUIRED:
Grease, oil, and sand interceptors shall be provided when, in the opinion of
the city, they are necessary for the proper handling of liquid wastes and
containing grease in excessive amounts, or any flammable wastes, sand, or other
harmful ingredients; except that such interceptors shall not be required for
private living quarters or dwelling units. Crankcase oil and transmission
grease from garages and service stations shall be drained into containers and
properly disposed of other than in the sewer. Special grease and sand traps or
pits shall be provided in garages and service stations to catch oil, grease,
and sand that may be accidentally spilled or washed off from cars. All
interceptors shall be of a type and capacity as approved by the city, and shall
be located as to be readily and easily accessible for easy cleaning and
inspection. (Ord. 310 Regulation III § F, 1971)
13.08.130: PRETREATMENT MAINTENANCE:
Where preliminary treatment or flow equalizing facilities are provided for any
waters or wastes, they shall be maintained continuously in satisfactory and
effective operation by the owner at his expense. (Ord. 310 Regulation III § G,
1971)
13.08.140: MANHOLE REQUIRED WHEN:
When required by the city, the owner of any property serviced by a building
sewer carrying industrial wastes shall install a suitable central manhole
together with the necessary meters and other appurtenances in the building
sewer to facilitate observation, sampling, and measurement of the wastes. Such
manholes, when required, shall be accessible and safely locked and shall be
constructed in accordance with a plan approved by the city. The manhole shall
be installed by the owner at his expense and shall be maintained by him so as
to be safe and accessible at all times. (Ord. 310 Regulation III § H, 1971)
13.08.150: TEST STANDARDS:
All measurements, tests, and analyses of the characteristics of the waters and
wastes to which reference is made in this chapter shall be determined in
accordance with the latest edition of "Standard Methods For The Examination Of
Water And Wastewater", published by the American Public Health Association, and
shall be determined at the control manhole provided or upon suitable samples
taken at the control manhole. In the event that no special manhole has been
required, the control manhole shall be considered to be the nearest downstream
manhole in the public sewer to a point at which the building sewer is
connected. Sampling shall be carried out by customarily accepted methods to
reflect the effect of the constituents upon the sewage works and to determine
the existence of hazards to life, limb, and property. (Ord. 310 Regulation III
§ I, 1971)
13.08.160: SPECIAL AGREEMENTS:
No statement contained in this chapter shall be construed as preventing any
special agreement between the city and any industrial concern whereby any
industrial waste of unusual strength or character may be accepted by the city
for treatment, subject to payment therefor by the industrial concern. (Ord. 310
Regulation III § J, 1971)
13.08.170: COMPLIANCE WITH PROVISIONS:
Any property owner or sewer user violating the provisions of sections 13.08.060
through 13.08.160 of this chapter shall upon notice by the city immediately
install such preliminary treatment through separators, traps, and/or chemical,
physical, or biochemical processes as will make and assure that the sewage
contributed from such property or premises will meet the requirements of this
chapter. (Ord. 310 Regulation III § K, 1971)
III. CONSTRUCTION REQUIREMENTS
13.08.180: PERMIT REQUIRED:
No connection shall be made to a municipally owned sewer line except in
compliance with city ordinances and regulations and under an authorization or
permit issued by competent authority of the city. (Ord. 310 Regulation IV § 1,
1971)
13.08.190: INSPECTION:
No connection to a municipally owned sewer shall be made and sewage permitted
to flow through such connection except pursuant to inspection of and approval
issued by an official invested by the city with authority to inspect, reject,
and/or approve sewer connections. Such official shall bear the title sewer
inspector and shall be referred to in this chapter as the inspector. (Ord. 310
Regulation IV § 2, 1971)
13.08.200: BUILDING PLUMBING REQUIREMENTS:
All plumbing for sewage, within any building, shall conform to city
requirements for building plumbing and be subject to all regulations and
inspection requirements now in force or that may be imposed in the future.
(Ord. 310 Regulation IV § 3, 1971)
13.08.210: SEWER CONNECTION INTAKE DETERMINATION:
For the purpose of definition, the beginning or intake end of any sewer
connection is established at a point not more than five feet (5') from the
point where building sewer plumbing crosses the outside wall of the building in
question. (Ord. 310 Regulation IV § 4, 1971)
13.08.220: CLEANOUT REQUIRED:
At the beginning or intake end of the house service connection(s) shall be
installed a cast iron or approved cleanout wye or tee, equipped with gas proof
screw thread cap and in such positions as to allow passage of sewer pipe
cleaning equipment for cleaning the entire length of the service line from that
point to the sewer connection. Additional cleanouts shall be installed at bends
or changes in direction throughout the length of the service line or as may be
ordered by the inspector. (Ord. 310 Regulation IV § 5, 1971)
13.08.230: TERMINUS DETERMINATION:
For the purpose of definition, the terminus or outfall end of a house service
connection is at the point the service line connects to a municipal sewer main.
(Ord. 310 Regulation IV § 6, 1971)
13.08.240: MATERIAL AND SIZE APPROVAL:
None other than materials approved by the city inspector shall be used or
incorporated in the construction or installation of a house service connection.
Material rejected by the inspector shall be removed from the site of work and
replaced with approved materials. (Ord. 310 Regulation IV § 7, 1971)
13.08.250: CONNECTION; RESIDENTIAL:
Residence sewer service connections pipe and fitting shall be not less than
four inches (4") inside diameter and shall be made of one of the following
materials:
   A.   Cast iron, using leaded or hot-poured joint or approved rubber joint;
   B.   Cement-asbestos, using rubber gasket joints;
   C.   Concrete bell and spigot, using rubber gasket joints;
   D.   Approved plastic, using cemented or rubber gasket joints. (Ord. 310
Regulation IV § 7(a), 1971)
13.08.260: CONNECTION; COMMERCIAL AND BUSINESS:
Commercial and/or business sewer service connection pipes and fittings shall be
not less than four inches (4") inside diameter and shall be made of one of the
materials listed in section 13.08.250 of this chapter. The inspector shall have
the authority to require installation of six inches (6") inside diameter pipe
or such larger size pipe as may be required to carry both present and estimated
future flows in accordance with recognized sewer design standards. (Ord. 310
Regulation IV § 7(b), 1971)
13.08.270: PIPE; JOINTING REQUIREMENTS:
The pipe used for service connections shall be carefully and properly jointed
according to the accepted code for jointing the particular type and class of
pipe used. (Ord. 310 Regulation IV § 7(c), 1971)
13.08.280: PIPE; GRADE, ALIGNMENT, AND DEPTH:
   A.   The invert of the intake end at cleanout location shall be on grade
with the invert of the cleaning fitting and jointed to the fitting with a
gastight connection. The cleanout shall not be smaller than four inches (4") in
diameter. No sewer line parallel to a water line shall be laid closer than six
feet (6') thereto unless where crossing over or under sewer water line.
   B.   Four inch (4") diameter sewer pipe shall be laid on a continuous and
uniform grade of not less than one-eighth inch (1/8") per foot from cleanout to
sewer connection (10 feet per 1,000 feet).
   C.   Six inch (6") diameter sewer pipe shall be laid on a continuous and
uniform grade of not less than three thirty-seconds inch (3/32") per foot or
may be laid on a grade of not less than seven and one-half feet (71/2') per one
thousand feet (1,000') if an engineer level is used to set grade.
   D.   Eight inch (8") diameter sewer pipe shall be laid on a continuous and
uniform grade of not less than four feet (4') per one thousand feet (1,000').
An engineer level shall be used to set the grade.
   E.   Alignment from cleanout to sewer connection shall be straight, with no
bends, warps, or sags permitted, except for bends as authorized by permit.
   F.   Depth below ground shall be not less than twelve inches (12") of ground
cover above the top of the sewer service connection pipe at the point of
leaving the house or building. It is preferred that a minimum of twenty four
inches (24") of ground cover be maintained where possible. The inspector may
order a mound or terrace of earth placed over the pipe in order to provide at
least twenty four inches (24") cover above the top of the pipe at any joint
along its length. (Ord. 310 Regulation IV § 8, 1971)
13.08.290: LAYING, BACKFILLING:
Laying and backfilling of service lines shall conform to standard
specifications for laying sewers and shall be subject to inspection by and
approval of the inspector. The inspection and approval shall embrace all
details of materials and workmanship and shall properly include all factors
that affect or may affect the connection in part or as a whole, including
trench excavation, pipe jointing, pipe laying and backfilling, and testing for
leakage. (Ord. 310 Regulation IV § 9, 1971)
13.08.300: SERVICE CONNECTION; GENERALLY:
Connections from the sewer main to sewer service connection pipelines shall be
made as prescribed in sections
13.08.310 through
13.08.360 of this chapter. (Ord. 310 Regulation IV § 10, 1971)
13.08.310: SERVICE CONNECTION; MANHOLE:
When authorized by permit, a sewer service connection may connect to a city
sewer at a manhole. A hole shall be carefully cut in the manhole at the proper
elevation, one and one-half inches (11/2") larger than the outside diameter of
the service line piping. The discharge end of the service line shall discharge
inside the manhole into a tee fitting connected flush against the inside wall
of the manhole, and with one opening extending horizontally for cleaning access
to the sewer service line, and discharging through a vertical section of pipe
laid against the inside manhole wall, and thence discharging through a ninety
degree (90°) ell onto the manhole floor. All joints inside the manhole shall be
grouted with concrete mortar and otherwise anchored to provide a durable
assembly to meet approval of the inspector. (Ord. 310 Regulation IV § 10(a),
1971)
13.08.320: SERVICE CONNECTION; SADDLE TO NONREINFORCED PIPE:
A precast concrete service connection saddle with one inch (1") or wider
shoulder shall be fitted into the sewer pipeline at the appropriate point and
near the center of a length of sewer pipe to avoid breaking the bell or the
spigot end of the sewer pipe. The saddle shall be installed in the top or in
the top third of the sewer pipe just large enough to admit the saddle but small
enough to preclude passage of the shoulder of the saddle. The saddle fitting
shall be carefully jointed with concrete mortar and covered with an approved
asphaltic base jointing material. Great care shall be taken to remove all
foreign material for the sewer pipe and to make a tight and permanent
connection between the saddle and the service pipeline. Backfilling shall be
done with great care to avoid breakage of pipe or connections and to prevent
settlement that might later cause injury of any character. Strap on service
connection saddle connections may also be used subject to approval of the
inspector. (Ord. 310 Regulation IV § 10(b), 1971)
13.08.330: SERVICE CONNECTION; SADDLE TO REINFORCED PIPE:
Sewer service line connections to reinforced sewer line mains shall be made as
specified in section
13.08.320 of this chapter except that in cutting a hole in reinforced pipe for
installation of service pipe, extreme care shall be exercised to avoid damage
to the pipe. The hole for the saddle shall be carefully chipped first to
contact with the reinforcing steel and the steel cut by torch or saw. No chisel
cutting of any character will be permitted. In lieu of standard saddle a wye
branch or riser connection may be made to sewer lines that are deep below
ground surface. A riser shall be connected the same as a saddle, except that it
shall be set vertically over the sewer pipe in all cases. A branch shall be set
horizontal with flow line at same elevation as that of sewer flow line is at
the inside top of the pipe flowing full. If more than one service is to be
connected to any branch or riser, the branch or riser shall be six inches (6")
for two (2) connections and eight inches (8") for more than six (6)
connections. (Ord. 310 Regulation IV § 10(c), 1971)
13.08.340: SERVICE CONNECTION; REJECTION:
Any authorized inspector may reject any material or workmanship for cause and,
upon his order, rejected material shall be removed or replaced with approved
material. Disapproved workmanship shall cause the removal and replacement of
all materials involved, including appurtenant excavation, backfilling and other
work items. (Ord. 310 Regulation IV § 11, 1971)
13.08.350: SERVICE CONNECTION; CONSTRUCTION AUTHORITY:
   A.   Authority To Construct: Authority to construct and use a sewer service
connection shall be obtained from the city as required by this chapter.
   B.   Construction Prohibited Unless Permit Issued: No sewer service
connection shall be constructed except pursuant to permit or authorization
issued by the city clerk.
   C.   Usage Prohibited Unless Application Approved: No sewer service
connection shall be placed in service until after an application for sewer
service has been approved by competent city authority, and thereafter no sewer
service connection shall be used after competent city authority has formally
notified the user that such connection is in need of repair, replacement, or
alteration, and such prohibition shall continue until the specific requirements
have been met in full and a permit or authorization has been issued by
competent authority to resume use of the sewer service connection in question.
(Ord. 310 Regulation IV § 12, 1971)
13.08.360: INSPECTOR APPOINTMENT:
The mayor and city council are authorized and empowered to appoint and employ a
sewer inspector or inspectors for the purpose of proper enactment, enforcement,
and administration of this chapter, and compensation paid to the inspector
shall be determined by action of the city council. (Ord. 310 Regulation IV §
13, 1971)
13.08.370: SERVICE CONNECTION; VIOLATION, PENALTY:
Any person, firm, or corporation, or agents thereof, violating any of the
provisions of sections 13.08.180 through
13.08.360 of this chapter is guilty of a misdemeanor. (Ord. 310 Regulation IV §
14, 1971)
IV. RATES AND CHARGES
13.08.380: SERVICE CHARGE; REQUIRED:
It is determined and declared necessary and conducive to and for the protection
of the health, safety, and welfare of the public and inhabitants of the city,
and for the purpose of providing a more equitable distribution of the costs and
expenses of maintenance, operation, upkeep, repair, repayment of bonded and
other indebtedness, and reserves for depreciation of the sewer system to charge
and collect service charges or fees upon the premises served or benefitted by
the sewer utility facility of the city. (Ord. 310 Regulation V § 1, 1971)
13.08.390: SERVICE CHARGE; ESTABLISHED:
   A.   There is established a system of periodic service charges, rates, and
fees for the use of, or for service rendered by, the sewer system of the city,
which service charges and fees are based upon:
      1.   Liquid volume of sewage effluent discharged into the sewer system;
      2.   Variance in biochemical oxygen demand (BOD), solids content, and
other properties differing from normal domestic sewage.
   B.   Service charges are uniform as to the different classes of property
served and as to the type, amount, and degree of service provided.
   C.   Rates, charges and fees are levied and assessed against each customer
or premises having a sewer connection with the sewer system of the city or who
otherwise have available the uses of any of the sewer facilities of the city.
   D.   All service charges, rates, fees or changes or revisions thereof, upon
approval of the city council, shall become a part of this chapter. The minimum
rate of fourteen dollars ($14.00) per month will be charged for sewer service
for all establishments.
      1.   Each establishment having a meter for the measurement of water
consumption and using more than four thousand (4,000) gallons of water per
month will pay, in addition to the fourteen dollar ($14.00) minimum, a sum
equal to one-half (1/2) of that which the user pays for water, the scale for
water being as follows:
 
Amount In Gallons     Fee
Up to 4,000       $10.50
Over 4,000        1.00    per thousand
 
      2.   Special accounts, not metered:
         a.   Beauty salon combined with residence, twelve dollars ($12.00);
         b.   Churches and church properties, eight dollars ($8.00) monthly for
each connection;
         c.   Fairgrounds, eight dollars ($8.00) monthly for each connection;
         d.   Lodges, eight dollars ($8.00) monthly for each connection;
         e.   Mobile home or trailer house, not metered, eight dollars ($8.00)
each;
         f.   Mortuary, twelve dollars ($12.00);
         g.   Multiple-living units. Living quarters containing multiple-
occupancy units, such as homes with rooms or apartments for rent, apartment
buildings, motels, hotels, trailer courts, where water service is not metered,
the monthly rate for sewer services shall be eight dollars ($8.00) per each
unit;
         h.   Railroad depot, twelve dollars ($12.00);
         i.   Schools, twenty dollars ($20.00) monthly for each school.
   E.   The city may install a test meter in the water service line at any time
to determine the amount of water being used and may adjust the sewer rates to
conform to actual usage. (Ord. 421 §§ 1, 2, 1993: Ord. 414 § 1, 1991: Ord. 413
§ 1, 1991: Ord. 412 § 1, 1991: Ord. 390, 1988: Ord. 381, 1986: Ord. 374, 1985:
Ord. 370, 1984: Ord. 310 Regulation V § 2, 1971)
13.08.400: SERVICE CHARGE; REVISION:
Service charges, rates, and fees may be changed or revised from time to time as
deemed necessary by resolution of the city council. Any property owner or user
of sewer facilities feeling aggrieved at the charges or revisions fixed and
established by the city council may within ten (10) days of the date of
adoption of the resolution file a written notice of appeal with the city
council. The city council shall, within twenty (20) days of notice of appeal,
hold a hearing thereon and shall have power and authority to ratify, confirm,
modify, or amend the changes or revisions. (Ord. 460, 1999 1 : Ord. 310
Regulation V § 3, 1971)
 
Notes
1 1. This ordinance shall be effective August 15, 1999.
13.08.406: WATER AND SEWER VACATION FEE:
   A.   A reduced fee for sewer and water service to residential properties in
the city is available for residential properties, which shall be vacant for a
period of time not less than three (3) months.
   B.   An individual requesting the vacation sewer and water rate shall make
application for said rate to the city on a form to be provided by the city
clerk.
   C.   Sewer and water vacation rate shall be fifteen dollars ($15.00) per
month.
   D.   All applicants for a vacation rate shall certify that the residential
property for which the vacation rate is requested will be vacated, and not used
by any individuals, during the period requested. Any individual who violates
the provisions of this section regarding the nonuse of the property for which
the vacation rate has been granted, shall result in the full water and sewer
and monthly fee being imposed for the period in which a violation has been
discovered.
   E.   If an application is made for a water and sewer vacation rate to begin
on a date other than the beginning of the normal monthly billing cycle, the
city clerk shall prorate the vacation fee for the period of time from the date
requested by the applicant to begin the vacation fee and the date of the next
normal monthly billing cycle.
   F.   The city clerk shall have the power to approve or deny all applications
for sewer and water vacation rates.
   G.   An individual whose application for sewer and water vacation has been
denied shall have the right to appeal such denial to the city council by filing
a written notice of appeal no later than ten (10) days after the date of the
denial of the application. The city council shall hear the applicant's appeal
no later than the next regularly scheduled meeting after the date of the
applicant's appeal being filed.
   H.   The sewer and water vacation rate may be amended by the city council by
resolution. (Ord. 461, 1999)
13.08.410: SEWER FUND ESTABLISHED:
All fees, charges, and amounts of money or monetary value received and
collected by or for the sewer system shall be deposited and credited to a
special fund to be designated as the city of Shoshone sewer revenue bond fund.
The accounts of the fund shall show all receipts and expenditures of, by, or
for the sewer system and accounting procedures for small sewer utilities as
recommended by the Federation of Sewage and Industrial Wastes Association.
Accounting procedures may be obtained through the Federation of Sewage and
Industrial Wastes Association, 4435 Wisconsin Avenue N.W., Washington, D.C.
(Ord. 310 Regulation V § 4, 1971)
13.08.420: COLLECTIONS; EXPENDITURES:
The city clerk shall collect all monies due the city of Shoshone sewer revenue
bond fund and shall attest all payments made from the fund in the same manner
as is required for the handling of other city funds. (Ord. 310 Regulation V §
5, 1971)
V. CONNECTIONS
13.08.430: REQUIRED:
   A.   Connection To Sewer Service Is Mandatory: It is determined and declared
to be necessary and conducive to and for the protection of the health, safety,
and welfare of the public and inhabitants of the city that all owners of
buildings for human occupancy within the city limits which abut on streets and
alleys containing city sewer lines shall connect to the city sewer system
within thirty (30) days' time after receiving written notice to connect.
   B.   Connection To Sewer Service During Construction: Owners of newly
constructed buildings constructed for human occupancy and abutting on streets
or alleys containing city sewer lines shall connect to the city sewer system
during construction and before such newly constructed buildings are occupied.
(Ord. 310 Regulation VI § 1, 1971)
13.08.440: PRIVATE SEWER ABATEMENT:
The maintenance and/or use of privies, private sewer lines, and septic tanks
within the city limits where city sewer lines are available by adjacent street
or alley is determined and declared to be extremely detrimental to public and
private health, safety, and welfare and is declared to be a public nuisance,
and the city council shall order their abatement and may also order the
abatement of privies in other areas of the city. (Ord. 310 Regulation VI § 2,
1971)
13.08.450: APPLICATION:
   A.   All applications for sewer service connections must be made in writing
by the owner or occupant of the premises to be served on a form provided by the
city for that purpose. Where the city has in place sewer collector mains of
sufficient size adjacent to the applicant's premises to furnish the service
desired, the city shall install, at the applicant's expense, and thereafter
maintain, at city expense, a service connection of proper size to the
applicant.
   B.   The connection permit and inspection fee for connecting to the city
sewer system within thirty (30) days after receiving written notice to connect
and before the sewer lines along the alleys and/or streets abutting the
premises to be served are covered is set in the amount of five dollars ($5.00).
   C.   Any person, firm or corporation occupying or using premises abutting
any street, avenue or alley along which are laid sewer mains, but not connected
with sewer, shall make and sign a written application therefor on forms
furnished by the city clerk, and present the same to the city clerk or
appointed deputies. The charges for making the connection shall be deposited
with the city clerk at the time of making the application and the rates shall
be in the amount of two thousand five hundred dollars ($2,500.00) plus all
costs for labor, materials, and machinery incurred by the city in connecting
such property to the city sewer system. (Ord. 504 § 1, 2006: Ord. 474 § 1,
2001: Ord. 310 Regulation VII § 1, 1971)
13.08.460: DENIAL:
Except as otherwise provided by this chapter, the city will refuse to:
   A.   Install a service connection of larger size than in its opinion is
adequate to properly service the premises;
   B.   Install a service connection at city expense except where service
connections or portions thereof are included as a part of project cost for new
construction and then not where the permanency of the building or institution
proposed to be served is such that the city's investment therein may be
jeapordized;
   C.   Install a service connection which in its opinion will work an undue
hardship on the city or its existing customers;
   D.   Install one service connection to serve more than one building or
premises except where special multiple-living units rates apply;
   E.   Connect to any service, main, or other appurtenance that in its opinion
does not conform to good engineering design or meet the standard specifications
of the city;
   F.   Make service connection for a premises on which there is no permanent
building until payment of the estimated cost of the service connection has been
made to the city according to section 13.08.470 of this chapter;
   G.   Accept an application for a service connection if it requires an
extension of the city's mains unless the requirements of sections 13.08.550
through 13.08.590 of this chapter are met. (Ord. 310 Regulation VII § 2, 1971)
13.08.470: CONSTRUCTION:
   A.   All customers who wish to make application for sewer service to lots
which are vacant or unimproved prior to the time when sewer mains are installed
along such properties may in lieu of paying the regular two hundred dollar
($200.00) connection fee agree to pay a minimum service charge of three dollars
($3.00) per month from the date the sewer mains are installed along such
properties until such time as the properties are improved or for a period of
six (6) years whichever first occurs. This rate applies only for construction
projects or that portion of construction projects wherein its use is authorized
by the city council.
   B.   Application and first month's fee must be received prior to a deadline
date as set by the city council.
   C.   The rate of three dollars ($3.00) per month includes application fees
for service and turnon.
   D.   Those connecting to and using city sewerage service at the time the
system is installed will pay only the five dollar ($5.00) connection fee rather
than the two hundred dollar ($200.00) connection fee charged those who connect
after the sewer system has been installed and who have failed to pay the three
dollar ($3.00) per month charge set forth in this section. (Ord. 310 Regulation
VII § 3, 1971)
13.08.480: SERVICE OUTSIDE CITY:
   A.   No service from the municipal sewer system will be rendered to any
applicant outside of the corporate limits of the city until, in the judgment of
the city council, those requiring service within the corporate limits have been
properly serviced and there are available sewers and sewage treatment
facilities for outside users and then only under the conditions of subsection B
of this section.
   B.   The applicant must submit his application for service to the city
council of the city and secure its approval and then the applicant himself must
install or pay the cost of installing the service connection in compliance with
this chapter and under the supervision of the city engineer or supervisor, and
title to the right of way, pipeline, and other connections must be properly
conveyed to the city all under special rate for service and maintenance charge
and possible ultimate refund because of other services rendered through the
same line or for other reasons as may be mutually agreed upon between the
outside sewer user and the city council prior to the rendering of service.
(Ord. 310 Regulation VII § 4, 1971)
13.08.490: REPLACEMENT:
The city shall replace or enlarge service connections at its own expense:
   A.   Whenever it is necessary to change the location of any service
connection due to relocation or abandonment of the city's mains and the city
will also furnish all materials and perform all work inside the premises
necessary to reconnect the service;
   B.   Where the customer desires the enlargement of his service connection
and such enlargement will result in a higher monthly minimum sewer bill. (Ord.
310 Regulation VIII § 1, 1971)
13.08.500: COST ASSESSMENT:
The city shall replace or enlarge service connections at the expense of the
customer:
   A.   Whenever any service connection is relocated at the request of the
customer for his convenience.
   B.   Where the customer desires enlargement of his service connection and
such enlargement will result in no higher monthly sewer bill. (Ord. 310
Regulation VIII § 2, 1971)
13.08.510: OWNERSHIP:
The customer must install and maintain, at his own expense, all lines and other
sewer connections within the property line of his premises and after the
connection has been made by the city from the customer's premises to the city's
main sewer line adjacent to the customer's premises at the regular installation
fee, the customer must use the connection in a manner that will prevent
blockage of the line to the city main; and if blockage occurs, due to the
manner in which the customer has used or permitted the use of the line, the
customer is responsible for clearing the same to the city's main sewer. (Ord.
346, 1980: Ord. 310 Regulation IX § 1(a), 1971)
13.08.520: LEAK RESPONSIBILITY:
The city is not obligated to perform any service whatever in locating leaks or
other trouble inside the customer's premises. It shall, however, endeavor to
assist the customer in finding the cause of trouble whenever conditions permit.
(Ord. 310 Regulation IX § 2, 1971)
13.08.530: RIGHT OF ENTRY FOR INSPECTION:
All officers and employees of the city shall have free access at all reasonable
hours to any and all parts of property and buildings supplied by sewer for the
purpose of installing appliances desired by the city in rendering service
therein, or for repairing or removing any property of the city installed
thereon. The sewer supply will be shut off from all premises where inspection
is refused and not turned on again until work is allowed. (Ord. 310 Regulation
IX § 3, 1971)
13.08.540: GROUND WIRES PROHIBITED:
All unauthorized persons, firms, or corporations are strictly forbidden to
attach any ground wire or wires to any plumbing which is or may be connected to
any service connection or main belonging to the city. (Ord. 310 Regulation IX §
4, 1971)
13.08.550: EXTENSIONS; GENERALLY:
Extensions to sewer collector mains will be made by the city only along
streets, roads, highways, alleys, or satisfactory ways; provided, that in these
cases of extensions, if pressure and flow conditions permit and the city has
sufficient sewer capacity developed to supply the additional demands without
detriment to those already being served, and that the provisions of this
chapter governing service shall apply. (Ord. 310 Regulation X § 1, 1971)
13.08.560: EXTENSIONS; SPECIFICATIONS:
The city shall specify size, character, and location of pipes and appurtenances
and all construction work shall conform to recognized standards. (Ord. 310
Regulation X § 2, 1971)
13.08.570: EXTENSIONS; COST PAYMENT:
The city shall extend its sewer collector mains to serve any bona fide customer
under the following conditions:
   A.   All costs therefor shall be advanced by the applicant for such
extension of sewer main and may be reimbursed to the extent provided in section
13.08.580 of this chapter;
   B.   Provided, however, that if the debt service on bonds has been
consistently met and if the reserves in the sewer revenue fund meet the
requirements set forth in the bond ordinance adopted by the city and there are
sufficient reserves thereafter remaining in the sewer revenue fund, then the
city may, at the city's option, reimburse the customer who paid for the
extension of the sewer main. The reimbursement may be from the sewer revenue
fund up to the sum of one hundred dollars ($100.00) per outlet added to and in
use on the extended sewer collector main; such expenditure shall be known as
the city investment. The city investment shall come from the sewer revenue fund
whenever the city determines it is available and only after the city has taken
all precautions specified in this section to see that the debt service on bonds
will be consistently met and that the reserves in the sewer revenue fund meet
the requirements set forth in the bond ordinance. (Ord. 310 Regulation X § 3,
1971)
13.08.580: EXTENSIONS; REFUND:
All monies advanced by customers under subsection 13.08.570A of this chapter
for extension of sewer main may, if the sewer revenue fund meets the
requirements set out in subsection 13.08.570B of this chapter, be refunded as
follows: If at any time within five (5) years from the date of installation of
extension required by a customer additional consumers are connected to the
extension (there being no further extension thereof) and are receiving service
therefrom, the city may refund to the customer advancing the cost of the
extension of the sewer main an amount equal to the city investment for each
additional consumer joined onto the extended sewer collector main, but the
refund shall in no event exceed the amount without interest advanced to the
city. (Ord. 310 Regulation X § 4, 1971)
13.08.590: EXTENSIONS; ADMINISTRATION:
   A.   Upon completion of an extension, where an applicant makes an advance in
excess of the actual cost thereof, the advance in excess of the actual cost
will be reimbursed in addition to reimbursement provided in subsection
13.08.570B and section 13.08.580 of this chapter.
   B.   Any applicant who has made an advance toward the cost of an extension
may, by proper instrument, transfer to his assigns his interest in whatever
part of the advance may then not have been refunded; but the city is not
required to admit or accept such assignment and transfer the balance of the
advance until duly notified thereof in writing by and over the signatures of
the applicant and his assignee. Thereafter, the balance of the advance shall
continue in possession of the city and shall be refunded to the assignee as
provided by the assignment and the city rules and regulations made a part
thereof.
   C.   In administering the provisions of sections 13.08.570 through 13.08.590
of this chapter, the city shall not impair the ability of the city to repay the
city's 1971 sewer revenue bonds issued to pay for part of the cost of acquiring
and constructing the sewer system, or the interest thereon, according to their
terms and the terms of the ordinances of the city authorizing the issue of
bonds or the funds required to operate and maintain the system or the reserve
to be established under the provisions of the city ordinance authorizing the
issue of sewer revenue bonds. (Ord. 310 Regulation X § 5, 1971)
VI. SERVICE
13.08.600: TURN ON:
The city is not obligated to turn on sewer service for any person until an
application has been signed and application fee paid at the office of the city
by the responsible party or his agent and his credit established as provided in
this chapter. (Ord. 310 Regulation XI § 1, 1971)
13.08.610: APPLICATION:
   A.   For any customer making application for sewer service at the same time
application for new service connection is made, the fee is included in the
application for service connection fee as provided in section 13.08.450 of this
chapter.
   B.   For all other customers making application for service where service
connection is already installed, the fee is one dollar ($1.00), subject to the
provisions of this chapter including application for resumption of service,
deposit as guaranteed payment for service, violators to pay costs before being
reconnected. (Ord. 310 Regulation XI § 2, 1971)
13.08.620: RESUMPTION:
All customers requesting resumption of sewer service, where service connections
are already installed and have been used once or more, shall pay an application
fee of one dollar ($1.00) for resumption of service from installed services,
which fee is for the purpose of opening an account and for resuming sewer
service. For any customer making application for sewer service at the same time
application for new service is made, the fee is included in the application for
service connection fee as provided in section
13.08.450 of this chapter. (Ord. 310 Regulation XI § 3, 1971)
13.08.630: DEPOSIT; REQUIRED:
   A.   Every person desiring to apply for sewer service to the premises
occupied by the applicant or under the control of the applicant, shall deposit
with the city an amount not to exceed an estimated two (2) months' billing for
sewer service prior to the connection of any sewer service to the premises or
the resumption of any sewer service that has been disconnected for nonpayment
of a prior bill.
   B.   Said sum shall be collected as a deposit to ensure the timely payment
for sewer service and may be applied to payment of any unpaid bill rendered to
sewer or related items after the date that such bill becomes delinquent.
   C.   The sewer service may also be discontinued. Further service shall not
be rendered to the customer until all delinquent bills and other charges and
fees are paid in full and a new and further deposit is placed with the city to
guarantee prompt payment of future bills. (Ord. 388, 1987: Ord. 310 Regulation
XI § 4, 1971)
13.08.640: DEPOSIT; REFUND:
Upon application by the customer for discontinuance of service, the unused
balance of the deposit shall be returned to the user, after first deducting and
crediting to the customer's account all amounts due up to and including the
date of the request for discontinuance of service. (Ord. 310 Regulation XI § 5,
1971)
13.08.650: DELIVERY:
The city shall endeavor at all times to render adequate service to its
customers in accordance with this chapter, general rules and regulations of the
Idaho state health department, adopted August 15, 1968, at Coeur D'Alene,
Idaho, effective September 4, 1968, and in accordance with Idaho state law and
any amendments thereto. (Ord. 310 Regulation XII § 1, 1971)
13.08.660: INTERRUPTION:
The city reserves the right at any time upon verbal or written notice to shut
off the sewer lines for repairs, extensions, nonpayment of bills, and other
reasons and in emergencies may do so without notice. The city shall at all
times use reasonable diligence and care to prevent interruption of the sewer
service. (Ord. 310 Regulation XII § 2, 1971)
13.08.670: BILLING; COLLECTION:
The collection of all rates, fees, tolls or charges shall be by and through the
city clerk at such times and under such methods as are established in this
chapter by the city council. (Ord. 310 Regulation XIII § 1, 1971)
13.08.680: BILLING; DATES:
   A.   Bills shall be mailed or delivered whenever practicable on or before
the first day of the month.
   B.   Whenever bills are mailed or delivered after the first day of the month
a period of time of ten (10) days from the date of mailing or delivering the
bills shall be allowed before the bills become delinquent. (Ord. 310 Regulation
XIII § 2, 1971)
13.08.690: CHARGE; MONTHLY:
No sewer bill shall be less than the minimum charge for a full month where the
sewer is turned off for a customer vacating a premises within thirty (30) days
from the date sewer has been turned on for the customer. (Ord. 310 Regulation
XIII § 3, 1971)
13.08.700: CHARGE; RESPONSIBILITY:
Owners of the premises with one or more buildings, stores, apartments, or any
other division of like or similar character, all of which divisions are served
from one service connection, are held responsible for the entire sewer charges.
(Ord. 310 Regulation XIII § 4, 1971)
13.08.710: CHARGE; RECONNECTION:
When the user has not paid his bills, or in case of a new user occupying the
premises, being entitled to have the sewer turned on again at the premises,
there is a charge of five dollars ($5.00) levied for turning on the
disconnected service. (Ord. 310 Regulation XIII § 7, 1971)
13.08.720: DISCONTINUANCE:
   A.   Accounts will be continued and sewer bills rendered regularly until the
city has been duly notified in writing to discontinue service.
   B.   Failure of the city to close any account or discontinue service, when
such order is not in writing, shall not be grounds for any adjustment of
service charges rendered. (Ord. 310 Regulation XIII § 5, 1971)
13.08.730: DELINQUENT PAYMENT; NOTICE:
   A.   All sewer charges shall be due and payable to the city clerk between
the first and tenth day of each month, and upon failure to pay the same as
prescribed, each charge shall be considered delinquent on the evening of the
twentieth and shall be subject to a penalty charge of fifty cents ($0.50). If
such delinquent charge plus penalty is not paid in full before the tenth day of
the following month, service shall be subject to discontinuance for nonpayment
at, or any time after, the date and all city services to the premises may then
be turned off or disconnected without further notice.
   B.   Provided, however, that prior to turning off or disconnecting any or
all city services as provided in subsection A of this section, the city clerk
shall first cause notice to be served upon the customer or owner of the
premises by an officer or employee of the city. Notice may either be delivered
in person or to customer or owner of the structure to which water is delivered,
or mailed to the customer or owner of the premises by United States mail.
   C.   The notice shall specify the delinquency and give the person served no
less than ninety six (96) hours in which to pay the delinquency or have the
water service cut off. Within twenty four (24) hours of receipt of the notice,
the customer may request a hearing before the water department dispute board to
show cause, if any, why the services should not be discontinued. The right to
appeal the decision reached by the board to the court shall not be denied.
   D.   The prevailing party shall be entitled to all costs and expenses
including reasonable attorney fees. Should the city prevail, all costs, service
charges, and reasonable attorney fees shall be paid before the service is
restored. The board shall consist of the city clerk, a member of the city
council assigned to the water department, and the city overseer or his
functional successor. (Ord. 310A, 1981: Ord. 310 Regulation XIII § 6, 1971)
13.08.740: DELINQUENT PAYMENT; COLLECTION:
All billings and/or charges not paid or covered in full by deposits within
thirty (30) days following the date of delinquency shall be, and the same are
imposed as a lien against the property or premises against which the billings
and/or charges are levied and assessed, and the city shall at the time of
certifying the city taxes of the city certify such delinquencies together with
all penalties to the tax collector, county clerk, and/or board of county
commissioners and when so certified the same shall be a lien upon the property
and collectible as other special assessments. (Ord. 310 Regulation XIII § 8,
1971)
13.08.750: USE RESTRICTIONS:
No customer shall permit any person from another premises or building to
discharge sewage into his sewer service connection for more than one week
without the written permission and consent of the city. (Ord. 485, 2003: Ord.
310 Regulation XV § 1, 1971)
13.08.760: DISTURBING PROPERTY PROHIBITED:
   A.   No person, except an authorized agent of the city, shall without
permission from the city turn on or turn off sewer service, nor shall they
tamper with, interfere with, make repairs, connections, or replacements to any
of the city's property.
   B.   If a change or relocation of the city's property is desired,
application should be made as provided and in accordance with this chapter.
(Ord. 485, 2003: Ord. 310 Regulation XV § 2, 1971)
13.08.770: OBSTRUCTING PROPERTY PROHIBITED:
No person shall place upon or about any sewer manhole, lift station, or other
property of the city sewer system, any building material or other substance so
as to prevent free access at all times to the same. (Ord. 485, 2003: Ord. 310
Regulation XV § 3, 1971)
13.08.780: DISPUTE SETTLEMENT:
In the event of difference of opinion on the interpretation of this chapter,
the decision of the city council shall govern. (Ord. 485, 2003: Ord. 310
Regulation XV § 4, 1971)
13.08.790: RECONNECTION COST PAYMENT:
   A.   For any violations of this chapter, the sewer will be turned off
without notice or disconnected and not reconnected until adequate assurances
have been given the city that the violations will cease.
   B.   If the violation resulted in the user or customer securing sewer
service without paying for it as provided in this chapter, the city shall
estimate the amount of sewer so used and shall bill the customer for it.
   C.   The services will not be reconnected or continued until after the
estimated bill and cost for reconnection is paid.
   D.   The method of turning off or disconnecting the sewer may be by
discontinuing water services to the premises even though there are no
delinquent payments for water services at the time.
   E.   Provided, that the services rendered by the city shall not be
discontinued until the city has complied with the procedure for notice and
hearing as specified in this chapter. (Ord. 485, 2003: Ord. 310A, 1981: Ord.
310 Regulation XV § 5, 1971)
13.08.800: INTERFERENCE WITH PERSONNEL PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful for any person, firm, or corporation, or the employees or agent
of any person, firm, or corporation using sewer service from the city sewer
system to in any way interfere with the person or persons appointed as provided
in this chapter in the execution of and performance of duties as defined in
this chapter or anyone under orders relating thereto as authorized by action of
the city council. (Ord. 485, 2003: Ord. 310 Regulation XV § 6, 1971)
13.08.810: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person, firm, organization, copartnership, or corporation violating any
provision of this chapter is guilty of a misdemeanor. (Ord. 485, 2003: Ord. 310
Regulation XV § 7, 1971)

CHAPTER 15.04
BUILDING CODES
SECTION:
15.04.010: International Codes Adopted
15.04.020: [Reserved]
15.04.030: Conflict Of Provisions

15.04.010: INTERNATIONAL CODES ADOPTED:
The following nationally recognized codes are adopted as the official building
codes of the City of Shoshone, Idaho:
   A.   International Building Code: The International Building Code, 2018
edition, prepared by the International Code Council, Inc., as adopted by the
state of Idaho or the Idaho building code board, together with any amendments
or revisions to the International Building Code made by the Idaho Building Code
Board through the negotiated rulemaking process, is adopted.
   B.   Idaho Residential Code: The Idaho residential code, 2020 edition, as
adopted by the state of Idaho or the Idaho building code board, consisting of
the 2018 International Residential Code prepared by the International Code
Council, Inc. and amended by the Idaho building code board through the
negotiated rulemaking process, is adopted.
   C.   Idaho Energy Conservation Code: The Idaho energy conservation code,
2020 edition, as adopted by the state of Idaho Building Code Board, consisting
of the 2018 International Energy Conservation Code prepared by the
International Code Council, Inc. and amended by the Idaho Building Code Board
through the negotiated rulemaking process, is adopted.
   D.   Idaho Existing Building Code: The Idaho existing building code, 2018
edition, as adopted by the state of Idaho building code board, consisting of
the 2018 International Existing Building Code prepared by the International
Code Council, Inc. and amended by the Idaho Building Code Board through the
negotiated rulemaking process, is adopted.
Exemptions: Agricultural Buildings, as defined by the International Building
Code, are exempt from the building codes adopted herein but shall remain
subject to placement requirements and permits established by zoning
regulations. (Ord. 569, 2023: Ord. 484, 2003: Ord. 481, 2002: Ord. 335 § 1,
1977)
15.04.020: [RESERVED]:
15.04.030: CONFLICT OF PROVISIONS:
If any conflict should appear between this chapter and the provisions of
chapter 41 of title 39 of the Idaho Code or amendments thereof, the provisions
of the Idaho Code shall prevail. (Ord. 335 § 3, 1977)
15.04.040: BUILDING PERMIT; REQUIRED:
No person, firm, partnership, or corporation shall, within the city, erect or
construct, or commence the erection or construction of, or alter or commence
the alteration, which alteration will affect the dimensions of the existing
building, of any type of building without first obtaining a building permit in
accordance with the provisions and procedures set forth in this chapter. (Ord.
335 § 4, 1977)
15.04.050: BUILDING PERMIT; APPLICATION:
Application for a building permit shall be made to the city clerk, or duly
appointed deputies, on forms prescribed and furnished by the city, and shall be
accompanied by a permit fee of twenty dollars ($20.00). A short description
describing the proposed construction or alteration shall accompany the
application. In addition to the permit fee of twenty dollars ($20.00), to be
retained by the city, the applicant shall, at the time the application is made,
pay the proper building permit fees as set forth in subsection D of this
section and in section 303 of the building code, and, if required, a plan
inspection fee as set forth in section 303.
Prior to obtaining a building permit the following must be submitted to the
city clerk:
   A.   Building Plans And Specifications Required When: An architect or
licensed engineer is required to design, stamp and submit building plans and
specifications when the structure is more than two (2) stories in height.
   B.   Plans Required With Building Permit Application: Three (3) sets of the
following plans are required to be submitted with each building permit
application:
      1.   New Construction:
         a.   Complete plot plan, drawn to scale, with the following
information:
            (1)   North arrow.
            (2)   Scale of drawing of building.
            (3)   Legal description.
            (4)   Owner's name, address and telephone number.
            (5)   Property line and lot dimensions.
            (6)   Street(s) names.
            (7)   Setbacks from property lines; front, sides, rear.
            (8)   Location diagram and dimensions of all buildings on property.
            (9)   Curbs, cuts and driveway widths.
            (10)   Front entrances.
            (11)   Square footage of building.
            (12)   Proposed additions and dimensions.
         b.   A complete set of building plans, drawn to scale, including the
following:
            (1)   Floor plan.
            (2)   Foundation plan.
            (3)   Two (2) building elevations (front and side).
            (4)   Typical building section or wall section, showing
construction system.
            (5)   Multi-story houses will require floor framing plans, showing
directions of joists and major supporting members.
            (6)   Houses with trusses or rafters in more than one direction
will require a roof framing plan.
            (7)   Certifications are required for preengineered trusses.
      2.   Additions To Existing Structures:
         a.   Additions and/or remodel work will require all of the items
listed for new construction except for building elevations.
         b.   Interior remodeling will not require plot plan for residential
(but commercial construction does require floor plan if changed).
   C.   Inspections:
      1.   The building contractor or owner is responsible for notifying the
building department when inspections are required; at least four (4) hours'
notice is required prior to the inspection. Ordinance 425 codified herein
supplements and does not replace any other existing ordinance.
      2.   For building information, zoning, and setbacks, contact with the
building inspector can be made by contacting the city clerk at the Shoshone
city hall or by telephone. Ordinance 425 codified herein does not affect
existing structures or projects as of the effective date hereof.
   D.   Fee Computation: The following valuation data is adopted for fee
computation. All other fees and computations are determined by the schedules
and provisions of the uniform building code as adopted by the city and which
are to be found in the city hall.
CONSTRUCTION RATES BY SQUARE FOOT

   E.   Minimum Sizes: The minimum permissible building size, lot size, percent
of structure coverage on any lot and other dimensions are fifty foot (50')
street frontage and a minimum area of six thousand (6,000) square feet for any
lot on which a home is constructed or is moved on as in the case of mobile
homes of any size, manufactured homes and frame structures that are moved onto
the lot from any other location. There may only be a maximum of thirty percent
(30%) lot coverage for any structure or combination of structures placed on any
lot. There is a minimum dwelling or home size of nine hundred (900) square
feet. These requirements pertain to all residential zones.
   F.   Building Permit Fees:

15.04.060: BUILDING PERMIT; APPROVAL:
   A.   All applications for a building permit under this chapter shall be
examined by the mayor and/or city council who shall, during the course of the
examination, confer with other public officials that they deem may be
interested in the proposed building or building site. The mayor and/or council
shall review all building permit applications for new construction or
alterations to existing structures to determine whether proposed building sites
will be reasonably safe from flooding. If a proposed building site is in a
location that has a flood hazard, any proposed new construction or substantial
improvement must:
      1.   Be designed or modified and anchored to prevent flotation, collapse,
or lateral movement of the structure;
      2.   Use construction materials and utility equipment that are resistant
to flood damage; and
      3.   Use construction methods and practices that will minimize flood
damage.
   B.   The mayor and/or council shall review all subdivision proposals and
other proposed new developments to assure that:
      1.   All such proposals are consistent with the need to minimize flood
damage;
      2.   All public utilities and facilities are located and constructed to
minimize or eliminate flood damage; and
      3.   Adequate drainage is provided so as to reduce exposure to flood
hazards.
   C.   After examination of the application and after determining that the
requested information is contained on the application, the permit may be
granted; provided, however, if granting application will violate any city
ordinance or state law it shall be denied. (Ord. 335 § 4, 1977)
15.04.070: VESTED RIGHT PROHIBITED:
No person, firm, partnership, or corporation shall acquire any vested right to
construct, alter, or maintain any building by virtue of money spent or work
done prior to obtaining a building permit required by the terms of this
chapter. (Ord. 335 § 4, 1977)
CHAPTER 15.08
SIGNS AND AWNINGS
(Rep. by Ord. 485, 2003)
CHAPTER 15.12
FLOOD DAMAGE PREVENTION
SECTION:
15.12.010: Statutory Authorization, Findings Of Fact, Purpose, And Objectives
15.12.020: Definitions
15.12.030: General Provisions
15.12.040: Administration
15.12.050: Provisions For Flood Hazard Reduction
15.12.060: Legal Status Provisions
15.12.010: STATUTORY AUTHORIZATION, FINDINGS OF FACT, PURPOSE, AND OBJECTIVES:
   A.   Statutory Authority: The Legislature of the State of Idaho, pursuant to
Idaho Code sections 46-1020, 46-1023, and 46-1024, authorizes local governments
to adopt floodplain management ordinances that identify floodplains and minimum
floodplain development standards to minimize flood hazards and protect human
life, health, and property. Therefore, the City Council of the City of
Shoshone, Idaho does hereby ordain as follows.
   B.   Findings Of Fact:
      1.   The flood hazard areas of the City of Shoshone are subject to
periodic inundation that results in:
         a.   Loss of life and property;
         b.   Health and safety hazards;
         c.   Disruption of commerce and governmental services;
         d.   Extraordinary public expenditures for flood relief and
protection; and
         e.   Impairment of the tax base, all of which adversely affect the
public health, safety, and general welfare.
      2.   These flood losses are caused by structures in flood hazard areas,
which are inadequately elevated, flood-proofed, or otherwise unprotected from
flood damages, and by the cumulative effect of obstructions in floodplains
causing increases in flood heights and velocities.
      3.   Local government units have the primary responsibility for planning,
adopting, and enforcing land use regulations to accomplish proper floodplain
management.
   C.   Statement Of Purpose: The purpose of this chapter is to promote public
health, safety, and general welfare and to minimize public and private losses
due to flood conditions in specific areas by provisions designed to:
      1.   Protect human life, health, and property;
      2.   Minimize damage to public facilities and utilities such as water
purification and sewage treatment plants, water and gas mains, electric,
telephone and sewer lines, streets, and bridges located in floodplains;
      3.   Help maintain a stable tax base by providing for the sound use and
development of flood prone areas;
      4.   Minimize expenditure of public money for costly flood control
projects;
      5.   Minimize the need for rescue and emergency services associated with
flooding, generally undertaken at the expense of the general public;
      6.   Minimize prolonged business interruptions;
      7.   Ensure potential buyers are notified the property is in an area of
special flood hazard; and
      8.   Ensure those who occupy the areas of special flood hazard assume
responsibility for their actions.
   D.   Objectives And Methods Of Reducing Flood Losses: In order to accomplish
its purpose, this chapter includes methods and provisions to:
      1.   Require that development which is vulnerable to floods, including
structures and facilities necessary for the general health, safety, and welfare
of citizens, be protected against flood damage at the time of initial
construction;
      2.   Restrict or prohibit uses which are dangerous to health, safety, and
property due to water or erosion hazards, or which increase flood heights,
velocities, or erosion;
      3.   Control filling, grading, dredging, and other development which may
increase flood damage or erosion;
      4.   Prevent or regulate the construction of flood barriers that will
unnaturally divert flood waters or that may increase flood hazards to other
lands;
      5.   Preserve and restore natural floodplains, stream channels, and
natural protective barriers which carry and store flood waters. (Ord. 553,
2017)
15.12.020: DEFINITIONS:
Unless specifically defined below, words or phrases used in this chapter shall
be interpreted according to the meaning they have in common usage and to give
this chapter its most reasonable application.
ACCESSORY STRUCTURE (APPURTENANT STRUCTURE): A structure on the same lot or
parcel as a principal structure, the use of which is incidental and subordinate
to the principal structure.
ADDITION (TO AN EXISTING BUILDING): An extension or increase in the floor area
or height of a building or structure.
APPEAL: A request for review of the Floodplain Administrator's interpretation
of provisions of this chapter or request for a variance.
AREA OF SHALLOW FLOODING: A designated AO, AH, AR/AO, or AR/AH Zone on a
community's Flood Insurance Rate Map (FIRM) with a one percent (1%) or greater
annual chance of flooding to an average depth of one foot (1') to three feet
(3') where a clearly defined channel does not exist, where the path of flooding
is unpredictable, and where velocity flow may be evident. Such flooding is
characterized by ponding or sheet flow.
AREA OF SPECIAL FLOOD HAZARD: See definition of special flood hazard area
(SFHA).
BASE FLOOD: The flood having a one percent (1%) chance of being equaled or
exceeded in any given year.
BASE FLOOD ELEVATION (BFE): A determination by the Federal Insurance
Administrator of the water surface elevations of the base flood, that is, the
flood level that has a one percent or greater chance of occurrence in any given
year. When the BFE has not been provided in a special flood hazard area, it may
be obtained from engineering studies available from a Federal, State, or other
source using FEMA-approved engineering methodologies. This elevation, when
combined with the freeboard, establishes the flood protection elevation.
BASEMENT: Any area of the building having its floor subgrade (below ground
level) on all sides.
BUILDING: See definition of structure.
CRITICAL FACILITIES: Facilities that are vital to flood response activities or
critical to the health and safety of the public before, during, and after a
flood, such as a hospital, emergency operations center, electric substation,
police station, fire station, nursing home, school, vehicle and equipment
storage facility, or shelter; and facilities that, if flooded, would make the
flood problem and its impacts much worse, such as a hazardous materials
facility, power generation facility, water utility, or wastewater treatment
plant.
DATUM: The vertical datum is a base measurement point (or set of points) from
which all elevations are determined. Historically, that common set of points
was the National Geodetic Vertical Datum of 1929 (NGVD29). The vertical datum
currently adopted by the Federal government as a basis for measuring heights is
the North American Vertical Datum of 1988 (NAVD88).
DEVELOPMENT: Any man-made change to improved or unimproved real estate,
including but not limited to buildings or other structures, mining, dredging,
filling, grading, paving, excavation or drilling operations, or storage of
equipment or materials.
DEVELOPMENT ACTIVITY: Any activity defined as development which will
necessitate a floodplain development permit; such as: the construction of
buildings, structures, or accessory structures; additions or substantial
improvements to existing structures; bulkheads, retaining walls, piers, and
pools; the placement of mobile homes; or the deposition or extraction of
materials; the construction or elevation of dikes, berms and levees.
DIGITAL FLOOD INSURANCE RATE MAP (DFIRM): The digital official map of a
community, issued by the Federal Emergency Management Agency, on which both the
special flood hazard areas and the risk premium zones applicable to the
community are delineated.
ELEVATED BUILDING: For insurance purposes, a non-basement building which has
its lowest elevated floor raised above ground level by foundation walls, shear
walls, posts, piers, pilings, or columns.
ELEVATION CERTIFICATE: The Elevation Certificate is an important administrative
tool of the NFIP. It is used to determine the proper flood insurance premium
rate; it is used to document elevation information necessary to ensure
compliance with community floodplain management regulations; and it may be used
to support a request for a Letter of Map Amendment (LOMA) or Letter of Map
Revision Based On Fill (LOMR-F).
ENCLOSURE: An area enclosed by solid walls below the BFE/FPE or an area formed
when any space below the BFE/FPE is enclosed on all sides by walls or
partitions. Insect screening or open wood lattice used to surround space below
the BFE/RFPE is not considered an enclosure.
ENCROACHMENT: The advance or infringement of uses, fill, excavation, buildings,
structures, or development into a floodplain, which may impede or alter the
flow capacity of a floodplain.
EXISTING CONSTRUCTION: For the purposes of determining rates, structures for
which the "start of construction" commenced before the effective date of the
FIRM or before January 1, 1975, for FIRMs effective before that date. "Existing
construction" may also be referred to as "existing structures".
EXISTING MANUFACTURED HOME PARK OR MANUFACTURED HOME SUBDIVISION: A
manufactured home park or subdivision where the construction of facilities for
servicing the lots on which the manufactured homes are to be affixed
(including, at a minimum, the installation of utilities, the construction of
streets, and final site grading or the pouring of concrete pads) is completed
before the effective date of the original floodplain management regulations
adopted by the community, June 19, 1985.
EXISTING STRUCTURES: See definition of existing construction.
EXPANSION TO AN EXISTING MANUFACTURED HOME PARK OR SUBDIVISION: The preparation
of additional sites by the construction of facilities for servicing the lots on
which the manufacturing homes are to be affixed (including the installation of
utilities, the construction of streets, and either final site grading or the
pouring of concrete pads).
FLOOD ELEVATION DETERMINATION: See definition of base flood elevation (BFE).
FLOOD ELEVATION STUDY: See definition of Flood Insurance Study (FIS).
FLOOD HAZARD BOUNDARY MAP (FHBM): An official map of a community, issued by the
Federal Insurance Administrator, where the boundaries of the flood, mudslide
(i.e., mudflow) related erosion areas having special hazards have been
designated as Zones A, M, and/or E.
